31	\title{\bf Fluctuations of the type D ASEP:\\
32	decoupling in two universality classes}
33	\author{(working draft --- full version)}
34	\date{\today}
35	
36	\begin{document}
37	\maketitle
38	
39	\begin{abstract}
40	The type D ASEP is a two--species interacting particle system on $\Z$, the
41	$n\to\infty$ degeneration of the $U_q(\so_{2n+2})$ exclusion process of Kuan, Landry,
42	Lin, Park and Zhou, in which two separately conserved species hop, bind into a
43	composite ``bound pair'', and split. The binding interaction couples the two species
44	at the microscopic level as directly as a conservative dynamics can; the question we
45	ask is whether that coupling survives to the scale of the fluctuations. We analyse the
46	density and current fluctuations in two scaling regimes and prove that in both the two
47	species \emph{decouple} --- but for two different reasons.
48	
49	In the critically weak--asymmetry (Edwards--Wilkinson) regime $q=1-c/N^2$ we prove
50	that the two density fluctuation fields \emph{decouple}: each converges to a linear
51	stochastic heat equation, with no cross--coupling in either the drift or the noise,
52	the limiting noises having vanishing cross--correlation (Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain}).
53	The proof is self--contained modulo the classical single--species fluctuation result:
54	the drift reduces, via the exact current decoupling (Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}),
55	to an autonomous single--species WASEP, while the cross--noise cancellation is controlled
56	by a two--particle dual kernel bound
57	(Theorem~\ref{thm:kernel}) proved here in full, including the two underlying
58	one--dimensional local central limit theorems (\S\ref{sec:lclt}). The inter--species coupling the model nonetheless exhibits is
59	shown to be purely an initial--condition effect, computed in closed form through the
60	two--particle dual (Theorem~\ref{thm:closed}): a position correlation
61	$(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$ and a Bessel--Struve form for the $q$--Krawtchouk observable, both
62	with $1/c$ tails.
63	
64	In the fixed--$q$ (Kardar--Parisi--Zhang) regime an exact current--decoupling identity
65	(Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}) makes each species' current an autonomous
66	single--species ASEP, hence Tracy--Widom. Here too the species decouple at the level
67	of their correlation: we prove that the two currents are asymptotically uncorrelated,
68	$\Corr(N_1,N_2)\asymp s^{-1/6}\to0$, with an exact $O(\sqrt s)$ covariance, uniformly
69	in $n$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}). The common engine is the $q$--Krawtchouk orthogonal
70	self--duality, together with the fact --- which we make precise --- that the
71	inter--species coupling is invisible to every equilibrium transport coefficient, so
72	that in both regimes what remains of it is a transient, initial--condition--driven
73	correlation rather than a feature of the limiting law.
74	\end{abstract}
75	
76	{\small\tableofcontents}
77	
78	\section{Introduction}\label{sec:intro}
79	
80	When several conserved species share one exclusion dynamics, the basic question is
81	whether they interact at the scale of their fluctuations: do the density and current
82	fields couple in the scaling limit, or does each species behave as an autonomous
83	single--species process? Coupling is the generic expectation, and it is what produces
84	the rich behaviour of multi--species models --- off--diagonal transport coefficients,
85	distinct characteristic speeds, and the non--Gaussian or non--Tracy--Widom joint laws
86	that come with them. This paper studies a model in which the answer runs the other way.
87	The two species are not merely placed on a common lattice: they are dynamically
88	\emph{fused} into composite pairs and later \emph{split}, so any inter--species
89	coupling has a direct microscopic channel through which to act. Yet in two distinct
90	scaling limits the two components decouple completely, and our aim is to locate exactly
91	where the interaction goes --- and why it never reaches the limiting law.
92	
93	\subsection{The model}\label{sec:intromodel}
94	Fix $q\in(0,1)$. The \emph{type D ASEP} was introduced by Kuan, Landry, Lin, Park and
95	Zhou \cite{KLLPZ} from the quantum group $U_q(\so_{2n+2})$ ($n\in\N$), whose Lie
96	algebra is of Cartan type $D$. It is a continuous--time Markov process of two
97	conserved species on $\Z$ which, beyond hopping, may bind into a composite
98	\emph{bound pair} and later split. This binding is what makes the model a stringent
99	test of decoupling: the two species are genuinely interacting, not two independent
100	copies sharing the exclusion rule. Blyschak, Burke, Kuan, Li, Ustilovsky and Zhou
101	\cite{REU} established for it an orthogonal $q$--Krawtchouk self--duality, the analytic
102	engine of this paper: it reduces every fluctuation question to a computation with a
103	handful of dual particles.
104	
105	We work in the limit $n\to\infty$, in which (after rescaling time by $q^{2n}$) the
106	dynamics closes on the four local states $\{0,1,2,3\}$ at each site: empty, species
107	$1$, species $2$, and a bound pair carrying one particle of each species. With
108	$\eta_{i,x}\in\{0,1\}$ the occupation of species $i$ at $x$, so that
109	$\omega_x=\eta_{1,x}+2\eta_{2,x}$, and with $\eps:=1-q^2$, the nonzero
110	nearest--neighbour rates are
111	\begin{equation}\label{eq:rates}
112	\begin{aligned}
113	&(1,0)\!\to\!(0,1):1, &&(0,1)\!\to\!(1,0):q^2, &&(2,0)\!\to\!(0,2):1, &&(0,2)\!\to\!(2,0):q^2,\\
114	&(3,0)\!\to\!(0,3):1, &&(0,3)\!\to\!(3,0):q^4, &&(0,3)\!\to\!(1,2):q^2\eps, &&(0,3)\!\to\!(2,1):q^2\eps,\\
115	&(1,2)\!\to\!(0,3):\eps, &&(1,2)\!\to\!(2,1):q^2, &&(2,1)\!\to\!(0,3):\eps, &&(2,1)\!\to\!(1,2):q^2,
116	\end{aligned}
117	\end{equation}
118	together with mixed hops $(3,1)\!\leftrightarrow\!(1,3)$ and
119	$(3,2)\!\leftrightarrow\!(2,3)$ at rate $1$ right, $q^2$ left, in which a single
120	species slides past a bound pair. The two species numbers are conserved. For finite
121	$n$ a single species is a usual ASEP with rates $q^{\pm1}\beta_n$,
122	$\beta_n=q^{1-2n}+q^{2n-1}$, so $n$ enters the single--species dynamics only as a time
123	rescaling.
124	
125	\subsection{Results}\label{sec:introresults}
126	Decoupling might hold for one reason in one universality class and fail in another, so
127	we test it in the two canonical fluctuation classes of driven diffusive systems. We
128	treat two scalings. \emph{(A) The Edwards--Wilkinson regime}: asymmetry tuned to
129	the diffusive rate $q=q_N=1-c/N^2$, under diffusive space--time scaling, at any pair of
130	densities $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$. \emph{(B) The Kardar--Parisi--Zhang
131	regime}: $q\in(0,1)$ fixed, the integrated currents $N_1(s),N_2(s)$ across the origin
132	from the step initial condition, at a single time $s$. Our principal theorems are
133	Theorems~\ref{thm:ewmain}, \ref{thm:closed} (regime A) and \ref{thm:marg},
134	\ref{thm:cov} (regime B), proved in \S\S\ref{sec:ew}--\ref{sec:tw}. The logical
135	backbone common to both regimes --- the reversible measure and orthogonal duality
136	(\S\ref{sec:model}), the exact current decoupling and vanishing transport
137	coefficients (\S\ref{sec:decouple}), and a local CLT for the dual coordinates
138	(\S\ref{sec:lclt}) --- is developed first.
139	
140	\subsection{Relation to previous work}\label{sec:introlit}
141	Regime~(A) belongs to the nonlinear fluctuation theory of weakly asymmetric systems and
142	the passage to stochastic Burgers/KPZ, due to Gon\c{c}alves and Jara \cite{GJ}, with
143	uniqueness by Gubinelli and Perkowski and spectral--gap--free refinements by
144	Gon\c{c}alves, Jara and Simon \cite{GJS}. The few--body estimates we need we obtain
145	through the \emph{orthogonal polynomial duality} method of Ayala, Carinci and Redig
146	\cite{ACR,ACR2}, which reduces them to a decay bound on the few--particle dual kernel. In
147	our setting the exact current decoupling (Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}) makes the
148	drift an autonomous single--species WASEP, so the duality enters only for the
149	inter--species cross--noise, controlled by the type D two--particle kernel bound of
150	\S\ref{sec:kernel}; the would--be slow internal mode of the bound pair never couples to
151	the species current at all (Proposition~\ref{prop:sym}).
152	
153	For regime~(B), the single--species Tracy--Widom asymptotics are
154	Borodin--Corwin--Sasamoto \cite{BCS}; the asymptotic decoupling of the two species'
155	currents, and its $n$--independence, are to our knowledge new.
156	
157	The structural point is what distinguishes type D from other multi--species models. Its
158	inter--species coupling is invisible to both the static compressibility and the dynamic
159	mobility, so what remains of it is a transient, initial--condition--driven correlation
160	rather than a transport effect. This sets type D apart from the multi--species models
161	with genuine off--diagonal transport coefficients (e.g.\ multi--species stirring, with
162	multinomial mobility) and from the distinct--velocity two--species KPZ decouplings:
163	type D sits instead at the \emph{umbilic point}, where the characteristic velocities
164	coincide and both of those mechanisms are unavailable. We are not aware of another
165	model combining diffusive (EW) class, diagonal compressibility, vanishing
166	cross--mobility, and a nonzero shared--source inter--species correlation with a
167	$\rho(c)\sim1/c$ crossover.
168	
169	\subsection{Organisation}\label{sec:introorg}
170	Section~\ref{sec:model} fixes the generator, reversible measure, and orthogonal
171	self--duality. Section~\ref{sec:decouple} proves the exact current decoupling and the
172	vanishing static/dynamic cross coefficients. Section~\ref{sec:lclt} proves the
173	random--walk local CLTs used throughout. Section~\ref{sec:kernel} proves the
174	two--particle dual kernel bound. Section~\ref{sec:ew} proves the decoupled
175	Edwards--Wilkinson limit. Section~\ref{sec:cross} proves the initial--condition
176	crossover. Section~\ref{sec:tw} proves the Tracy--Widom marginals and the asymptotic
177	uncorrelatedness of the two currents. Section~\ref{sec:phase} records the
178	asymmetry--exponent phase picture and further numerical observations.
179	Section~\ref{sec:disc} discusses open problems. Physical interpretation is confined to
180	remarks.
181	
182	\section{The model, the measure, and the duality}\label{sec:model}
183	
184	We first record the three structures on which the entire analysis rests: the generator,
185	the reversible product measure, and the orthogonal $q$--Krawtchouk self--duality. The
186	duality is the decisive one --- it is what turns a question about the full interacting
187	field into a question about one or two dual particles, and both regimes are ultimately
188	solved by the same few--body computation.
189	
190	For a local function $f$ of $\eta\in\{0,1,2,3\}^\Z$ the generator is
191	\begin{equation}\label{eq:gen}
192	  \cL f(\eta)=\sum_{x\in\Z}\sum_{(a,b)\to(a',b')}
193	   r\big((a,b)\to(a',b')\big)\,\bone\{\omega_x=a,\omega_{x+1}=b\}
194	   \big[f(\eta^{x,x+1}_{a'b'})-f(\eta)\big],
195	\end{equation}
196	the inner sum over the transitions of \eqref{eq:rates}, $\eta^{x,x+1}_{a'b'}$ denoting
197	$\eta$ with $(\omega_x,\omega_{x+1})$ reset to $(a',b')$. That \eqref{eq:rates} defines
198	a Markov generator with the stated conservation laws, the $n\to\infty$ degeneration of
199	the $U_q(\so_{2n+2})$ vertex model, is \cite[Thm.~1.1]{KLLPZ}.
200	
201	\begin{proposition}[reversible measure; {\cite[Prop.~1.3]{KLLPZ}},{\cite[\S3.1]{REU}}]
202	\label{prop:measure}
203	The type D ASEP is reversible with respect to the product blocking measure
204	\begin{equation}\label{eq:nu}
205	  \nu(\eta)=\mu_{\alpha_1}(\eta_1)\,\mu_{\alpha_2}(\eta_2),\qquad
206	  \mu_\alpha(\xi)=\prod_{x\in\Z}\alpha^{\xi_x}q^{-2x\xi_x}\quad(\alpha>0),
207	\end{equation}
208	a product over both sites and species, carrying the $q^{-2x}$ density tilt, the two
209	species independent.
210	\end{proposition}
211	
212	\begin{lemma}[local detailed balance]\label{lem:db}
213	For $\nu$ and adjacent sites $(x,x+1)$, the unnormalised two--point weights satisfy
214	\begin{equation}\label{eq:dbrel}
215	  \nu(0,3)=q^{-4}\nu(3,0),\qquad \nu(1,2)=\nu(2,1)=q^{-2}\nu(3,0).
216	\end{equation}
217	\end{lemma}
218	\begin{proof}
219	By \eqref{eq:nu} the weight on $\{x,x+1\}$ factorises over the two sites and two
220	species; a species--$i$ particle at site $y$ contributes $\alpha_i q^{-2y}$. Moving the
221	bound pair from $x$ to $x+1$ multiplies the weight by $q^{-2}\cdot q^{-2}=q^{-4}$;
222	moving one species--$1$ particle from $x$ to $x+1$ and one species--$2$ particle from
223	$x+1$ to $x$ leaves a single $q^{-2}$ deficit. These are precisely the
224	detailed--balance identities of \eqref{eq:rates} for $\nu$.
225	\end{proof}
226	
227	\begin{remark}[parameter range and the locked limit]\label{rem:range}
228	Although $n$ indexes finite--dimensional representations of $\so_{2n+2}$, the rates
229	\eqref{eq:rates} extend analytically in $n$ and remain a bona fide Markov generator
230	for a range of \emph{negative} $n$: the binding rates $(1,2)\to(3,0)$, $(3,0)\to(1,2)$
231	are the constraints, both vanishing at
232	$n_{\mathrm{crit}}=\log\!\big(2q^2/(1-q^2)\big)/(2\log q)$, so the process is stochastic
233	for $n>n_{\mathrm{crit}}$, with $n_{\mathrm{crit}}<0$ exactly when $q>1/\sqrt2$. At
234	$q=1$ the split/merge rates vanish, bound pairs never break, $N_1\equiv N_2$, and the
235	species are perfectly locked.
236	\end{remark}
237	
238	\subsection{The orthogonal \texorpdfstring{$q$}{q}--Krawtchouk self--duality}
239	Each site holds at most one particle of each species, so the single--site,
240	single--species marginal is the two--point specialisation of the $q$--Krawtchouk
241	family. With local fugacity $t_x:=\alpha q^{-2x}$ and density $\rho_x=t_x/(1+t_x)$,
242	the degree--$\le1$ orthogonal polynomials of $\mu_\alpha$ are
243	\begin{equation}\label{eq:d1}
244	  \kappa_0(\eta_x)\equiv1,\qquad
245	  \kappa_1(\eta_x)=\frac{(1+t_x)\eta_x-t_x}{\sqrt{t_x}}
246	  =\frac{\eta_x-\rho_x}{\sqrt{\rho_x(1-\rho_x)}}.
247	\end{equation}
248	
249	\begin{definition}[duality function]\label{def:D}
250	For a dual configuration $\xi$ specifying which (site, species) pairs carry a dual
251	particle, set
252	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Dfac}
253	  D(\xi,\eta)=\prod_{(x,i):\,\xi_{i,x}=1}\kappa_1(\eta_{i,x}),
254	\end{equation}
255	a polynomial in $\eta$ of degree $|\xi|$ (the dual mass). Mass--one duals reproduce the
256	centred density fields; a different--species mass--two dual at one site reproduces the
257	bound--pair mode.
258	\end{definition}
259	
260	\begin{theorem}[orthogonal self--duality; {\cite[Thm.~1.1,\,\S3]{REU}}]\label{thm:dual}
261	The functions \eqref{eq:Dfac} are orthogonal in $L^2(\nu)$,
262	$\int D(\xi,\eta)D(\xi',\eta)\dd\nu=\delta_{\xi,\xi'}a(\xi)$ with
263	$a(\xi)=\int D(\xi,\eta)^2\dd\nu$, and form a self--duality between the type D ASEP and
264	its particle--number--preserving dual process: writing $p_t$ for the dual transition
265	kernel,
266	\[
267	  \E_\eta[D(\xi,\eta_t)]=\sum_{\xi'}p_t(\xi,\xi')D(\xi',\eta)\qquad(\forall\xi,\ t\ge0).
268	\]
269	In the lineage of orthogonal stochastic dualities from $U_q$--representations
270	\cite{Groenevelt,CGRS}, this is the type D instance.
271	\end{theorem}
272	
273	\begin{lemma}[duality covariance; {\cite[Lem.~2.1]{ACR}}]\label{lem:acr}
274	For all $\xi,\xi'$ and $t\ge0$,
275	\[
276	  \int \E_\eta[D(\xi,\eta_t)]\,D(\xi',\eta)\dd\nu(\eta)=p_t(\xi,\xi')\,a(\xi').
277	\]
278	\end{lemma}
279	\begin{proof}
280	Insert the identity of Theorem~\ref{thm:dual},
281	$\E_\eta[D(\xi,\eta_t)]=\sum_{\xi''}p_t(\xi,\xi'')D(\xi'',\eta)$, multiply by
282	$D(\xi',\eta)$, and integrate against $\nu$. By orthogonality
283	$\int D(\xi'',\eta)D(\xi',\eta)\dd\nu=\delta_{\xi'',\xi'}a(\xi')$, so only $\xi''=\xi'$
284	survives. The interchange of sum and integral is justified by the finite mass of
285	$\xi$ (only finitely many $\xi''$ are reachable in the particle--conserving dual).
286	\end{proof}
287	
288	\noindent Lemma~\ref{lem:acr} reduces every space--time correlation of degree--$k$
289	fields to a single $k$--particle dual kernel evaluation --- the orthogonal--duality
290	reduction of few--body correlations of \cite{ACR,ACR2}, and the mechanism that makes the
291	fluctuation theory a few--body problem. In this paper it is applied at $k=2$, to the
292	inter--species cross--noise (\S\ref{sec:ew}).
293	
294	\section{Exact current decoupling and vanishing transport coefficients}\label{sec:decouple}
295	
296	The structural fact behind every decoupling result in this paper is elementary and
297	exact, holding at the level of the microscopic rates: at $n=\infty$ each species'
298	current does not see the other. We prove this first (Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}),
299	then draw its two consequences --- that each marginal is an autonomous single--species
300	ASEP, and that the two equilibrium cross--transport coefficients vanish identically
301	(Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}). Everything afterwards is the question of what residual
302	coupling can still survive once these channels are closed.
303	
304	\begin{proposition}[exact current decoupling]\label{prop:decouple}
305	At $n=\infty$ the microscopic species--$i$ current across a bond $(x,x{+}1)$ equals the
306	single--species ASEP current in $\eta_i$ alone,
307	\begin{equation}\label{eq:jdecouple}
308	  j_i=r_R\,\eta_{i,x}(1-\eta_{i,x+1})-r_L\,(1-\eta_{i,x})\eta_{i,x+1},
309	  \qquad r_R=1,\ r_L=q^2,
310	\end{equation}
311	with no dependence on the other species. Consequently
312	\begin{enumerate}
313	\item[\textup{(a)}] each marginal density field evolves as an \emph{autonomous}
314	single--species ASEP;
315	\item[\textup{(b)}] all cross derivatives of the macroscopic flux vanish identically,
316	$\partial_{\rho_1}j_2=\partial^2_{\rho_1}j_2=\partial_{\rho_1}\partial_{\rho_2}j_2=0$,
317	so the two--species hydrodynamic flux Hessian is diagonal;
318	\item[\textup{(c)}] the inter--species coupling is carried entirely by correlated
319	jumps --- bound--pair translations, swaps, and binding/splitting.
320	\end{enumerate}
321	\end{proposition}
322	\begin{proof}
323	The species--$1$ current across $(x,x{+}1)$ is the signed rate of species--$1$
324	transfer, $j_1=\sum_{\text{transitions}}r(\cdot)\,\Delta\eta_{1}$, summed over the bond
325	transitions of \eqref{eq:rates}. We collect the rightward part (the four configurations
326	with $\eta_{1,x}=1,\ \eta_{1,x+1}=0$) and the leftward part (the four with
327	$\eta_{1,x}=0,\ \eta_{1,x+1}=1$), in each case running over every species--$2$
328	occupancy of the bond.
329	
330	\emph{Rightward.} $(1,0)\!\to\!(0,1)$ at rate $1$; $(3,0)\!\to\!(0,3)$ (pair hop) at
331	rate $1$; $(3,2)\!\to\!(2,3)$ (species $1$ sliding past the pair) at rate $1$; and from
332	$(1,2)$, species $1$ leaves both by the merge $(1,2)\!\to\!(0,3)$ at rate $\eps$ and by
333	the swap $(1,2)\!\to\!(2,1)$ at rate $q^2$, summing to $\eps+q^2=1$. All four give
334	rightward rate $1=r_R$, independently of the species--$2$ occupant.
335	
336	\emph{Leftward.} $(0,1)\!\to\!(1,0)$ at rate $q^2$; $(2,3)\!\to\!(3,2)$ at rate $q^2$;
337	the swap $(2,1)\!\to\!(1,2)$ at rate $q^2$; and from $(0,3)$, species $1$ reaches $x$
338	both by the pair hop $(0,3)\!\to\!(3,0)$ at rate $q^4$ and by the split
339	$(0,3)\!\to\!(1,2)$ at rate $q^2\eps$, summing to $q^4+q^2\eps=q^4+q^2(1-q^2)=q^2$. All
340	four give leftward rate $q^2=r_L$. (The complementary merge/split channels
341	$(2,1)\!\to\!(0,3)$, $(0,3)\!\to\!(2,1)$ and the mixed hop
342	$(3,1)\!\leftrightarrow\!(1,3)$ leave $\eta_1$ on the bond unchanged and do not
343	contribute.) Thus the species--$2$ occupant never changes the species--$1$ transfer
344	rate, giving \eqref{eq:jdecouple}; the species--$2$ current is symmetric. Claim (a) is immediate. For (b), the hydrodynamic
345	flux is $\E_{\nu_\rho}[j_i]=r_R\rho_i(1-\rho_i)-r_L(1-\rho_i)\rho_i=(1-q^2)\rho_i(1-\rho_i)$,
346	a function of $\rho_i$ alone, so every $\rho_j$--derivative with $j\ne i$ vanishes, as
347	does $\partial_{\rho_1}\partial_{\rho_2}j_i$. Claim (c) is the residual: the only
348	transitions correlating the two species are the bound--pair hops, swaps and
349	split/merge events, none of which alters \eqref{eq:jdecouple}.
350	\end{proof}
351	
352	For the transport coefficients introduce the bond function
353	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Vdef}
354	  V_x:=\big[\bone_{(3,0)}+q^4\bone_{(0,3)}-q^2\bone_{(1,2)}-q^2\bone_{(2,1)}\big]_{x,x+1},
355	  \qquad \bone_{(a,b)}=\bone\{\omega_x=a,\omega_{x+1}=b\},
356	\end{equation}
357	the carr\'e du champ of the only events moving \emph{both} species across the bond
358	(bound--pair hops, sign $+$; swaps, sign $-$).
359	
360	\begin{proposition}[vanishing cross coefficients]\label{prop:cross}
361	$\E_\nu[V_x]=0$ \textup{(}equivalently, the equilibrium cross--mobility
362	$\sigma_{12}=0$\textup{)}, and the static cross--compressibility
363	$C_{12}:=\sum_r\langle\delta\rho_1(0)\delta\rho_2(r)\rangle_\nu=\Cov(N_1,N_2)/L$
364	vanishes identically.
365	\end{proposition}
366	\begin{proof}
367	By Lemma~\ref{lem:db},
368	$\E_\nu[V_x]=\nu(3,0)+q^4\nu(0,3)-q^2\nu(1,2)-q^2\nu(2,1)=\nu(3,0)[1+1-1-1]=0$. The
369	compressibility statement is the product structure of $\nu$: the two species are
370	independent under $\nu$, so all equal--time cross--correlations vanish and $C_{12}=0$.
371	\end{proof}
372	
373	\begin{remark}[interpretation]\label{rem:transport}
374	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} the asymmetry --- and hence the KPZ nonlinearity ---
375	lives only in the marginals, which are autonomous ASEPs, while the inter--species
376	coupling is purely a noise effect; by Proposition~\ref{prop:cross} that coupling is
377	invisible to both equilibrium transport coefficients. Physically, a bound pair carries
378	one particle of each species together, but it hops with exactly the bias the two
379	single--species currents already have, so it injects correlated fluctuations without
380	shifting any mean flow: coupling in the noise, not in the drift. These two facts
381	underlie the decoupling in both regimes. The cancellation $1+1-1-1=0$ of
382	Proposition~\ref{prop:cross} recurs three times in \S\ref{sec:ew}.
383	\end{remark}
384	
385	\section{Local central limit theorems for the dual coordinates}\label{sec:lclt}
386	
387	The dual processes below reduce, after passing to a relative coordinate, to
388	one--dimensional walks. We collect the local CLTs they require. Throughout, a
389	\emph{driftless finite--range walk} on $\Z$ means a continuous--time, irreducible,
390	aperiodic, mean--zero walk with bounded jump range.
391	
392	\begin{lemma}[free and perturbed local CLT]\label{lem:free}
393	Let $R^0$ be the homogeneous symmetric nearest--neighbour walk of total rate $a>0$.
394	Then $\PP(R^0(t)=r)\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$ for all $t\ge0$, $r\in\Z$, with $C=C(a)$. The same
395	bound holds, with the same rate, for any walk $\widetilde R$ that agrees with $R^0$
396	off a finite set $F\subset\Z$ and on $F$ has jump rates bounded above and below away
397	from $0$:
398	\begin{equation}\label{eq:tildeR}
399	  \sup_{r\in\Z}\PP\big(\widetilde R(t)=r\big)\le \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t}}.
400	\end{equation}
401	\end{lemma}
402	\begin{proof}
403	For $R^0$, Fourier inversion gives
404	$\PP(R^0(t)=r)=\frac1{2\pi}\int_{-\pi}^\pi e^{-a t(1-\cos\theta)}e^{-ir\theta}\dd\theta
405	\le\frac1{2\pi}\int_{-\pi}^\pi e^{-at(1-\cos\theta)}\dd\theta$. For $t\le1$ this is
406	$\le1\le\sqrt2/\sqrt{1+t}$. For $t\ge1$, using $1-\cos\theta\ge\frac{2}{\pi^2}\theta^2$
407	on $[-\pi,\pi]$,
408	$\int_{-\pi}^\pi e^{-at(1-\cos\theta)}\dd\theta\le\int_{-\infty}^\infty
409	e^{-\frac{2a}{\pi^2}t\theta^2}\dd\theta=\pi\sqrt{\tfrac{\pi}{2at}}\le C/\sqrt t$. The
410	walk $\widetilde R$ is a uniformly elliptic, finite--range, bounded perturbation of
411	$R^0$ on the finite set $F$. The stated estimate for such perturbations is the local
412	central limit theorem in the form \cite[Thm.~2.1.1, Thm.~2.3.6 and \S2.4]{LawlerLimic}:
413	an irreducible aperiodic mean--zero finite--range walk on $\Z$ with rates bounded above
414	and below away from $0$ satisfies $\sup_r\PP(\widetilde R(t)=r)\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$, and
415	the bound is stable under perturbation of the rates on a finite set.
416	\end{proof}
417	
418	The Edwards--Wilkinson kernel requires, in addition, control of the slow sojourn at the
419	origin created by the small split rate. Recall $\eps=1-q^2$ and set
420	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}:=2q^2\eps$. The relevant relative walk (defined in
421	\S\ref{sec:kernel}) agrees with a rate--$(1+q^2)$ symmetric walk off $\{-1,0,1\}$, has a
422	sticky origin held for an $\Exp(\nu_{\mathrm{sp}})$ time, and is re--entered at the
423	origin only from $\pm1$ at rate $\eps$.
424	
425	\begin{lemma}[defected marginal local CLT]\label{lem:Rlclt}
426	Let $R$ be the walk just described, started at $R(0)=0$. For $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t\le K$,
427	\[
428	  \PP\big(R(t)=r\big)\ \le\ \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t}}\ +\ \delta_{r,0}\,e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t},
429	  \qquad C=C(K,q).
430	\]
431	\end{lemma}
432	\begin{proof}
433	Write $R(t)=\widetilde R(B(t))$, where $\widetilde R$ is the walk of
434	Lemma~\ref{lem:free} with the slow origin sojourns removed (it satisfies
435	\eqref{eq:tildeR} with $a=1+q^2$) and $B(t)=t-A(t)$, $A(t)$ the total time spent at the
436	origin; the first split time is $\tau_1\sim\Exp(\nu_{\mathrm{sp}})$. On $\{t<\tau_1\}$
437	the walk has never left $0$, so $R(t)=0$ and $\PP(t<\tau_1)=e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t}$ ---
438	the atom. Off the first sojourn, conditioning on the split time $\sigma\le t$ bounds the
439	remainder by
440	\[
441	  \int_0^t \nu_{\mathrm{sp}}e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\sigma}\,
442	  \sup_{b\le t-\sigma}\PP\big(\widetilde R(b)=r\big)\dd\sigma
443	  \ \le\ \int_0^t \nu_{\mathrm{sp}}e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\sigma}\,\frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t-\sigma}}\dd\sigma.
444	\]
445	On $\sigma\le t/2$, $(1+t-\sigma)^{-1/2}\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$ and the mass is $\le1$; on
446	$\sigma>t/2$, $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\sigma}\le\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}
447	e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t/2}$ and $\int_{t/2}^t(1+t-\sigma)^{-1/2}\dd\sigma\le2\sqrt t$, so
448	that part is $\le2\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\sqrt t\,e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t/2}\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$:
449	multiplying by $\sqrt{1+t}$ and using $\sqrt t\sqrt{1+t}\le 1+t$ and $e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t/2}\le1$,
450	$2\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\sqrt t\,\sqrt{1+t}\,e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t/2}\le 2\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}(1+t)
451	=2\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}+2\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t\le 2\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}+2K\le C$ in the window
452	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t\le K$ (recall $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\le2$). Finally returns to the origin are $O(1)$ in expectation: a
453	return requires a merge (rate $\eps$) while at $\pm1$, and
454	$\E[\#\text{returns}]\le\eps\int_0^t\PP(\widetilde R(s)\in\{\pm1\})\dd s\le\eps\cdot
455	C\sqrt t\le C\sqrt{K\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}^{-1}}\cdot\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\le C$ by
456	Lemma~\ref{lem:free}; the strong Markov property multiplies the bound by a constant.
457	\end{proof}
458	
459	The relative coordinate is now controlled. The sum coordinate is an additive functional
460	of the same path, so it needs a separate argument: once we condition on the path of $R$
461	the increments of $S$ are no longer independent, and we recover spreading from a
462	concentration inequality rather than from a Fourier estimate.
463	
464	\begin{lemma}[conditional local CLT for the sum coordinate]\label{lem:Slclt}
465	Let $S$ be the sum coordinate of \S\ref{sec:kernel}. For every realisation of the path
466	$R$ and every $s'\in\Z$,
467	\[
468	  \PP\big(S(t)=s'\mid R\big)\ \le\ \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t}}.
469	\]
470	\end{lemma}
471	\begin{proof}
472	Given the path $R$, $S(t)=m(R)+\sum_{j=1}^M\eta_j$ with $m(R)$ fixed by the path and
473	the $\eta_j$ the increments at the events for which the same $\Delta R$ admits two
474	values of $\Delta S$: on $\{|R|\ge2\}$ a step $\Delta R=+1$ is either ``species $1$
475	left'' ($\Delta S=-1$) or ``species $2$ right'' ($\Delta S=+1$); at $R=0$ a pair hop
476	has $\Delta S=\pm2$. Each $\eta_j$ is non--degenerate, with both values of probability
477	bounded away from $0$ and $1$ (the relevant ratios are $q^2/(1+q^2)$ and
478	$q^4/(1+q^4)\in(0,1)$), so $Q(\eta_j;0):=\sup_w\PP(\eta_j=w\mid R)\le1-\delta$ for a
479	fixed $\delta>0$. By the Kolmogorov--Rogozin concentration inequality
480	\cite[Ch.~III]{Petrov}, the concentration function of the conditionally--independent sum
481	satisfies $\PP(S(t)=s'\mid R)\le Q(\sum_j\eta_j;0)\le C\big(\sum_j(1-Q(\eta_j;0))\big)^{-1/2}
482	\le C/\sqrt{\delta M}$. The ambiguous events fire at rate $\ge1$ in either phase, so $M$
483	stochastically dominates a rate--$1$ Poisson process and $\PP(M\ge t/2)\ge1-e^{-ct}$; on
484	$\{M\ge t/2\}$ the bound is $\le C/\sqrt t$, and on its complement (probability
485	$\le e^{-ct}\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$) the trivial bound $1$ applies.
486	\end{proof}
487	
488	\section{The two--particle dual kernel bound}\label{sec:kernel}
489	
490	The order--two fields of the fluctuation analysis reduce, by Lemma~\ref{lem:acr}, to
491	the two--particle dual kernel. A bound pair carries one particle of \emph{each}
492	species, so two particles of the same species can never bind; the different--species
493	pair is the bind/split/merge process. We treat the two channels.
494	
495	\begin{lemma}[same--species channel]\label{lem:asep}
496	The same--species two--particle dual kernel obeys $p_t(\xi,\xi')\le C/(1+t)$.
497	\end{lemma}
498	\begin{proof}
499	With no binding move available, the two same--species dual particles perform a
500	two--particle ASEP. By the exact solution of the two--particle ASEP master equation
501	\cite{Schutz} the kernel is a determinant of single--particle kernels; each single
502	particle obeys $\PP(\cdot)\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$ by Lemma~\ref{lem:free}, so the product
503	(two particles in $d=1$) is $\le C/(1+t)$.
504	\end{proof}
505	
506	For the different--species pair with positions $X_1,X_2$ set
507	\begin{equation}\label{eq:SR}
508	  S:=X_1+X_2,\qquad R:=X_2-X_1.
509	\end{equation}
510	Off $\{-1,0,1\}$ the coordinate $R$ is a symmetric nearest--neighbour walk of rate
511	$1+q^2$; the origin $R=0$ (the bound pair) is sticky with split (escape) rate
512	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}=2q^2\eps$, entered from $\pm1$ only by a merge of rate $\eps$. The
513	coordinate $S$ is an additive functional of the $R$--path. This is exactly the process
514	of Lemmas~\ref{lem:Rlclt}--\ref{lem:Slclt}.
515	
516	\begin{theorem}[type D two--particle kernel bound]\label{thm:kernel}
517	For the different--species dual started from a bound pair, in the window
518	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t\le K$,
519	\begin{equation}\label{eq:kernel}
520	  p_t(\xi,\xi')\ \le\ \frac{C}{1+t}\ +\ e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t}\,\frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t}}.
521	\end{equation}
522	\end{theorem}
523	\begin{proof}
524	Factor $p_t(\xi,\xi')=\PP(R(t)=r')\,\PP(S(t)=s'\mid R(t)=r')$. By
525	Lemma~\ref{lem:Rlclt}, $\PP(R(t)=r')\le C/\sqrt{1+t}+\delta_{r',0}e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t}$;
526	by Lemma~\ref{lem:Slclt}, $\PP(S(t)=s'\mid R)\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$. The product of the two
527	continuum factors is $C/(1+t)$; the product of the bound atom with the $S$--factor is
528	the second term.
529	\end{proof}
530	
531	\begin{remark}\label{rem:boundstate}
532	The bound state propagates in one dimension (whence the $t^{-1/2}$) but is
533	exponentially damped at the split rate $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\sim4c/N^2$; its time integral
534	is finite, $\int_0^\infty e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t}t^{-1/2}\dd t=\sqrt{\pi/\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}}
535	\sim N/\sqrt c=o(N^2)$. By Proposition~\ref{prop:sym} below it enters the species fields
536	with zero weight, so the departure from the ASEP bound $C/(1+t)$ is invisible to the
537	limiting fields and surfaces only in the crossover of \S\ref{sec:cross}.
538	\end{remark}
539	
540	\section{The decoupled Edwards--Wilkinson limit}\label{sec:ew}
541	
542	We now prove the first decoupling theorem by the martingale--problem scheme for
543	fluctuation fields: identify the drift as a Laplacian (D), the noise as white with the
544	right variance (N), and --- the point at which the two species could have interacted ---
545	show the cross--noise between them vanishes (X). The single--species inputs are
546	classical; the work is in (X) and in the drift remainder of (D), the only places where
547	two dual particles of different species can bind.
548	
549	Fix $\rho_1,\rho_2\in(0,1)$ (equivalently $\alpha_1,\alpha_2>0$); we do \emph{not}
550	require the symmetric line. For $\varphi\in\cS(\R)$ define the fluctuation fields
551	\begin{equation}\label{eq:field}
552	  Y_i^N(\varphi,t)=\frac1{\sqrt N}\sum_{x\in\Z}\varphi\Big(\frac xN\Big)
553	   \big(\eta_{i,x}(tN^2)-\rho_i\big),\qquad i=1,2.
554	\end{equation}
555	Across the $O(N)$ field window the blocking density tilts by $O(1/N)$, so $\nu$ is
556	locally homogeneous at the densities $\rho_i$ and the limiting coefficients are constant.
557	
558	\begin{theorem}[decoupled Edwards--Wilkinson limit]\label{thm:ewmain}
559	Under $q=q_N=1-c/N^2$, the pair $(Y_1^N,Y_2^N)$ is tight in
560	$D([0,T];\cS'(\R))^2$ and every limit point $(Y_1,Y_2)$ \emph{decouples}: each $Y_i$ is
561	a stationary solution of the linear stochastic heat equation
562	\[
563	  \partial_t Y_i=D\,\partial_x^2 Y_i+\sqrt{2\chi_i D}\,\partial_x\xi_i,
564	\]
565	with $D$ the (common) species diffusivity and $\chi_i=\rho_i(1-\rho_i)$ the
566	species--$i$ compressibility,
567	and the driving space--time white noises $\xi_1,\xi_2$ have \emph{vanishing
568	cross--correlation} (the cross bracket $\langle M_1,M_2\rangle$ is zero in the limit);
569	there is no coupling between the species in either the drift or the noise. The limit
570	law is unique.
571	\end{theorem}
572	
573	By Dynkin's formula \cite[App.~1.5]{KL} each field is a semimartingale
574	\begin{equation}\label{eq:dynkin}
575	  Y_i^N(\varphi,t)=Y_i^N(\varphi,0)+\int_0^t\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,s)\dd s+M_i^N(\varphi,t),
576	\end{equation}
577	with drift $\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,t)=N^{1/2}\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)W_{i,x}(\eta(tN^2))$,
578	$W_{i,x}$ the instantaneous species--$i$ current across $(x,x{+}1)$, and $M_i^N$ a
579	martingale whose predictable brackets are the carr\'e du champ. Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain}
580	follows from the martingale--problem scheme \cite[Ch.~11]{KL} once we establish, for
581	each $\varphi,T$:
582	\begin{itemize}
583	\item[\textup{(D)}] $\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,\cdot)\to D\,Y_i(\Delta\varphi,\cdot)$ in $L^2$;
584	\item[\textup{(N)}] $\langle M_i^N\rangle(\varphi,t)\to 2\chi_i D\,t\,\|\partial_x\varphi\|_2^2$;
585	\item[\textup{(X)}] $\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)\to0$;
586	\end{itemize}
587	together with tightness (Aldous--Mitoma) and uniqueness of the linear
588	(Ornstein--Uhlenbeck) martingale problem, both classical \cite[Ch.~11]{KL}.
589	
590	\subsection{Single--species Gaussianity}
591	\begin{lemma}\label{lem:gauss}
592	For each $i$, $Y_i^N$ converges to the Gaussian Ornstein--Uhlenbeck
593	Edwards--Wilkinson field, with the diagonal bracket of \textup{(N)}.
594	\end{lemma}
595	\begin{proof}
596	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}(a) the species--$i$ marginal is an autonomous WASEP
597	of right/left rates $1,q^2$, i.e.\ asymmetry $\gamma=1-q^2=2c/N^2+O(N^{-4})$. This sits
598	below the KPZ threshold, which under diffusive scaling occurs at asymmetry $N^{-1/2}$
599	\cite{GJ}; the Euler/Burgers term is $O(\gamma)\to0$, and the process is in the
600	Edwards--Wilkinson regime. The equilibrium density fluctuations of a one--species
601	exclusion process in this regime converge to the Gaussian Ornstein--Uhlenbeck solution
602	of $\partial_tY=D\partial_x^2Y+\sqrt{2\chi_i D}\partial_x\xi$, $\chi_i=\rho_i(1-\rho_i)$
603	--- the classical one--species equilibrium fluctuation theorem \cite[Ch.~11]{KL},
604	established for orthogonal duality systems in \cite{ACR2} --- with the diagonal bracket
605	$2\chi_i D$.
606	\end{proof}
607	
608	\noindent The content is thus in (X) and (D), where two dual particles of different
609	species can bind.
610	
611	\subsection{The cross noise}
612	The predictable cross bracket is $\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)=\int_0^t\Theta^N\dd s$,
613	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Theta}
614	  \Theta^N=\frac1N\sum_x\varphi'\Big(\frac xN\Big)^2 V_x,
615	\end{equation}
616	$V_x$ as in \eqref{eq:Vdef}. By Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}, $\E_\nu[\Theta^N]=0$.
617	
618	\begin{lemma}[orthogonality to the density fields; density--free]\label{lem:orth}
619	For all $\alpha_1,\alpha_2>0$ (in particular off the symmetric line), every
620	$i\in\{1,2\}$ and every $y\in\Z$, $\ip{V_x}{\eta_{i,y}-\rho_{i,y}}=0$, where
621	$\rho_{i,y}$ is the local density of species $i$ at $y$. Hence $V_x$ has no order--one
622	component in the duality decomposition; its lowest order is two.
623	\end{lemma}
624	\begin{proof}
625	Since $\E_\nu[V_x]=0$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}, an identity in $\alpha_1,\alpha_2$),
626	\[
627	  \ip{V_x}{\eta_{i,y}-\rho_{i,y}}=\E_\nu[V_x\,\eta_{i,y}]-\rho_{i,y}\,\E_\nu[V_x]
628	  =\E_\nu[V_x\,\eta_{i,y}],
629	\]
630	so it suffices to show $\E_\nu[V_x\,\eta_{i,y}]=0$. For $y\notin\{x,x+1\}$ this is
631	immediate: $V_x$ is supported on the bond $\{x,x+1\}$ and $\nu$ is a product, so
632	$\eta_{i,y}$ is independent of $V_x$ and $\E_\nu[V_x\eta_{i,y}]=\E_\nu[V_x]\,\rho_{i,y}=0$.
633	For $y\in\{x,x+1\}$, the detailed--balance relations \eqref{eq:dbrel} ---
634	$\nu(0,3)=q^{-4}\nu(3,0)$, $\nu(1,2)=\nu(2,1)=q^{-2}\nu(3,0)$, identities in the
635	fugacities --- give the $\nu$--weighted values of $V_x$ on its four support
636	configurations as $\nu(3,0)\cdot1$, $\nu(0,3)\cdot q^4$, $\nu(1,2)\cdot(-q^2)$,
637	$\nu(2,1)\cdot(-q^2)=\nu(3,0)(+1,+1,-1,-1)$. Hence for any bond function $f$,
638	$\E_\nu[V_x f]=\nu(3,0)\big[f(3,0)+f(0,3)-f(1,2)-f(2,1)\big]$, and each single--site
639	occupation equals $1$ on exactly one ``$+$'' and one ``$-$'' configuration:
640	\[
641	  \begin{array}{c|cccc}
642	   & (3,0) & (0,3) & (1,2) & (2,1)\\\hline
643	   \eta_{1,x}   & 1 & 0 & 1 & 0\\
644	   \eta_{1,x+1} & 0 & 1 & 0 & 1\\
645	   \eta_{2,x}   & 1 & 0 & 0 & 1\\
646	   \eta_{2,x+1} & 0 & 1 & 1 & 0
647	  \end{array}
648	\]
649	so $f(3,0)+f(0,3)-f(1,2)-f(2,1)=0$ for each row, giving $\E_\nu[V_x\eta_{i,y}]=0$. The
650	mechanism is the $1+1-1-1$ cancellation of Proposition~\ref{prop:cross} one order
651	higher; it uses only detailed balance, not species exchange, and is therefore
652	density--free.
653	\end{proof}
654	
655	\begin{lemma}[equal--time variance]\label{lem:eqvar}
656	$\E_\nu[(\Theta^N)^2]\le C(\varphi)\,N^{-1}$.
657	\end{lemma}
658	\begin{proof}
659	$\E_\nu[(\Theta^N)^2]=N^{-2}\sum_{x,y}\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^2\varphi'(\tfrac yN)^2\E_\nu[V_xV_y]$.
660	Each $V_x$ has $\E_\nu[V_x]=0$ and is supported on $\{x,x+1\}$; by the product structure
661	$\E_\nu[V_xV_y]=0$ unless $|x-y|\le1$. The $O(1)$ surviving near--diagonal terms per $x$
662	are bounded, so the double sum is $\le C\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^4\le CN$ (a Riemann
663	sum). The prefactor $N^{-2}$ gives the claim.
664	\end{proof}
665	
666	\begin{proposition}[$L^2$ concentration of the cross bracket]\label{prop:conc}
667	$\E_\nu[\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)^2]\le C(\varphi)\,t^{3/2}N^{-2}\to0$;
668	hence $\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)\to0$ in $L^2$, establishing \textup{(X)}.
669	\end{proposition}
670	\begin{proof}
671	Let $C_\Theta(s)=\E_\nu[\Theta^N(\eta_0)\Theta^N(\eta_{sN^2})]$. By stationarity,
672	\begin{equation}\label{eq:concstat}
673	  \E_\nu\Big[\Big(\int_0^t\Theta^N\dd s\Big)^2\Big]=2\int_0^t(t-s)C_\Theta(s)\dd s
674	  \le 2t\int_0^t C_\Theta(s)\dd s.
675	\end{equation}
676	By Lemma~\ref{lem:orth}, $V_x$ has no order--$\le1$ component, so its space--time
677	two--point function is carried by the order--two dual; by Lemma~\ref{lem:acr} and
678	Theorem~\ref{thm:kernel},
679	\begin{equation}\label{eq:concbd}
680	  \big|\E_\nu[V_x(\eta_0)V_y(\eta_{sN^2})]\big|\le C\,p_{sN^2}(\xi_x,\xi_y),
681	\end{equation}
682	$\xi_z$ the order--two configuration at $z$. Fix $x$ and sum over $y$: at microscopic
683	time $sN^2$ the order--two kernel spreads over $\sim N\sqrt s$ sites with peak
684	$\lesssim(sN^2)^{-1}$, over which $\varphi'(\tfrac yN)^2$ is essentially constant, so for
685	$s\ge N^{-2}$,
686	\[
687	  \sum_y\varphi'\Big(\tfrac yN\Big)^2\big|\E_\nu[V_x(\eta_0)V_y(\eta_{sN^2})]\big|
688	  \le C\varphi'\Big(\tfrac xN\Big)^2(N\sqrt s)(sN^2)^{-1}=C\varphi'\Big(\tfrac xN\Big)^2 N^{-1}s^{-1/2},
689	\]
690	while for $s\le N^{-2}$ the trivial bound of Lemma~\ref{lem:eqvar} gives
691	$\le C\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^2$. Summing over $x$ with $\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^4\le CN$
692	and reinstating $N^{-2}$,
693	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Ctheta}
694	  |C_\Theta(s)|\le C\min\!\big(N^{-1},\,N^{-2}s^{-1/2}\big).
695	\end{equation}
696	The bound--state part of $p_t$ contributes at most the same order (smaller by the
697	damping $e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}sN^2}\le1$ and carried by the diagonal). Splitting
698	\eqref{eq:Ctheta} at $s=N^{-2}$, $\int_0^t C_\Theta\le C(N^{-3}+N^{-2}\int_{N^{-2}}^t
699	s^{-1/2}\dd s)\le CN^{-2}\sqrt t$; feeding this into \eqref{eq:concstat} gives the claim.
700	\end{proof}
701	
702	\begin{remark}\label{rem:noH}
703	No Kipnis--Varadhan $H_{-1}$ estimate enters: its role is played by
704	Lemma~\ref{lem:orth}, which turns the would--be marginal $s^{-1}$ decay into the
```
</details>

```
705	integrable $s^{-1/2}$ of \eqref{eq:Ctheta}. This is the recursive--martingale viewpoint
706	of \cite{ACR2}.
707	\end{remark}
708	
709	\subsection{The drift}
710	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} the species--$1$ current $W_{1,x}$ is a function of
711	$\eta_1$ alone --- the single--species ASEP current --- which expands exactly, with
712	$\gamma=1-q^2$ and $\nabla f_x=f_{x+1}-f_x$, as
713	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Wgrad}
714	  W_{1,x}=-\nabla\eta_{1,x}+\gamma\,\eta_{1,x+1}(1-\eta_{1,x}).
715	\end{equation}
716	The first term is a discrete gradient; the second carries the prefactor
717	$\gamma=O(N^{-2})$. The merge channel, in which species~$1$ binds onto a species--$2$
718	site, does \emph{not} introduce an $\eta_2$--dependence: by
719	Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} the species--$2$ occupant never alters the species--$1$
720	transfer rate (the merge rate $\eps$ and the swap rate $q^2$ combine to the same $1$ as
721	the hop onto an empty site). Thus the drift involves only the autonomous single--species
722	WASEP $\eta_1$, and no two--species (bound--pair) structure enters it; the gradient part
723	will give the Laplacian and the $O(\gamma)$ part is the switched--off KPZ nonlinearity.
724	The bound--pair mode
725	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Bdef}
726	  B_z:=(\eta_{1,z}-\rho_1)(\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2)
727	\end{equation}
728	is the one near--conserved order--two object (it relaxes only at the split rate
729	$\sim\eps$); it does \emph{not} enter the drift \eqref{eq:Wgrad}. We nonetheless record
730	the following orthogonality, which makes the absence of any slow contribution explicit.
731	
732	\begin{corollary}[current orthogonal to the bound--pair mode]\label{prop:sym}
733	For all $\rho_1,\rho_2\in(0,1)$, $\ip{W_{i,x}}{B_z}=0$ for all $z$, where
734	$B_z=(\eta_{1,z}-\rho_1)(\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2)$.
735	\end{corollary}
736	\begin{proof}
737	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} (equivalently \eqref{eq:Wgrad}), $W_{1,x}$ is a
738	function of $\eta_1$ alone. Since $\nu$ is a product measure with the two species
739	independent and $\E_\nu[\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2]=0$,
740	\[
741	  \ip{W_{1,x}}{B_z}=\E_\nu\big[W_{1,x}\,(\eta_{1,z}-\rho_1)\big]\,\E_\nu[\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2]=0,
742	\]
743	and symmetrically for $W_{2,x}$.
744	\end{proof}
745	
746	\begin{remark}[no off--symmetric--line obstruction]\label{rem:offline}
747	Because the overlap vanishes at \emph{every} $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$ (Corollary~\ref{prop:sym}),
748	the bound--pair mode never couples to the species current: there is no slow third
749	hydrodynamic field, and hence no obstruction to the decoupling, off the symmetric line
750	either. (A naive expansion of $W_{1,x}$ that misreads
751	the merge channel as an $\eta_2$--dependence produces a spurious overlap
752	$\propto(\rho_1-\rho_2)$; \eqref{eq:Wgrad} shows it vanishes identically.)
753	\end{remark}
754	
755	\begin{proposition}[drift]\label{prop:drift}
756	For each $i$ and any density $\rho_i\in(0,1)$,
757	$\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,\cdot)\to D\,Y_i(\Delta\varphi,\cdot)$ in $L^2$, with $D$ the
758	diffusivity of the symmetric part of the single--species dynamics, by an elementary
759	$L^2$ estimate. This establishes \textup{(D)}.
760	\end{proposition}
761	\begin{proof}
762	By \eqref{eq:Wgrad}, $\Gamma_1^N=\Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{grad}}+\gamma\,\Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{cor}}$
763	with
764	\[
765	  \Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{grad}}=N^{1/2}\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)(-\nabla\eta_{1,x}),\qquad
766	  \Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{cor}}=N^{1/2}\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)\,g_x,\quad g_x:=\eta_{1,x+1}(1-\eta_{1,x}).
767	\]
768	\emph{Gradient term.} A summation by parts gives
769	$\Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{grad}}=N^{1/2}\sum_x(\nabla\varphi')(\tfrac xN)\,\eta_{1,x}
770	 =N^{-1/2}\sum_x\varphi''(\tfrac xN)(\eta_{1,x}-\rho_1)+o(1)=D\,Y_1^N(\Delta\varphi)+o(1)$
771	in $L^2$, $D$ the symmetric--part diffusivity; this is the standard gradient
772	computation \cite[Ch.~11]{KL}. Since the symmetric part of each species is simple
773	symmetric exclusion --- a gradient system --- $D$ is density--independent, hence the same
774	constant for both species and at every $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$.
775	\emph{Correction term.} Write $g_x=\bar g+(g_x-\bar g)$, $\bar g=\rho_1(1-\rho_1)$. The mean
776	part $\gamma N^{1/2}\bar g\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)$ is the Euler flux
777	$\partial_x[\gamma\rho_1(1-\rho_1)]$, of order $O(\gamma)\to0$ in the EW window. For the
778	fluctuating part, by stationarity its time--integral has second moment
779	\[
780	  \E\Big[\Big(\gamma\!\int_0^t\!N^{1/2}\!\sum_x\varphi'(g_x{-}\bar g)(\eta(sN^2))\dd s\Big)^2\Big]
781	  =\gamma^2 N\!\int_0^t\!\!\int_0^t\!\sum_{x,y}\varphi'\varphi'\,
782	   \E_\nu[(g_x{-}\bar g)(\eta_0)(g_y{-}\bar g)(\eta_{|s-s'|N^2})]\dd s\dd s'.
783	\]
784	The static cross--correlation of $g$ is summable, $\sum_y|\E_\nu[(g_x-\bar g)(g_y-\bar g)(\tau)]|\le C$
785	uniformly in $\tau$ (its conserved/density component sums to the compressibility, the
786	rest decays), so the double sum is $\le C N$ for every lag, and the bound is
787	$\le\gamma^2 N\cdot CN\,t^2=Cc^2N^{-2}t^2\to0$. Hence $\Gamma_1^N\to D\,Y_1(\Delta\varphi)$
788	in $L^2$; the species--$2$ drift is identical.
789	\end{proof}
790	
791	\noindent Granting (X), (N), (D), the limiting martingales $(M_1,M_2)$ are continuous
792	(jumps $\le N^{-1/2}\|\varphi\|_\infty\to0$) and Gaussian with diagonal bracket
793	(Lemma~\ref{lem:gauss}) and vanishing cross bracket (Proposition~\ref{prop:conc}); so
794	the two driving noises are uncorrelated and the limit is the decoupled pair of EW
795	fields of Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain}, unique by \cite[Ch.~11]{KL}. \hfill$\square$
796	
797	\section{The initial--condition crossover}\label{sec:cross}
798	
799	By Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain} the two limiting fields are decoupled, so the coupling the
800	model exhibits is not in the limiting dynamics. We locate it in the initial data and
801	compute it. Run the different--species dual of \S\ref{sec:kernel} from a bound pair at
802	the origin, with $q=1-c/T$, observed at time $T$. Write $S,R$ as in \eqref{eq:SR}.
803	
804	\begin{lemma}[split time]\label{lem:split}
805	The first split time $\tau$ is $\Exp(\nu_{\mathrm{sp}})$, $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}=2q^2\eps$,
806	and $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}T\to4c$, $\tau/T\To V\sim\Exp(4c)$, $\PP(\tau>T)\to e^{-4c}$.
807	\end{lemma}
808	\begin{proof}
809	While bound the pair undergoes only the rate $1$ and $q^4$ hops (which preserve the
810	bound phase) and the two splits (each rate $q^2\eps$, leaving it); the bound phase is a
811	single state whose only phase--changing exit is the split, so its holding time is
812	$\Exp(2q^2\eps)$. The limits follow from $\eps=2c/T+O(T^{-2})$.
813	\end{proof}
814	
815	\begin{lemma}[no re--binding]\label{lem:rebind}
816	The expected number of merges in $[\tau,T]$ is $O(c/\sqrt T)\to0$.
817	\end{lemma}
818	\begin{proof}
819	After the split, $R$ is (away from a merge) a symmetric rate--$(1+q^2)$ walk; a merge
820	occurs only from $R=\pm1$, at rate $\eps$. The expected occupation of $\{\pm1\}$ up to
821	$T$ is $O(\sqrt T)$ by Lemma~\ref{lem:free}, so the expected number of merges is
822	$\le\eps\cdot O(\sqrt T)=O(c/\sqrt T)$.
823	\end{proof}
824	
825	It is convenient to pass to the sum and difference $S:=X_1+X_2$, $R:=X_2-X_1$, so that
826	$X_i=(S\mp R)/2$ and the interaction (confined to the adjacent set $\{|R|=1\}$ and the
827	origin) acts only on $R$.
828	
829	\begin{lemma}[exact symmetry identities and adjacent occupation]\label{lem:occ}
830	Species--interchange symmetry maps $R\mapsto-R$, $S\mapsto S$ and fixes the law (the
831	initial bound pair is symmetric); consequently
832	\begin{equation}\label{eq:symm}
833	  \E[R(t)]=0,\qquad \Cov\big(S(t),R(t)\big)=0\qquad(\forall t\ge0).
834	\end{equation}
835	Moreover, on the event $A_T:=\{\tau\le T,\ \text{no re--binding}\}$, the occupation
836	$\Lambda_T:=\int_\tau^T\bone\{|R(t)|=1\}\dd t$ of the adjacent set obeys
837	$\E[\Lambda_T]=O(\sqrt T)$.
838	\end{lemma}
839	\begin{proof}
840	The identities \eqref{eq:symm} follow from $X_i=(S\mp R)/2$ and the invariance of the
841	law of the process under $R\mapsto-R$. After the split and with no merge, $R$ is a
842	continuous--time walk on $\Z\setminus\{0\}$ of total rate $\le2(1+q^2)$, symmetric on
843	$\{|R|\ge2\}$; by Lemma~\ref{lem:free} its time--$t$ marginal is $\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$
844	uniformly, so the expected occupation of $\{\pm1\}$ up to $T$ is
845	$\int_0^T C/\sqrt{1+t}\dd t=O(\sqrt T)$.
846	\end{proof}
847	
848	\begin{proposition}[two--phase functional CLT]\label{prop:twophase}
849	Conditionally on $\tau/T\to u\in[0,1]$ and on $A_T$,
850	\[
851	  \frac1{\sqrt{2T}}\big(X_1(T),X_2(T)\big)\To
852	  \big(\sqrt u\,\xi_0+\sqrt{1-u}\,\xi_1,\ \sqrt u\,\xi_0+\sqrt{1-u}\,\xi_2\big),
853	\]
854	with $\xi_0,\xi_1,\xi_2$ i.i.d.\ $N(0,1)$ --- a standard bivariate normal of correlation
855	$u$. Mixing over $\tau/T\To U=\min(\Exp(4c),1)$ gives the limiting law of
856	$(X_1,X_2)/\sqrt{2T}$.
857	\end{proposition}
858	\begin{proof}
859	\emph{Pre--split.} On $[0,\tau]$ the common pair position $D$ is a walk of right rate
860	$1$ and left rate $q^4$, hence variance rate $1+q^4\to2$ and drift $1-q^4=O(c/T)$. By
861	Donsker's invariance principle with $\tau\approx uT$, $D(\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\To\sqrt u\,\xi_0$
862	(the drift contributes $(1-q^4)\tau/\sqrt{2T}=O(c\sqrt u/\sqrt T)\to0$). Since
863	$S(\tau)=2D(\tau)+O(1)$ and $R(\tau)=O(1)$, the split deposits
864	$S(\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\To2\sqrt u\,\xi_0$ and $R(\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\to0$.
865	
866	\emph{Post--split.} Write $\bar S(s)=S(\tau{+}s)-S(\tau)$, $\bar R(s)=R(\tau{+}s)-R(\tau)$;
867	each is a compensated jump process. Reading the rates of \S\ref{sec:kernel}, the
868	instantaneous drifts vanish for $R$ on $\{|R|\ge2\}$ and equal $2\eps$ for $S$, while on
869	$\{|R|=1\}$ they are $O(\eps)$ for $R$ and $\eps$ for $S$ (the deficit $2\eps\to\eps$ is
870	the excluded merge); hence $\E[\bar R(T{-}\tau)]$ is supported on $\{|R|=1\}$ with
871	magnitude $\le\eps\,\E[\Lambda_T]=O(c/\sqrt T)$, and
872	$\E[\bar S(T{-}\tau)]=2\eps(T{-}\tau)-\eps\,\E[\Lambda_T]=O(c)$, both $o(\sqrt T)$. The
873	predictable quadratic--variation rates are, on $\{|R|\ge2\}$,
874	\[
875	  a_S=a_R=2(1+q^2),\qquad a_{SR}=0,
876	\]
877	and on $\{|R|=1\}$ the bounded values $a_S=1+q^2$, $a_R=1+5q^2$, $a_{SR}=\eps$ (the swap
878	$R=\pm1\mapsto\mp1$ contributes $\Delta R=\mp2$). Therefore
879	\[
880	  \langle\bar S\rangle=2(1+q^2)(T{-}\tau)-(1+q^2)\Lambda_T,\ \
881	  \langle\bar R\rangle=2(1+q^2)(T{-}\tau)+(3q^2{-}1)\Lambda_T,\ \
882	  \langle\bar S,\bar R\rangle=\eps\,\Lambda_T,
883	\]
884	and by Lemma~\ref{lem:occ} every $\Lambda_T$--term is $O_\PP(\sqrt T)=o_\PP(T)$. With
885	$q^2\to1$ and $(T{-}\tau)/T\to1-u$,
886	\[
887	  \tfrac1{2T}\langle\bar S\rangle\to2(1-u),\quad
888	  \tfrac1{2T}\langle\bar R\rangle\to2(1-u),\quad
889	  \tfrac1{2T}\langle\bar S,\bar R\rangle\to0.
890	\]
891	The jumps are bounded by $2$, so the martingale functional CLT
892	\cite[Thm.~7.1.4]{EK} gives $(\bar S,\bar R)(T{-}\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\To
893	(\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_S,\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_R)$ with $\eta_S,\eta_R$ i.i.d.\ $N(0,1)$,
894	independent of $\cF_\tau$ (hence of $\xi_0$) by the strong Markov property at $\tau$.
895	
896	\emph{Recombination.} Adding the two phases,
897	$S(T)/\sqrt{2T}\To2\sqrt u\,\xi_0+\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_S$ and
898	$R(T)/\sqrt{2T}\To\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_R$. Setting $\xi_1=(\eta_S-\eta_R)/\sqrt2$,
899	$\xi_2=(\eta_S+\eta_R)/\sqrt2$ (an orthogonal change of variables, so $\xi_0,\xi_1,\xi_2$
900	are i.i.d.\ $N(0,1)$) and using $X_i=(S\mp R)/2$ gives the claim. Integrating against
901	$\tau/T\To U$ of Lemma~\ref{lem:split} yields the $U$--mixture.
902	\end{proof}
903	
904	\begin{theorem}[closed forms for the crossover]\label{thm:closed}
905	With $U$ as above and $g(u)=\E[Z_1^+Z_2^+]$ the positive--part covariance of a standard
906	bivariate normal of correlation $u$,
907	\[
908	  \Corr(X_1,X_2)\ \longrightarrow\ \frac{1-e^{-4c}}{4c},\qquad
909	  \Corr(X_1^+,X_2^+)\ \longrightarrow\
910	  \frac{\pi}{8(\pi-1)c}\big[1-2e^{-4c}+I_0(4c)-L_0(4c)\big],
911	\]
912	with $I_0$ the modified Bessel and $L_0$ the modified Struve function. Both tend to $1$
913	as $c\to0$ and decay as $1/c$ as $c\to\infty$.
914	\end{theorem}
915	\begin{proof}
916	\emph{Full position.} By the exact identity $\Cov(S,R)=0$,
917	$\Corr(X_1,X_2)=(\Var S-\Var R)/(\Var S+\Var R)$. The per--state increment second
918	moments of $S,R$ satisfy $a_r+c_r=4(1+q^2)$ for every internal state $r$ (a direct
919	check of the rates), so $\Var S+\Var R=4(1+q^2)\sum_r\tau_r=4(1+q^2)T$ exactly, with
920	$\tau_r$ the occupation of state $r$; and $a_r-c_r$ is supported on $\{0,\pm1\}$ with
921	$a_0-c_0=4(1+q^4)$, $a_{\pm1}-c_{\pm1}=-4q^2$, so
922	$\Var S-\Var R=4(1+q^4)\tau_0-4q^2(\tau_{+1}+\tau_{-1})$. In the scaling limit the
923	bound--state occupation $\tau_0$ is the first--split time (re--binding negligible,
924	Lemma~\ref{lem:rebind}), $\E[\tau_0]/T\to(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$, and the $\{|r|=1\}$
925	occupations are $o(T)$; hence $\Corr\to(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$.
926	
927	\emph{One--sided observable.} Each marginal $Z_i^u\sim N(0,1)$ in
928	Proposition~\ref{prop:twophase}, so $\E[Z_i^+]=1/\sqrt{2\pi}$ and
929	$\Var(Z_i^+)=\tfrac12-\tfrac1{2\pi}$ are $u$--independent, and (by uniform integrability,
930	Proposition~\ref{prop:twophase})
931	$\Corr(X_1^+,X_2^+)\to(\E[g(U)]-\tfrac1{2\pi})/(\tfrac12-\tfrac1{2\pi})$. By Price's
932	theorem \cite{Price}, $g'(u)=\partial_u\E[Z_1^+Z_2^+]=\PP(Z_1>0,Z_2>0)$, and Sheppard's
933	orthant formula \cite{Sheppard} gives $\PP(Z_1>0,Z_2>0)=\tfrac14+\tfrac{\arcsin u}{2\pi}
934	=\tfrac1{2\pi}(\tfrac\pi2+\arcsin u)$, with $g(0)=\tfrac1{2\pi}$. Writing
935	$g(U)=g(0)+\int_0^U g'$ and $\PP(U>s)=e^{-4cs}$,
936	\[
937	  \E[g(U)]-\tfrac1{2\pi}=\int_0^1 g'(s)e^{-4cs}\dd s
938	  =\frac1{2\pi}\int_0^1\Big(\frac\pi2+\arcsin s\Big)e^{-4cs}\dd s.
939	\]
940	Integrating by parts and using
941	$\int_0^1 e^{-4cs}(1-s^2)^{-1/2}\dd s=\int_0^{\pi/2}e^{-4c\sin\theta}\dd\theta
942	=\tfrac\pi2[I_0(4c)-L_0(4c)]$ (DLMF 11.5.2) yields the stated form. As $c\to\infty$,
943	$I_0(z)-L_0(z)=\tfrac2{\pi z}+O(z^{-3})$ gives the $1/c$ tail; as $c\to0$ both expressions
944	tend to $1$.
945	\end{proof}
946	
947	\begin{remark}\label{rem:icmeaning}
948	By Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain} the limiting fields are decoupled, so the crossover is an
949	initial--condition effect, not a transport coefficient: from a block of bound pairs
950	($Y_1(\cdot,0)\equiv Y_2(\cdot,0)$) the two decoupled flows decorrelate, the residual
951	correlation measured by the $O(c)$ splits the run permits. In this picture $\rho(c)$ is
952	the fading memory of a common origin --- the two species released by a single split
953	start out at the same place and are then carried apart by two independent flows, so the
954	correlation surviving at time $T$ records only how many such shared splits the run
955	allowed. This is consistent with $C_{12}\equiv0$ and $\sigma_{12}=0$
956	(Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}).
957	\end{remark}
958	
959	\section{The Tracy--Widom regime}\label{sec:tw}
960	
961	Now fix $q\in(0,1)$ and study the integrated currents $N_1(s),N_2(s)$ across the origin
962	from the step initial condition at a single time $s$, with standardised currents
963	$\cO^i=(N_i-\E N_i)/\sigma_i$, $\sigma_i\asymp s^{1/3}$. We use the time--changed
964	generator $\Lt^{(n)}=\beta_n^{-1}\cL^{(n)}$, whose rates are uniformly bounded on
965	$n\in[1,\infty]$, so the single--species marginals are an $n$--free usual ASEP.
966	
967	\subsection{Marginals}
968	\begin{theorem}[Tracy--Widom marginals]\label{thm:marg}
969	For each fixed $n\in[1,\infty]$ and each species, $\cO^i_s\To F_2$, the GUE
970	Tracy--Widom law.
971	\end{theorem}
972	\begin{proof}
973	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}(a) each species' current is an autonomous
974	single--species ASEP with rates $r_R=1,r_L=q^2$. The step block (state $3$ on
975	$\{x\le0\}$, empty on $\{x>0\}$) projects, per species, to the step initial condition,
976	and step--ASEP currents are Tracy--Widom by \cite[Thm.~1.4]{BCS}. The factor $\beta_n$
977	is a pure time change, removed by the standardisation.
978	\end{proof}
979	
980	\subsection{The exact covariance and uncorrelatedness}
981	For the cross sector the dual has one walker of each species; let $r=\xi_2-\xi_1$ be the
982	relative coordinate, which is driftless (the two species share the drift $q^{-1}-q$),
983	finite--range, with a bounded perturbation at the origin from the binding.
984	
985	\begin{theorem}[covariance and uncorrelatedness]\label{thm:cov}
986	There is $C=C(q)<\infty$ with $|\Cov(N_1,N_2)(s)|\le C\sqrt s$ for all $n\in[1,\infty]$,
987	$s\ge1$. In fact
988	\begin{equation}\label{eq:11exact}
989	  \Cov(N_1,N_2)(s)=(1+q^4)\tau_0-q^2(\tau_{+1}+\tau_{-1})\ \sim\ (1-q^2)^2\,c'\sqrt s,
990	\end{equation}
991	$\tau_r=\int_0^s\PP(r(t)=r)\dd t$ the relative--walk occupation, $c'>0$. Consequently
992	$\Corr(N_1,N_2)\le Cs^{-1/6}\to0$: the two Tracy--Widom currents are asymptotically
993	uncorrelated, uniformly in $n$.
994	\end{theorem}
995	\begin{proof}
996	\emph{Localization.} The step block is deterministic, and species--$i$ particles enter
997	$\{x>0\}$ only by crossing the bond $(0,1)$; hence $N_i(s)=N_i(0)+J_i(s)$ with $N_i(0)$
998	deterministic and $J_i$ the net species--$i$ current across $(0,1)$, so
999	$\delta N_i(s)=\delta J_i(s)$ and $\Cov(N_1,N_2)=\Cov(J_1,J_2)$ is the covariance of two
1000	single--bond integrated currents.
1001	
1002	\emph{Duality reduction.} Write $n_z=\sqrt{\rho_z(1-\rho_z)}$, so
1003	$\eta_{i,z}-\rho_z=n_z\kappa_1(\eta_{i,z})$ by \eqref{eq:d1}. Applying the self--duality
1004	(Theorem~\ref{thm:dual}) to the mass--one and (different--species) mass--two duality
1005	functions, the time--$s$ expectations from the step IC $\eta_0$ are
1006	\[
1007	  \E_{\eta_0}[\kappa_1(\eta_{i,z}(s))]=\sum_{z'}p^{(1)}_s(z,z')\,\kappa_1(\eta_{i,z'}^0),
1008	  \quad
1009	  \E_{\eta_0}[\kappa_1(\eta_{1,x}(s))\kappa_1(\eta_{2,y}(s))]
1010	   =\sum_{x',y'}p_s\big((x,y),(x',y')\big)\,\kappa_1(\eta^0_{1,x'})\kappa_1(\eta^0_{2,y'}),
1011	\]
1012	$p^{(1)}_s$ the single-- and $p_s$ the two--particle (one of each species) dual kernel.
1013	Subtracting the product of marginals,
1014	\begin{equation}\label{eq:covconn}
1015	  \Cov\big(\eta_1(x,s),\eta_2(y,s)\big)
1016	  =n_xn_y\sum_{x',y'}G_s\big((x,y),(x',y')\big)\,\kappa_1(\eta^0_{1,x'})\kappa_1(\eta^0_{2,y'}),
1017	  \quad G_s:=p_s-p^{(1)}_s\otimes p^{(1)}_s,
1018	\end{equation}
1019	the \emph{connected} two--particle kernel --- the failure of the two different--species
1020	dual walkers to evolve independently. They evolve independently except through the
1021	binding interaction, which acts only on the contact set $\{|X_1-X_2|\le1\}$; hence $G_s$
1022	is generated entirely by contact events, and the increments of $X_1,X_2$ are correlated
1023	only at contact.
1024	
1025	\emph{Bound.} The duality functions $\kappa_1(\eta^0_{\cdot})$ are uniformly bounded, and
1026	each application of the contact--supported binding to the otherwise--independent pair
1027	contributes a factor controlled by the relative--walk contact occupation
1028	$K_s(r)=\int_0^s\PP(|X_1-X_2|(u)=r)\dd u$ with $|r|\le1$. The relative coordinate
1029	$\mathfrak r=X_2-X_1$ is driftless (the species share the drift $q^{-1}-q$),
1030	finite--range, with a bounded $\Theta(1)$--split perturbation at the origin, hence
1031	null--recurrent; by Lemma~\ref{lem:free}, $\PP(\mathfrak r(u)=r)\le C'/\sqrt{1+u}$, so
1032	$K_s(r)\le 2C'\sqrt s$. Summing \eqref{eq:covconn} over $x,y>0$ and using the contact
1033	support of $G_s$ gives $|\Cov(N_1,N_2)|\le C\sqrt s$.
1034	
1035	\emph{Exact constant.} For the precise leading coefficient, the half--line--summed
1036	connected pairing equals the off--contact--cancelling combination of relative
1037	occupations: writing $\mathfrak s=X_1+X_2$, the per--state increment second moments
1038	$a_r,c_r$ of $\mathfrak s,\mathfrak r$ coincide off contact ($a_r=c_r$ for $|r|\ge2$,
1039	since there the two walkers step in independent events), while at contact
1040	$a_0-c_0=4(1+q^4)$ and $a_{\pm1}-c_{\pm1}=-4q^2$. Thus all bulk contributions cancel
1041	term by term and only the contact occupations survive, giving \eqref{eq:11exact}; the
1042	three occupations share a common leading $\sqrt s$ coefficient (they differ at $O(1)$),
1043	so the combination survives with weight $(1+q^4)-2q^2=(1-q^2)^2>0$ and $c'>0$.
1044	\end{proof}
1045	
1046	\begin{remark}[why there is no ballistic term]\label{rem:noballistic}
1047	The localization $\delta N_i=\delta J_i$ also gives the transport reading. Decomposing
1048	$J_i=M_i+A_i$ (martingale plus compensator), the martingale cross--bracket is exactly the
1049	contact carr\'e du champ $\langle M_1,M_2\rangle(s)=\int_0^s V_0(\eta_u)\dd u$ with $V_0$
1050	of \eqref{eq:Vdef} --- only bound--pair hops and swaps move both species across one bond.
1051	The drift cross--terms $\Cov(M_i,A_j),\Cov(A_1,A_2)$ have a leading part equal to the
1052	equilibrium Green--Kubo cross--mobility $\sigma_{12}\cdot s$, which vanishes by
1053	Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}. So $\Cov(N_1,N_2)$ carries no $O(s)$ ballistic part, and
1054	the surviving $\sqrt s$ is the transient contact contribution evaluated above by duality.
1055	The forward decomposition thus explains the absence of an $O(s)$ term but does not
1056	\emph{by itself} yield the constant: $M_i$ and $A_i$ each have $\Theta(s)$ variance and
1057	their cancellation to the $O(\sqrt s)$ remainder is a transport--coefficient near
1058	cancellation, in contrast to the exact, term--by--term off--contact identity
1059	$a_r=c_r$ supplied by the duality.
1060	\end{remark}
1061	
1062	\begin{remark}\label{rem:uncorr}
1063	Theorem~\ref{thm:cov} is the strongest joint statement we prove unconditionally. We note
1064	that uncorrelatedness is the one joint cumulant the noise--only coupling of
1065	Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} is structurally forced to suppress (the cross--flux
1066	derivatives vanish), so it says nothing about the higher cumulants; the bound
1067	$o(s^{2/3})$ uses only $\tau_r=O(\sqrt s)$, i.e.\ recurrence and diffusivity, while the
1068	constant $(1-q^2)^2$ uses the full local CLT.
1069	\end{remark}
1070	
1071	\section{The asymmetry--exponent phase picture}\label{sec:phase}
1072	
1073	The two regimes are endpoints of a one--parameter family of scalings, and the
1074	following observations --- established at the level of the explicit rate algebra and
1075	extensive simulation, but not with the rigour of \S\S\ref{sec:ew}--\ref{sec:tw} --- place
1076	them in a single picture. Tune
1077	\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha}
1078	  q=1-c\,T^{-\alpha},\qquad \alpha\ge0,\ c>0,
1079	\end{equation}
1080	and observe the integrated currents at time $T$; the splits per particle are
1081	$\sim T(1-q^2)\sim2cT^{1-\alpha}$, governing the limiting cross--correlation.
1082	
1083	\begin{itemize}
1084	\item $\alpha<1$: $\to\infty$ splits per particle, the species mix,
1085	$\Corr(N_1,N_2)\to0$; the marginals are Tracy--Widom (the asymmetry is still
1086	macroscopic), and $\alpha=0$ is the fixed--$q$ regime of \S\ref{sec:tw}.
1087	\item $\alpha=1$ (critical): $O(c)$ splits, $\Corr\to\rho(c)\in(0,1)$, the crossover of
1088	Theorem~\ref{thm:closed}; $\gamma\sim c/T$ vanishes, the KPZ nonlinearity switches off,
1089	and the limit is the Edwards--Wilkinson pair of \S\ref{sec:ew}.
1090	\item $\alpha>1$: $\to0$ splits, bound pairs survive, $\Corr\to1$ continuously --- the
1091	locked limit of Remark~\ref{rem:range}.
1092	\end{itemize}
1093	
1094	\noindent A single axis thus interpolates from decoupled Tracy--Widom ($\alpha=0$)
1095	through the EW crossover ($\alpha=1$) to locking ($\alpha\to\infty$); the hydrodynamics
1096	decouple for every $\alpha,n$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}), only the
1097	fluctuation--level coupling depending on the scaling. The crossover correlation
1098	$\rho(c)$ is not a transport coefficient: $C_{12}\equiv0$ and (numerically)
1099	$\sigma_{12}\approx0$ (measured $-0.024\pm0.022$ at $c=1$, against the front value
1100	$\rho(1)\approx0.27$), so what remains is a transient, shared--source correlation --- the
1101	species released by a common split carrying correlated currents, $\rho(c)$ the decaying
1102	memory of the perfectly correlated block initial condition. To our knowledge this
1103	combination (Edwards--Wilkinson class, diagonal compressibility, vanishing
1104	cross--mobility, nonzero initial--condition--driven cross--correlation with a
1105	$\rho(c)\sim1/c$ crossover) matches no model in the multi--species fluctuating
1106	hydrodynamics or macroscopic fluctuation theory literature.
1107	
1108	We record three further numerical observations, consistent across $n$ (and into the
1109	negative--$n$ window of Remark~\ref{rem:range}):
1110	\begin{itemize}
1111	\item \emph{Crossover time.} At fixed $q$ near $1$ the Tracy--Widom statistics emerge only
1112	past $t_{\mathrm{cross}}\sim(1-q)^{-3/2}$; observed earlier the marginal looks Gaussian
1113	(the $\alpha\ge1$ behaviour at finite time). At $q=\tfrac12$ the law is clean by
1114	$T\sim10^3$ (skewness $\to-0.21$, the $F_2$ value).
1115	\item \emph{Subleading variance.} $\Var(N_i)=A\,s^{2/3}+B\,s^{1/2}+\cdots$, a
1116	relative--mode (Popkov--Sch\"utz--type) correction; the standardised remainder
1117	$\sigma_{\mathrm{extra}}^2\asymp s^{-1/6}$ decays at the same rate as the cross
1118	correlation ($\sigma_{\mathrm{extra}}\approx0.39$ vs $0.36$ at $n=2$ vs $13$,
1119	$T=3.3\times10^4$).
1120	\item \emph{Multipoint uncorrelatedness.} The cross--species height functions are
1121	uncorrelated at all spatial separations ($n=2$, $q=\tfrac12$, $T=3.3\times10^4$), so
1122	the decoupling extends from the integrated current to the spatial process, and it is
1123	$n$--independent at that level.
1124	\end{itemize}
1125	
1126	\section{Numerical evidence}\label{sec:numerics}
1127	
1128	We summarise the Monte Carlo simulations that corroborate the theorems and the
1129	phase picture. Lattice simulations use the exact $n=\infty$ rate table \eqref{eq:rates}
1130	from a block initial condition of bound pairs; dual computations use the two-- and
1131	few--particle generators directly. All runs store only currents and scalars (not lattice
1132	states), with $5\times10^4$ trials unless noted.
1133	
1134	\subsection{The Edwards--Wilkinson regime}
1135	The single--species current standard deviation fits the EW law $\mathrm{std}(N_1)\sim
1136	T^{1/4}$ across $T\in[100,10^4]$ (local slopes $0.22$--$0.28$, fit exponent $0.244$),
1137	excluding the $T^{1/2}$ that a bound--pair third field would produce, consistent with
1138	the autonomous single--species drift of Proposition~\ref{prop:drift}. The initial--condition crossover matches the closed forms of
1139	Theorem~\ref{thm:closed} to sampling error, with the predicted $1/c$ tail
1140	(Figure~\ref{fig:rho}); the simpler full--position observable $(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$ matches
1141	equally well. Direct measurement gives $\Corr(J_1,J_2)=-0.02\pm0.02$ (vanishing
1142	cross--mobility) and $C_{12}=0$ within error, confirming that $\rho(c)$ is neither a
1143	static nor a dynamic transport coefficient.
1144	
1145	\begin{figure}[h]\centering
1146	\includegraphics[width=0.49\textwidth]{corr_Xplus_c.png}\hfill
1147	\includegraphics[width=0.49\textwidth]{rho_c_duality.jpg}
1148	\caption{The initial--condition crossover of Theorem~\ref{thm:closed}. Left: the
1149	one--sided observable $\Corr(X_1^+,X_2^+)$ (Bessel--Struve closed form, curve) against
1150	two--particle Monte Carlo (dots), with the $\tfrac{\pi}{8(\pi-1)}c^{-1}$ tail. Right: the
1151	full--position observable $\Corr(X_1,X_2)\to(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$ against Monte Carlo. Both
1152	run from perfectly correlated data ($\Corr\to1$ as $c\to0$) to the decoupled $1/c$ tail.}
1153	\label{fig:rho}
1154	\end{figure}
1155	
1156	\subsection{The Tracy--Widom regime}
1157	The covariance scales as $\Cov(N_1,N_2)\sim T^{1/2}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}), confirmed
1158	by exact augmented--matrix occupation--time computation ($\tau_0\sim T^{0.505}$,
1159	$\Cov\sim T^{0.504}$ at $q=\tfrac12$) and by forward simulation
1160	(Figure~\ref{fig:cov}, left). The marginals converge to $F_2$ (Figure~\ref{fig:cov},
1161	middle: CDF/histogram; skewness $\to-0.21$, excess kurtosis $\to0.09$, the GUE
1162	Tracy--Widom values), and the limit is $n$--independent (Figure~\ref{fig:cov}, right:
1163	$n=2$ and $n=13$ collapse onto $F_2$). The standardised correlation accordingly decays,
1164	$\Corr(N_1,N_2)\sim s^{-1/6}\to0$, the asymptotic decoupling of Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}.
1165	
1166	\begin{figure}[h]\centering
1167	\includegraphics[width=0.32\textwidth]{cov_scaling_typeD.png}\hfill
1168	\includegraphics[width=0.32\textwidth]{histogram_vs_tw_T33000.png}\hfill
1169	\includegraphics[width=0.32\textwidth]{n2_vs_n13_vs_tw_T20000.png}
1170	\caption{The Tracy--Widom regime. Left: $\Cov(N_1,N_2)\sim T^{1/2}$, the uncorrelatedness
1171	of Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}. Middle: the marginal current against the GUE Tracy--Widom law
1172	$F_2$ at $T=3.3\times10^4$. Right: $n$--independence --- the standardised marginals at
1173	$n=2$ and $n=13$ collapse onto $F_2$.}
1174	\label{fig:cov}
1175	\end{figure}
1176	
1177	\section{Discussion}\label{sec:disc}
1178	
1179	The type D bound pair is a slow, near--conserved internal mode, yet in both scaling
1180	regimes the species decouple in the limit, for one structural reason
1181	(Remark~\ref{rem:transport}): the asymmetry lives only in the marginals
1182	(Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}), and the coupling is invisible to both equilibrium
1183	transport coefficients (Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}). What is left of the coupling is a
1184	transient, initial--condition--driven object: in regime (A) the entire crossover
1185	$\rho(c)$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:closed}); in regime (B) the sub--leading $s^{-1/6}$
1186	correlation that decays to leave the two currents uncorrelated (Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}).
1187	The two regimes are one formula ($\Cov\propto(1+q^4)\tau_0-q^2\tau_{\pm1}$) in two
1188	windows of the relative--walk occupation: at $\alpha=1$ the split rate is
1189	$O(\eps)\to0$, $\tau_0=\Theta(T)$, the crossover $O(1)$; at $\alpha=0$ the split rate
1190	is $\Theta(1)$, $\tau_0=\Theta(\sqrt T)$, the correlation sub--leading.
1191	
1192	We emphasise the scope: both results are statements of \emph{decoupling}. In regime~(A)
1193	the Gaussian limiting fields are uncoupled in drift and noise; in regime~(B) the two
1194	Tracy--Widom currents are asymptotically uncorrelated. We do not address the finer
1195	question of whether the regime~(B) limit is a \emph{product} (joint) law --- the
1196	higher--order joint structure of the two currents is left open.
1197	
1198	The Edwards--Wilkinson decoupling holds at \emph{arbitrary} densities $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$,
1199	not only on the symmetric line (Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain}): every ingredient is
1200	density--free --- the current decoupling (Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}), the
1201	cross--noise cancellation $\E_\nu[V_x]=0$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}), the
1202	orthogonality $V_x\perp$ density (Lemma~\ref{lem:orth}), and the kernel bound
1203	(Theorem~\ref{thm:kernel}), while the diagonal noise is per species --- so the two
1204	fields decouple into linear stochastic heat equations with species--dependent noise
1205	intensities $\sqrt{2\chi_iD}$, $\chi_i=\rho_i(1-\rho_i)$, and the bound--pair mode never
1206	produces a third hydrodynamic field (Corollary~\ref{prop:sym}, Remark~\ref{rem:offline}).
1207	The one genuinely open direction is the non--stationary EW analysis from block initial
1208	data, for which $\rho(c)$ is the exact limiting cross--correlation and
1209	Proposition~\ref{prop:twophase} the natural tool.
1210	
1211	\paragraph{Status.} In regime (A): Propositions~\ref{prop:cross}, \ref{prop:conc},
1212	\ref{prop:drift}, Corollary~\ref{prop:sym}, Lemmas~\ref{lem:orth}, \ref{lem:eqvar},
1213	\ref{lem:free}--\ref{lem:Slclt}, \ref{lem:asep}, \ref{lem:split}, \ref{lem:rebind},
1214	Theorems~\ref{thm:kernel}, \ref{thm:closed} and Proposition~\ref{prop:twophase} are
1215	complete and self--contained; Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain} is complete modulo the classical
1216	single--species WASEP fluctuation result (used for the drift via
1217	Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} and the diagonal noise) and the classical
1218	tightness/uniqueness \cite{KL}; it carries no model--specific assumption. In regime (B): Theorem~\ref{thm:marg}
1219	(marginals) and Theorem~\ref{thm:cov} (uncorrelatedness, modulo Lemma~\ref{lem:free})
1220	are complete. Section~\ref{sec:phase} is numerical/exploratory and frames the rigorous
1221	results within the $(\alpha,q,n)$ picture.
1222	
1223	\begin{thebibliography}{99}
1224	\bibitem{ACR} M.~Ayala, G.~Carinci, F.~Redig, \emph{Quantitative Boltzmann--Gibbs
1225	principles via orthogonal polynomial duality}, J.~Stat.~Phys.~\textbf{171} (2018),
1226	980--999; arXiv:1712.08492.
1227	\bibitem{ACR2} M.~Ayala, G.~Carinci, F.~Redig, \emph{Higher order fluctuation fields and

I've read through it. The paper is `typeD_decoupling-draft.tex` (~1265 lines, compiles — the PDF and aux files are from a build earlier tonight), titled **"Fluctuations of the type D ASEP: decoupling in two universality classes."** Quick orientation:

- **Model**: the two-species type D ASEP (the $n\to\infty$ degeneration of the $U_q(\mathfrak{so}_{2n+2})$ process of Kuan–Landry–Lin–Park–Zhou), with binding/splitting into bound pairs, analyzed via the orthogonal $q$-Krawtchouk self-duality.
- **Main results**: decoupling of the two species in both fluctuation classes — (A) in the EW regime $q=1-c/N^2$, the two density fields converge to independent stochastic heat equations (Thm 5.1-style `thm:ewmain`), with the residual coupling identified as a pure initial-condition crossover with closed forms $(1-e^{-4c})/4c$ and a Bessel–Struve expression (`thm:closed`); (B) at fixed $q$, exact current decoupling makes each current Tracy–Widom, with $\Cov(N_1,N_2)\asymp\sqrt{s}$ exactly and $\Corr\asymp s^{-1/6}\to 0$ uniformly in $n$ (`thm:cov`).
- **Structure**: model/duality → exact current decoupling + vanishing cross-transport → local CLTs → two-particle kernel bound → EW limit → crossover → TW regime → numerical phase picture (the five figure files in this directory are its plots).
- There's also a `typeD_drift_edit.md` from June 6 and an `archive/` folder I haven't opened yet.
