```
481	
482	\begin{remark}[interpretation]\label{rem:transport}
483	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} the asymmetry --- and hence the KPZ nonlinearity ---
484	lives only in the marginals, which are autonomous ASEPs, while the inter--species
485	coupling is purely a noise effect; by Proposition~\ref{prop:cross} that coupling is
486	invisible to both equilibrium transport coefficients. Physically, a bound pair carries
487	one particle of each species together, but it hops with exactly the bias the two
488	single--species currents already have, so it injects correlated fluctuations without
489	shifting any mean flow: coupling in the noise, not in the drift. These two facts
490	underlie the decoupling in both regimes. The cancellation $1+1-1-1=0$ of
491	Proposition~\ref{prop:cross} recurs three times in \S\ref{sec:ew}.
492	\end{remark}
493	
494	\section{Local central limit theorems for the dual coordinates}\label{sec:lclt}
495	
496	The dual processes below reduce, after passing to a relative coordinate, to
497	one--dimensional walks. We collect the local CLTs they require. Throughout, a
498	\emph{driftless finite--range walk} on $\Z$ means a continuous--time, irreducible,
499	aperiodic, mean--zero walk with bounded jump range.
500	
501	\begin{lemma}[free and perturbed kernel bounds]\label{lem:free}
502	Let $R^0$ be the homogeneous symmetric nearest--neighbour walk of total rate $a>0$.
503	Then $\PP(R^0(t)=r)\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$ for all $t\ge0$, $r\in\Z$, with $C=C(a)$.
504	Moreover, let $\widetilde R$ be an irreducible walk on $\Z$ (or on a state space
505	graph--isomorphic to $\Z$, such as $\Z\setminus\{0\}$ relabelled) which is
506	\emph{reversible} with respect to a measure $m$ with $c_1\le m\le c_2$, has jump range
507	$\le\varrho$ and total exit rates $\le\Lambda$, and whose nearest--neighbour
508	conductances are bounded below, $m(x)\,r(x,x+1)\ge\delta>0$ for all $x$. Then
509	\begin{equation}\label{eq:tildeR}
510	  \sup_{r}\PP\big(\widetilde R(t)=r\big)\le \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t}},
511	  \qquad C=C(c_1,c_2,\delta,\Lambda,\varrho).
512	\end{equation}
513	Every perturbed walk in this paper satisfies the hypotheses: the no--merge relative
514	walk on $\Z\setminus\{0\}$ of Lemmas~\ref{lem:Rlclt} and \ref{lem:occ} is reversible
515	with respect to counting measure (the swap channel is symmetric), with $\delta\ge
516	q^2$, so its constants are uniform as $q=q_N\to1$; the full relative walk of
517	\S\ref{sec:tw} is reversible with respect to $m(0)=q^{-2}$, $m\equiv1$ otherwise, with
518	$\delta=\min(\eps,q^2)>0$ at fixed $q$.
519	\end{lemma}
520	\begin{proof}
521	For $R^0$, Fourier inversion gives
522	$\PP(R^0(t)=r)=\frac1{2\pi}\int_{-\pi}^\pi e^{-a t(1-\cos\theta)}e^{-ir\theta}\dd\theta
523	\le\frac1{2\pi}\int_{-\pi}^\pi e^{-at(1-\cos\theta)}\dd\theta$. For $t\le1$ this is
524	$\le1\le\sqrt2/\sqrt{1+t}$. For $t\ge1$, using $1-\cos\theta\ge\frac{2}{\pi^2}\theta^2$
525	on $[-\pi,\pi]$,
526	$\int_{-\pi}^\pi e^{-at(1-\cos\theta)}\dd\theta\le\int_{-\infty}^\infty
527	e^{-\frac{2a}{\pi^2}t\theta^2}\dd\theta=\pi\sqrt{\tfrac{\pi}{2at}}\le C/\sqrt t$.
528	
529	For $\widetilde R$, the bound is trivial for $t\le1$, so let $t\ge1$. On $\ell^2(m)$
530	the generator is self--adjoint with Dirichlet form
531	$\cE(f)=\tfrac12\sum_{x,y}m(x)r(x,y)\big(f(y)-f(x)\big)^2
532	\ \ge\ \delta\sum_x\big(f(x+1)-f(x)\big)^2$. On $\Z$ the discrete Nash inequality
533	$\|f\|_2^6\le4\,\|\nabla f\|_2^2\,\|f\|_1^4$ holds: from
534	$f(x)^2=\sum_{y<x}\nabla(f^2)(y)$ and Cauchy--Schwarz,
535	$\|f\|_\infty^2\le2\|\nabla f\|_2\|f\|_2$, so
536	$\|f\|_2^2\le\|f\|_1\|f\|_\infty\le\|f\|_1\big(2\|\nabla f\|_2\|f\|_2\big)^{1/2}$,
537	and rearranging gives the claim. With the measure bounds $c_1\le m\le c_2$ this
538	transfers to $\|f\|_{2,m}^6\le C\,\cE(f)\,\|f\|_{1,m}^4$, a Nash inequality with
539	dimension parameter $d=1$ for the Dirichlet form of $\widetilde R$. By the
540	equivalence of Nash inequalities and on--diagonal kernel bounds for symmetric Markov
541	semigroups \cite{CKS}, $\sup_{x,y}p_t(x,y)/m(y)\le Ct^{-1/2}$, and $m\le c_2$ gives
542	\eqref{eq:tildeR}; all constants depend only on $(c_1,c_2,\delta,\Lambda,\varrho)$.
543	\end{proof}
544	
545	The Edwards--Wilkinson kernel requires, in addition, control of the slow sojourn at the
546	origin created by the small split rate. Recall $\eps=1-q^2$ and set
547	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}:=2q^2\eps$. The relevant relative walk (defined in
548	\S\ref{sec:kernel}) agrees with a rate--$(1+q^2)$ symmetric walk off $\{-1,0,1\}$, has a
549	sticky origin held for an $\Exp(\nu_{\mathrm{sp}})$ time, and is re--entered at the
550	origin only from $\pm1$ at rate $\eps$.
551	
552	\begin{lemma}[defected marginal local CLT]\label{lem:Rlclt}
553	Let $R$ be the walk just described, started at $R(0)=0$. For $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t\le K$,
554	\[
555	  \PP\big(R(t)=r\big)\ \le\ \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t}}\ +\ \delta_{r,0}\,e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t},
556	  \qquad C=C(K,q).
557	\]
558	\end{lemma}
559	\begin{proof}
560	Write $\nu=\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}$, so $\eps=\nu/(2q^2)$, and recall $\nu t\le K$,
561	$\nu\le2$; all constants are $C=C(K,q)$. For $t\le1$ the bound is trivial, so let
562	$t\ge1$. Three walks appear: $R$ itself; the \emph{no--merge} walk $\widehat R$ on
563	$\Z\setminus\{0\}$ (the rates of $R$ with the merge channel removed), which satisfies
564	\eqref{eq:tildeR} with constants uniform in $q\to1$; and the walk killed at the
565	merges, whose kernel is dominated by that of $\widehat R$, since killing only removes
566	mass: for $r\ne0$ and any starting point in $\{\pm1\}$,
567	\begin{equation}\label{eq:killdom}
568	  \PP_{\pm1}\big(R(u)=r,\ \text{no merge in }[0,u]\big)
569	  =\E_{\pm1}\Big[\bone\{\widehat R(u)=r\}\,e^{-\eps\Lambda_u}\Big]
570	  \ \le\ \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+u}},
571	\end{equation}
572	$\Lambda_u$ the occupation of $\{\pm1\}$ by $\widehat R$.
573	
574	\emph{Atom.} On $\{t<\tau_1\}$, $\tau_1\sim\Exp(\nu)$ the first split, the walk has
575	never left $0$: this is the term $\delta_{r,0}e^{-\nu t}$.
576	
577	\emph{Occupation of the adjacent set.} Let
578	$g(t):=\int_0^t\PP(R(u)\in\{\pm1\})\dd u$. Exits from $0$ occur at rate $\nu$ while at
579	$0$ (the two splits; pair hops do not change $R$), so the expected number of exits by
580	time $t$ is $\nu\int_0^t\PP(R(u)=0)\dd u\le\nu t\le K$. By the strong Markov property
581	at each exit and \eqref{eq:killdom}, each excursion contributes to $g$ at most
582	$\int_0^tC(1+v)^{-1/2}\dd v\le C\sqrt t$ in expectation, whence
583	$g(t)\le(1+K)\,C\sqrt t$.
584	
585	\emph{Off the origin.} Fix $r\ne0$. On $\{R(t)=r\}$ the time $t$ lies in an excursion,
586	begun at an exit from $0$; the exit times form a point process of intensity
587	$\nu\,\bone\{R(u)=0\}\dd u$, and given an exit at $u$ the probability that its
588	excursion still runs at time $t$ with $R(t)=r$ is bounded by \eqref{eq:killdom}.
589	Hence
590	\[
591	  \PP\big(R(t)=r\big)\ \le\ \nu\int_0^t\PP\big(R(u)=0\big)\,
592	  \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t-u}}\,\dd u,
593	\]
594	and we insert $\PP(R(u)=0)\le e^{-\nu u}+\eps\,g(u)\le e^{-\nu u}+C\eps\sqrt u$ (the
595	two events being ``never left'' and ``last merge before $u$'', the latter of
596	intensity $\eps\bone\{R\in\{\pm1\}\}$). The exponential part: on $u\le t/2$ it is at
597	most $C(1+t)^{-1/2}\int_0^\infty\nu e^{-\nu u}\dd u=C(1+t)^{-1/2}$; on $u>t/2$ it is
598	at most $\nu e^{-\nu t/2}\cdot2\sqrt t\le C(1+t)^{-1/2}$, since
599	$\nu\sqrt t\,\sqrt{1+t}\le2\nu(1+t)\le2(\nu+K)$. The occupation part is at most
600	$C\nu\eps\int_0^t\sqrt u\,(1+t-u)^{-1/2}\dd u\le C\nu\eps\,\sqrt t\cdot2\sqrt t
601	=C\nu\eps\,t$, and multiplying by $\sqrt{1+t}$,
602	$\nu\eps\,t\sqrt{1+t}\le2\nu\eps t^{3/2}=2(\nu t)\cdot\eps\sqrt t
603	=2(\nu t)\cdot\frac{\sqrt\nu\,\sqrt{\nu t}}{2q^2}\le\frac{\sqrt2\,K^{3/2}}{q^2}\le C$,
604	so this part too is $\le C(1+t)^{-1/2}$.
605	
606	\emph{At the origin.} Decomposing $\{R(t)=0\}$ on the last merge before $t$ (or none),
607	\[
608	  \PP\big(R(t)=0\big)=e^{-\nu t}
609	  +\eps\int_0^t\PP\big(R(u)\in\{\pm1\}\big)\,e^{-\nu(t-u)}\dd u
610	  \ \le\ e^{-\nu t}+\eps\int_0^t\frac{C}{\sqrt{1+u}}\dd u
611	  \ \le\ e^{-\nu t}+C\eps\sqrt t,
612	\]
613	using the off--origin bound just proved at $r=\pm1$; and
614	$\eps\sqrt t\,\sqrt{1+t}\le2\eps t=\nu t/q^2\le K/q^2$ shows
615	$C\eps\sqrt t\le C(1+t)^{-1/2}$. Collecting the three displays gives the claim.
616	\end{proof}
617	
618	The relative coordinate is now controlled. The sum coordinate is an additive functional
619	of the same event stream, so it needs a separate argument: conditionally on the
620	unsigned event skeleton, the remaining randomness of $S$ is a sum of independent
621	non--degenerate signs, and we recover spreading from a concentration inequality rather
622	than from a Fourier estimate.
623	
624	\begin{lemma}[conditional concentration for the sum coordinate]\label{lem:Slclt}
625	Let $S$ be the sum coordinate of \S\ref{sec:kernel}, and let $\mathfrak S$ denote the
626	\emph{unsigned skeleton}: the path of $R$ together with the times of the pair hops
627	(the events with $\Delta R=0$, which the $R$--path alone does not reveal), but not
628	their signs. Let $M=M(\mathfrak S)$ be the number of \emph{ambiguous} events, those
629	for which the skeleton admits two values of $\Delta S$. Then for every $s'\in\Z$,
630	\[
631	  \PP\big(S(t)=s'\mid \mathfrak S\big)\ \le\ \frac{C}{\sqrt{1+M}},
632	\]
633	and $M$ stochastically dominates a Poisson variable of mean $t$, so
634	$\PP(M<t/2)\le e^{-ct}$.
635	\end{lemma}
636	\begin{proof}
637	Given $\mathfrak S$, $S(t)=m(\mathfrak S)+\sum_{j=1}^M\eta_j$ with $m(\mathfrak S)$
638	determined by the skeleton and the $\eta_j$ conditionally independent: on
639	$\{|R|\ge2\}$, and on the outward steps from $\{\pm1\}$, a step $\Delta R=+1$ is
640	either ``species $1$ left'' ($\Delta S=-1$, conditional probability $q^2/(1+q^2)$) or
641	``species $2$ right'' ($\Delta S=+1$), and symmetrically for $\Delta R=-1$; a pair
642	hop has $\Delta S=\pm2$ with conditional probabilities $(1,q^4)/(1+q^4)$. (Merges,
643	splits and swaps determine $\Delta S$ and are unambiguous.) Each $\eta_j$ is
644	non--degenerate with both values of probability in $[\delta,1-\delta]$,
645	$\delta=\delta(q)>0$, so by the Kolmogorov--Rogozin concentration inequality
646	\cite[Ch.~III]{Petrov},
647	$\PP(S(t)=s'\mid\mathfrak S)\le C\big(\sum_j(1-Q(\eta_j;0))\big)^{-1/2}\wedge1
648	\le C(1+\delta M)^{-1/2}$. For the domination: in every state the total rate of
649	ambiguous events is $\ge1$ --- rate $2(1+q^2)$ on $\{|R|\ge2\}$, $1+q^2$ (the outward
650	steps) at $\{\pm1\}$, and $1+q^4$ (the pair hops) at the origin --- so, conditionally
651	on any past, ambiguous events fire at rate $\ge1$, $M$ dominates a rate--$1$ Poisson
652	count, and $\PP(M<t/2)\le e^{-ct}$.
653	\end{proof}
654	
655	The fixed--$q$ analysis of \S\ref{sec:tw} requires, beyond the upper bound
656	\eqref{eq:tildeR}, the exact leading occupation asymptotics of the relative walk,
657	including the invariant--measure weighting at the defect. The following elementary
658	lemma supplies them; its entire content is two exact identities (detailed balance and
659	first--passage decomposition) plus the free first--passage transform.
660	
661	\begin{lemma}[occupation--time asymptotics]\label{lem:tau}
662	Let $X$ be an irreducible, recurrent walk on $\Z$, reversible with respect to a
663	measure $m$ with $c_1\le m\le c_2$ and $m\equiv1$ off a finite set, and agreeing off a
664	finite set with the symmetric nearest--neighbour walk of rate $a$ per direction. Then
665	for every fixed $r$,
666	\[
667	  \tau_r(s):=\int_0^s\PP_0\big(X(t)=r\big)\dd t\ \sim\ m(r)\sqrt{\frac{s}{\pi a}}
668	  \qquad(s\to\infty).
669	\]
670	\end{lemma}
671	\begin{proof}
672	Let $G_\lambda(x,y)=\int_0^\infty e^{-\lambda t}\PP_x(X(t)=y)\dd t$, $\lambda>0$. Two
673	exact identities: detailed balance gives $m(x)G_\lambda(x,y)=m(y)G_\lambda(y,x)$, and
674	the first--passage decomposition at $y$ gives
675	$G_\lambda(x,y)=\E_x[e^{-\lambda T_y}]\,G_\lambda(y,y)$. Combining,
676	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Gid}
677	  G_\lambda(0,r)=\frac{m(r)}{m(0)}\,\E_r\big[e^{-\lambda T_0}\big]\,G_\lambda(0,0),
678	\end{equation}
679	and by recurrence $\E_r[e^{-\lambda T_0}]\to1$ as $\lambda\downarrow0$ for each fixed
680	$r$. To anchor $G_\lambda(0,0)$, sum \eqref{eq:Gid} over $r$ and use
681	$\sum_rG_\lambda(0,r)=\lambda^{-1}$:
682	\[
683	  \frac1\lambda=\frac{G_\lambda(0,0)}{m(0)}\sum_r m(r)\,\E_r\big[e^{-\lambda T_0}\big].
684	\]
685	Let $I$ be a finite interval containing the defect and the origin. From $r$ outside
686	$I$ the walk is free until it first hits $I$ (necessarily at the near edge), and from
687	$\partial I$ it reaches $0$ in a time which is almost surely finite, so
688	$\E_r[e^{-\lambda T_0}]=\varrho(\lambda)^{\mathrm{dist}(r,I)}\,
689	\E_{\partial I}[e^{-\lambda T_0}]$ with $\E_{\partial I}[e^{-\lambda T_0}]\to1$, where
690	$\varrho(\lambda)$ is the free nearest--neighbour first--passage root,
691	$\lambda+2a=a(\varrho+\varrho^{-1})$, i.e.\
692	$\varrho(\lambda)=1-\sqrt{\lambda/a}+O(\lambda)$. Hence
693	$\sum_rm(r)\E_r[e^{-\lambda T_0}]=\big(2\sqrt{a/\lambda}\big)(1+o(1))$ and
694	$G_\lambda(0,0)=\tfrac12\,m(0)\,(a\lambda)^{-1/2}(1+o(1))$. Returning to
695	\eqref{eq:Gid}, $G_\lambda(0,r)\sim\tfrac12\,m(r)\,(a\lambda)^{-1/2}$. Since
696	$\tau_r$ is the integral of a nonnegative function whose Laplace transform is
697	regularly varying of index $-\tfrac12$ at $0$, Karamata's Tauberian theorem gives
698	$\tau_r(s)\sim\tfrac12\,m(r)\,a^{-1/2}\,s^{1/2}/\Gamma(\tfrac32)
699	=m(r)\sqrt{s/(\pi a)}$.
700	\end{proof}
701	
702	\section{The two--particle dual kernel bound}\label{sec:kernel}
703	
704	The order--two fields of the fluctuation analysis reduce, by Lemma~\ref{lem:acr}, to
705	the two--particle dual kernel. A bound pair carries one particle of \emph{each}
706	species, so two particles of the same species can never bind; the different--species
707	pair is the bind/split/merge process. We treat the two channels.
708	
709	\begin{lemma}[same--species channel]\label{lem:asep}
710	The same--species two--particle dual kernel obeys $p_t(\xi,\xi')\le C/(1+t)$.
711	\end{lemma}
712	\begin{proof}
713	With no binding move available, the two same--species dual particles perform a
714	two--particle ASEP. By the exact Bethe--ansatz solution of the two--particle ASEP
715	master equation \cite{Schutz} the kernel is a sum of two products of
716	single--particle--type kernels (a free and a scattering term); each factor obeys the
717	Fourier bound of Lemma~\ref{lem:free}, so the kernel (two particles in $d=1$) is
718	$\le C/(1+t)$.
719	\end{proof}
720	
721	For the different--species pair with positions $X_1,X_2$ set
722	\begin{equation}\label{eq:SR}
723	  S:=X_1+X_2,\qquad R:=X_2-X_1.
724	\end{equation}
725	Off $\{-1,0,1\}$ the coordinate $R$ is a symmetric nearest--neighbour walk of rate
726	$1+q^2$; the origin $R=0$ (the bound pair) is sticky with split (escape) rate
727	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}=2q^2\eps$, entered from $\pm1$ only by a merge of rate $\eps$. The
728	coordinate $S$ is an additive functional of the $R$--path. This is exactly the process
729	of Lemmas~\ref{lem:Rlclt}--\ref{lem:Slclt}.
730	
731	\begin{theorem}[type D two--particle kernel bound]\label{thm:kernel}
732	For the different--species dual started from a bound pair, in the window
733	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t\le K$,
734	\begin{equation}\label{eq:kernel}
735	  p_t(\xi,\xi')\ \le\ \frac{C}{1+t}\ +\ e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t}\,\frac{C}{\sqrt{1+t}}.
736	\end{equation}
737	\end{theorem}
738	\begin{proof}
739	Write $p_t(\xi,\xi')=\E\big[\bone\{R(t)=r'\}\,\PP(S(t)=s'\mid\mathfrak S)\big]$ and
740	split on $\{M\ge t/2\}$. There Lemma~\ref{lem:Slclt} gives
741	$\PP(S(t)=s'\mid\mathfrak S)\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$, and taking the expectation against
742	$\bone\{R(t)=r'\}$ and applying Lemma~\ref{lem:Rlclt} yields
743	$\big(C/\sqrt{1+t}+\delta_{r',0}\,e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t}\big)\cdot C/\sqrt{1+t}$. On
744	$\{M<t/2\}$ the contribution is at most $\PP(M<t/2)\le e^{-ct}\le C/(1+t)$, absorbed
745	into the first term of \eqref{eq:kernel}.
746	\end{proof}
747	
748	\begin{remark}\label{rem:boundstate}
749	The bound state propagates in one dimension (whence the $t^{-1/2}$) but is
750	exponentially damped at the split rate $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}\sim4c/N^2$; its time integral
751	is finite, $\int_0^\infty e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}t}t^{-1/2}\dd t=\sqrt{\pi/\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}}
752	\sim N/\sqrt c=o(N^2)$. By Proposition~\ref{prop:sym} below it enters the species fields
753	with zero weight, so the departure from the ASEP bound $C/(1+t)$ is invisible to the
754	limiting fields and surfaces only in the crossover of \S\ref{sec:cross}.
755	\end{remark}
756	
757	\section{The decoupled Edwards--Wilkinson limit}\label{sec:ew}
758	
759	We now prove the first decoupling theorem by the martingale--problem scheme for
760	fluctuation fields: identify the drift as a Laplacian (D), the noise as white with the
761	right variance (N), and --- the point at which the two species could have interacted ---
762	show the cross--noise between them vanishes (X). The single--species inputs are
763	classical; the work is in (X) and in the drift remainder of (D), the only places where
764	two dual particles of different species can bind.
765	
766	Fix $\rho_1,\rho_2\in(0,1)$ (equivalently $\alpha_1,\alpha_2>0$); we do \emph{not}
767	require the symmetric line. For $\varphi\in\cS(\R)$ define the fluctuation fields
768	\begin{equation}\label{eq:field}
769	  Y_i^N(\varphi,t)=\frac1{\sqrt N}\sum_{x\in\Z}\varphi\Big(\frac xN\Big)
770	   \big(\eta_{i,x}(tN^2)-\rho_i\big),\qquad i=1,2.
771	\end{equation}
772	Across the $O(N)$ field window the blocking density tilts by $O(1/N)$, so $\nu$ is
773	locally homogeneous at the densities $\rho_i$ and the limiting coefficients are constant.
774	
775	\begin{theorem}[decoupled Edwards--Wilkinson limit]\label{thm:ewmain}
776	Let $\eta_0\sim\nu$, so that the process is stationary. Under $q=q_N=1-c/N^2$, the
777	pair $(Y_1^N,Y_2^N)$ is tight in
778	$D([0,T];\cS'(\R))^2$ and every limit point $(Y_1,Y_2)$ \emph{decouples}: each $Y_i$ is
779	a stationary solution of the linear stochastic heat equation
780	\[
781	  \partial_t Y_i=D\,\partial_x^2 Y_i+\sqrt{2\chi_i D}\,\partial_x\xi_i,
782	\]
783	with $D=1$ the (common) species diffusivity --- the symmetric--part diffusivity
784	$\tfrac12(1+q_N^2)\to1$, produced by the gradient computation of
785	Proposition~\ref{prop:drift} --- and $\chi_i=\rho_i(1-\rho_i)$ the
786	species--$i$ compressibility,
787	and the driving space--time white noises $\xi_1,\xi_2$ have \emph{vanishing
788	cross--correlation} (the cross bracket $\langle M_1,M_2\rangle$ is zero in the limit);
789	there is no coupling between the species in either the drift or the noise. The limit
790	law is unique.
791	\end{theorem}
792	
793	By Dynkin's formula \cite[App.~1.5]{KL} each field is a semimartingale
794	\begin{equation}\label{eq:dynkin}
795	  Y_i^N(\varphi,t)=Y_i^N(\varphi,0)+\int_0^t\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,s)\dd s+M_i^N(\varphi,t),
796	\end{equation}
797	with drift $\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,t)=N^{1/2}\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)W_{i,x}(\eta(tN^2))$,
798	$W_{i,x}$ the instantaneous species--$i$ current across $(x,x{+}1)$, and $M_i^N$ a
799	martingale whose predictable brackets are the carr\'e du champ. Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain}
800	follows from the martingale--problem scheme \cite[Ch.~11]{KL} once we establish, for
801	each $\varphi,T$:
802	\begin{itemize}
803	\item[\textup{(D)}] $\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,\cdot)\to D\,Y_i(\Delta\varphi,\cdot)$ in $L^2$;
804	\item[\textup{(N)}] $\langle M_i^N\rangle(\varphi,t)\to 2\chi_i D\,t\,\|\partial_x\varphi\|_2^2$;
805	\item[\textup{(X)}] $\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)\to0$;
806	\end{itemize}
807	together with tightness (Aldous--Mitoma) and uniqueness of the linear
808	(Ornstein--Uhlenbeck) martingale problem, both classical \cite[Ch.~11]{KL}.
809	
810	\subsection{Single--species Gaussianity}
811	\begin{lemma}\label{lem:gauss}
812	For each $i$, $Y_i^N$ converges to the Gaussian Ornstein--Uhlenbeck
813	Edwards--Wilkinson field, with the diagonal bracket of \textup{(N)}.
814	\end{lemma}
815	\begin{proof}
816	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}(a) the species--$i$ marginal is an autonomous WASEP
817	of right/left rates $1,q^2$, i.e.\ asymmetry $\gamma=1-q^2=2c/N^2+O(N^{-4})$. This sits
818	below the KPZ threshold, which under diffusive scaling occurs at asymmetry $N^{-1/2}$
819	\cite{GJ}; the Euler/Burgers term is $O(\gamma)\to0$, and the process is in the
820	Edwards--Wilkinson regime. The equilibrium density fluctuations of a one--species
821	exclusion process in this regime converge to the Gaussian Ornstein--Uhlenbeck solution
822	of $\partial_tY=D\partial_x^2Y+\sqrt{2\chi_i D}\partial_x\xi$, $\chi_i=\rho_i(1-\rho_i)$
823	--- the classical one--species equilibrium fluctuation theorem \cite[Ch.~11]{KL},
824	established for orthogonal duality systems in \cite{ACR2} --- with the diagonal bracket
825	$2\chi_i D$. (The classical statements concern the homogeneous Bernoulli equilibrium;
826	under the blocking measure the density tilts by $O(1/N)$ across the field window, and
827	the standard comparison --- coupling the dynamics from the tilted and untilted
828	equilibria and bounding the discrepancy field in $L^2$ --- transfers the result. We
829	omit the routine details.)
830	\end{proof}
831	
832	\noindent The content is thus in (X) and (D), where two dual particles of different
833	species can bind.
834	
835	\subsection{The cross noise}
836	The predictable cross bracket is $\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)=\int_0^t\Theta^N\dd s$,
837	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Theta}
838	  \Theta^N=\frac1N\sum_x\varphi'\Big(\frac xN\Big)^2 V_x,
839	\end{equation}
840	$V_x$ as in \eqref{eq:Vdef}. By Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}, $\E_\nu[\Theta^N]=0$.
841	
842	\begin{lemma}[orthogonality to the density fields; density--free]\label{lem:orth}
843	For all $\alpha_1,\alpha_2>0$ (in particular off the symmetric line), every
844	$i\in\{1,2\}$ and every $y\in\Z$, $\ip{V_x}{\eta_{i,y}-\rho_{i,y}}=0$, where
845	$\rho_{i,y}$ is the local density of species $i$ at $y$. Hence $V_x$ has no order--one
846	component in the local--basis decomposition \eqref{eq:Dfac}; its lowest order is two.
847	\end{lemma}
848	\begin{proof}
849	Since $\E_\nu[V_x]=0$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}, an identity in $\alpha_1,\alpha_2$),
850	\[
851	  \ip{V_x}{\eta_{i,y}-\rho_{i,y}}=\E_\nu[V_x\,\eta_{i,y}]-\rho_{i,y}\,\E_\nu[V_x]
852	  =\E_\nu[V_x\,\eta_{i,y}],
853	\]
854	so it suffices to show $\E_\nu[V_x\,\eta_{i,y}]=0$. For $y\notin\{x,x+1\}$ this is
855	immediate: $V_x$ is supported on the bond $\{x,x+1\}$ and $\nu$ is a product, so
856	$\eta_{i,y}$ is independent of $V_x$ and $\E_\nu[V_x\eta_{i,y}]=\E_\nu[V_x]\,\rho_{i,y}=0$.
857	For $y\in\{x,x+1\}$, the detailed--balance relations \eqref{eq:dbrel} ---
858	$\nu(0,3)=q^{-4}\nu(3,0)$, $\nu(1,2)=\nu(2,1)=q^{-2}\nu(3,0)$, identities in the
859	fugacities --- give the $\nu$--weighted values of $V_x$ on its four support
860	configurations as $\nu(3,0)\cdot1$, $\nu(0,3)\cdot q^4$, $\nu(1,2)\cdot(-q^2)$,
861	$\nu(2,1)\cdot(-q^2)=\nu(3,0)(+1,+1,-1,-1)$. Hence for any bond function $f$,
862	$\E_\nu[V_x f]=\nu(3,0)\big[f(3,0)+f(0,3)-f(1,2)-f(2,1)\big]$, and each single--site
863	occupation equals $1$ on exactly one ``$+$'' and one ``$-$'' configuration:
864	\[
865	  \begin{array}{c|cccc}
866	   & (3,0) & (0,3) & (1,2) & (2,1)\\\hline
867	   \eta_{1,x}   & 1 & 0 & 1 & 0\\
868	   \eta_{1,x+1} & 0 & 1 & 0 & 1\\
869	   \eta_{2,x}   & 1 & 0 & 0 & 1\\
870	   \eta_{2,x+1} & 0 & 1 & 1 & 0
871	  \end{array}
872	\]
873	so $f(3,0)+f(0,3)-f(1,2)-f(2,1)=0$ for each row, giving $\E_\nu[V_x\eta_{i,y}]=0$. The
874	mechanism is the $1+1-1-1$ cancellation of Proposition~\ref{prop:cross} one order
875	higher; it uses only detailed balance, not species exchange, and is therefore
876	density--free.
877	\end{proof}
878	
879	\begin{lemma}[equal--time variance]\label{lem:eqvar}
880	$\E_\nu[(\Theta^N)^2]\le C(\varphi)\,N^{-1}$.
881	\end{lemma}
882	\begin{proof}
883	$\E_\nu[(\Theta^N)^2]=N^{-2}\sum_{x,y}\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^2\varphi'(\tfrac yN)^2\E_\nu[V_xV_y]$.
884	Each $V_x$ has $\E_\nu[V_x]=0$ and is supported on $\{x,x+1\}$; by the product structure
885	$\E_\nu[V_xV_y]=0$ unless $|x-y|\le1$. The $O(1)$ surviving near--diagonal terms per $x$
886	are bounded, so the double sum is $\le C\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^4\le CN$ (a Riemann
887	sum). The prefactor $N^{-2}$ gives the claim.
888	\end{proof}
889	
890	\begin{proposition}[$L^2$ concentration of the cross bracket]\label{prop:conc}
891	$\E_\nu[\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)^2]\le
892	C(\varphi)\,\big(t^{3/2}N^{-2}+t\,c^{-1}N^{-1}\big)\to0$;
893	hence $\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle(\varphi,t)\to0$ in $L^2$, establishing \textup{(X)}.
894	\end{proposition}
895	\begin{proof}
896	Let $C_\Theta(s)=\E_\nu[\Theta^N(\eta_0)\Theta^N(\eta_{sN^2})]$. By stationarity,
897	\begin{equation}\label{eq:concstat}
898	  \E_\nu\Big[\Big(\int_0^t\Theta^N\dd s\Big)^2\Big]=2\int_0^t(t-s)C_\Theta(s)\dd s
899	  \le 2t\int_0^t C_\Theta(s)\dd s.
900	\end{equation}
901	By Lemma~\ref{lem:orth}, $V_x$ has no order--$\le1$ component, so its space--time
902	two--point function is carried by the order--two dual; by Lemma~\ref{lem:acr} and
903	Theorem~\ref{thm:kernel},
904	\begin{equation}\label{eq:concbd}
905	  \big|\E_\nu[V_x(\eta_0)V_y(\eta_{sN^2})]\big|\le C\,p_{sN^2}(\xi_x,\xi_y),
906	\end{equation}
907	$\xi_z$ the order--two configuration at $z$. Fix $x$ and sum over $y$: at microscopic
908	time $sN^2$ the order--two kernel spreads over $\sim N\sqrt s$ sites with peak
909	$\lesssim(sN^2)^{-1}$, over which $\varphi'(\tfrac yN)^2$ is essentially constant, so for
910	$s\ge N^{-2}$,
911	\[
912	  \sum_y\varphi'\Big(\tfrac yN\Big)^2\big|\E_\nu[V_x(\eta_0)V_y(\eta_{sN^2})]\big|
913	  \le C\varphi'\Big(\tfrac xN\Big)^2(N\sqrt s)(sN^2)^{-1}=C\varphi'\Big(\tfrac xN\Big)^2 N^{-1}s^{-1/2},
914	\]
915	while for $s\le N^{-2}$ the trivial bound of Lemma~\ref{lem:eqvar} gives
916	$\le C\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^2$. Summing over $x$ with $\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^4\le CN$
917	and reinstating $N^{-2}$,
918	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Ctheta}
919	  |C_\Theta(s)|\le C\min\!\big(N^{-1},\,N^{-2}s^{-1/2}\big)\;+\;C\,N^{-1}e^{-4cs}.
920	\end{equation}
921	The second term is the bound--state part of $p_t$, and it is \emph{larger} than the
922	continuum term by a factor $N$ (consistently with Remark~\ref{rem:boundstate}): summing
923	the atom of \eqref{eq:kernel} over $y$ costs the full $S$--spread,
924	$\sum_y p_{sN^2}(\xi_x,\xi_y)\bone\{R(\xi_y)=0\}=\PP\big(R(sN^2)=0\big)\le
925	C(N\sqrt s)^{-1}+e^{-\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}sN^2}$, and
926	$\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}sN^2=4cs(1+o(1))$, so at macroscopic times the damping is only
927	$e^{-4cs}=\Theta(1)$; multiplying by $N^{-2}\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)^4\le CN^{-1}$
928	gives the second term of \eqref{eq:Ctheta}. Splitting the first term at $s=N^{-2}$ and
929	integrating the second,
930	$\int_0^t C_\Theta\le C\big(N^{-3}+N^{-2}\sqrt t+(4cN)^{-1}\big)$; feeding this into
931	\eqref{eq:concstat} gives the claim.
932	\end{proof}
933	
934	\begin{remark}\label{rem:noH}
935	No Kipnis--Varadhan $H_{-1}$ estimate enters: its role is played by
936	Lemma~\ref{lem:orth}, which turns the would--be marginal $s^{-1}$ decay into the
937	integrable $s^{-1/2}$ of \eqref{eq:Ctheta}. This is the recursive--martingale viewpoint
938	of \cite{ACR2}.
939	\end{remark}
940	
941	\subsection{The drift}
942	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} the species--$1$ current $W_{1,x}$ is a function of
943	$\eta_1$ alone --- the single--species ASEP current --- which expands exactly, with
944	$\gamma=1-q^2$ and $\nabla f_x=f_{x+1}-f_x$, as
945	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Wgrad}
946	  W_{1,x}=-\nabla\eta_{1,x}+\gamma\,\eta_{1,x+1}(1-\eta_{1,x}).
947	\end{equation}
948	The first term is a discrete gradient; the second carries the prefactor
949	$\gamma=O(N^{-2})$. The merge channel, in which species~$1$ binds onto a species--$2$
950	site, does \emph{not} introduce an $\eta_2$--dependence: by
951	Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} the species--$2$ occupant never alters the species--$1$
952	transfer rate (the merge rate $\eps$ and the swap rate $q^2$ combine to the same $1$ as
953	the hop onto an empty site). Thus the drift involves only the autonomous single--species
954	WASEP $\eta_1$, and no two--species (bound--pair) structure enters it; the gradient part
955	will give the Laplacian and the $O(\gamma)$ part is the switched--off KPZ nonlinearity.
956	The bound--pair mode
957	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Bdef}
958	  B_z:=(\eta_{1,z}-\rho_1)(\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2)
959	\end{equation}
960	is the one near--conserved order--two object (it relaxes only at the split rate
961	$\sim\eps$); it does \emph{not} enter the drift \eqref{eq:Wgrad}. We nonetheless record
962	the following orthogonality, which makes the absence of any slow contribution explicit.
963	
964	\begin{corollary}[current orthogonal to the bound--pair mode]\label{prop:sym}
965	For all $\rho_1,\rho_2\in(0,1)$, $\ip{W_{i,x}}{B_z}=0$ for all $z$, where
966	$B_z=(\eta_{1,z}-\rho_1)(\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2)$.
967	\end{corollary}
968	\begin{proof}
969	By Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple} (equivalently \eqref{eq:Wgrad}), $W_{1,x}$ is a
970	function of $\eta_1$ alone. Since $\nu$ is a product measure with the two species
971	independent and $\E_\nu[\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2]=0$,
972	\[
973	  \ip{W_{1,x}}{B_z}=\E_\nu\big[W_{1,x}\,(\eta_{1,z}-\rho_1)\big]\,\E_\nu[\eta_{2,z}-\rho_2]=0,
974	\]
975	and symmetrically for $W_{2,x}$.
976	\end{proof}
977	
978	\begin{remark}[no off--symmetric--line obstruction]\label{rem:offline}
979	Because the overlap vanishes at \emph{every} $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$ (Corollary~\ref{prop:sym}),
980	the bound--pair mode never couples to the species current: there is no slow third
```
</details>

```
981	hydrodynamic field, and hence no obstruction to the decoupling, off the symmetric line
982	either. (A naive expansion of $W_{1,x}$ that misreads
983	the merge channel as an $\eta_2$--dependence produces a spurious overlap
984	$\propto(\rho_1-\rho_2)$; \eqref{eq:Wgrad} shows it vanishes identically.)
985	\end{remark}
986	
987	\begin{proposition}[drift]\label{prop:drift}
988	For each $i$ and any density $\rho_i\in(0,1)$,
989	$\Gamma_i^N(\varphi,\cdot)\to D\,Y_i(\Delta\varphi,\cdot)$ in $L^2$, with $D$ the
990	diffusivity of the symmetric part of the single--species dynamics, by an elementary
991	$L^2$ estimate. This establishes \textup{(D)}.
992	\end{proposition}
993	\begin{proof}
994	By \eqref{eq:Wgrad}, $\Gamma_1^N=\Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{grad}}+\gamma\,\Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{cor}}$
995	with
996	\[
997	  \Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{grad}}=N^{1/2}\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)(-\nabla\eta_{1,x}),\qquad
998	  \Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{cor}}=N^{1/2}\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)\,g_x,\quad g_x:=\eta_{1,x+1}(1-\eta_{1,x}).
999	\]
1000	\emph{Gradient term.} A summation by parts gives
1001	$\Gamma_1^{N,\mathrm{grad}}=N^{1/2}\sum_x(\nabla\varphi')(\tfrac xN)\,\eta_{1,x}
1002	 =N^{-1/2}\sum_x\varphi''(\tfrac xN)(\eta_{1,x}-\rho_1)+o(1)=D\,Y_1^N(\Delta\varphi)+o(1)$
1003	in $L^2$, $D$ the symmetric--part diffusivity; this is the standard gradient
1004	computation \cite[Ch.~11]{KL}. Since the symmetric part of each species is simple
1005	symmetric exclusion --- a gradient system --- $D$ is density--independent, hence the same
1006	constant for both species and at every $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$.
1007	\emph{Correction term.} Write $g_x=\bar g+(g_x-\bar g)$, $\bar g=\rho_1(1-\rho_1)$. The mean
1008	part $\gamma N^{1/2}\bar g\sum_x\varphi'(\tfrac xN)$ is the Euler flux
1009	$\partial_x[\gamma\rho_1(1-\rho_1)]$, of order $O(\gamma)\to0$ in the EW window. For the
1010	fluctuating part, by stationarity its time--integral has second moment
1011	\[
1012	  \E\Big[\Big(\gamma\!\int_0^t\!N^{1/2}\!\sum_x\varphi'(g_x{-}\bar g)(\eta(sN^2))\dd s\Big)^2\Big]
1013	  =\gamma^2 N\!\int_0^t\!\!\int_0^t\!\sum_{x,y}\varphi'\varphi'\,
1014	   \E_\nu[(g_x{-}\bar g)(\eta_0)(g_y{-}\bar g)(\eta_{|s-s'|N^2})]\dd s\dd s'.
1015	\]
1016	The static cross--correlation of $g$ is summable, $\sum_y|\E_\nu[(g_x-\bar g)(g_y-\bar g)(\tau)]|\le C$
1017	uniformly in $\tau$: $g$ is a function of $\eta_1$ alone, and expanding it in the
1018	single--species duality, its order--$k$ components propagate with $k$--particle
1019	kernels of total mass one, so the spatial sum of each component is bounded uniformly
1020	in the time lag. Hence the double sum is $\le C N$ for every lag, and the bound is
1021	$\le\gamma^2 N\cdot CN\,t^2=Cc^2N^{-2}t^2\to0$. Hence $\Gamma_1^N\to D\,Y_1(\Delta\varphi)$
1022	in $L^2$; the species--$2$ drift is identical.
1023	\end{proof}
1024	
1025	\noindent Granting (X), (N), (D), the limiting martingales $(M_1,M_2)$ are continuous
1026	(jumps $\le N^{-1/2}\|\varphi\|_\infty\to0$) and Gaussian with diagonal bracket
1027	(Lemma~\ref{lem:gauss}) and vanishing cross bracket (Proposition~\ref{prop:conc}); so
1028	the two driving noises are uncorrelated and the limit is the decoupled pair of EW
1029	fields of Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain}, unique by \cite[Ch.~11]{KL}. \hfill$\square$
1030	
1031	\section{The initial--condition crossover}\label{sec:cross}
1032	
1033	By Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain} the two limiting fields are decoupled, so the coupling the
1034	model exhibits is not in the limiting dynamics. We locate it in the initial data and
1035	compute it. Run the different--species dual of \S\ref{sec:kernel} from a bound pair at
1036	the origin, with $q=1-c/T$, observed at time $T$. Write $S,R$ as in \eqref{eq:SR}.
1037	
1038	\begin{lemma}[split time]\label{lem:split}
1039	The first split time $\tau$ is $\Exp(\nu_{\mathrm{sp}})$, $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}=2q^2\eps$,
1040	and $\nu_{\mathrm{sp}}T\to4c$, $\tau/T\To V\sim\Exp(4c)$, $\PP(\tau>T)\to e^{-4c}$.
1041	\end{lemma}
1042	\begin{proof}
1043	While bound the pair undergoes only the rate $1$ and $q^4$ hops (which preserve the
1044	bound phase) and the two splits (each rate $q^2\eps$, leaving it); the bound phase is a
1045	single state whose only phase--changing exit is the split, so its holding time is
1046	$\Exp(2q^2\eps)$. The limits follow from $\eps=2c/T+O(T^{-2})$.
1047	\end{proof}
1048	
1049	\begin{lemma}[no re--binding]\label{lem:rebind}
1050	The expected number of merges in $[\tau,T]$ is $O(c/\sqrt T)\to0$.
1051	\end{lemma}
1052	\begin{proof}
1053	After the split, $R$ is (away from a merge) a symmetric rate--$(1+q^2)$ walk; a merge
1054	occurs only from $R=\pm1$, at rate $\eps$. The expected occupation of $\{\pm1\}$ up to
1055	$T$ is $O(\sqrt T)$ by Lemma~\ref{lem:free}, so the expected number of merges is
1056	$\le\eps\cdot O(\sqrt T)=O(c/\sqrt T)$.
1057	\end{proof}
1058	
1059	It is convenient to pass to the sum and difference $S:=X_1+X_2$, $R:=X_2-X_1$, so that
1060	$X_i=(S\mp R)/2$ and the interaction (confined to the adjacent set $\{|R|=1\}$ and the
1061	origin) acts only on $R$.
1062	
1063	\begin{lemma}[exact symmetry identities and adjacent occupation]\label{lem:occ}
1064	Species--interchange symmetry maps $R\mapsto-R$, $S\mapsto S$ and fixes the law (the
1065	initial bound pair is symmetric); consequently
1066	\begin{equation}\label{eq:symm}
1067	  \E[R(t)]=0,\qquad \Cov\big(S(t),R(t)\big)=0\qquad(\forall t\ge0).
1068	\end{equation}
1069	Moreover, on the event $A_T:=\{\tau\le T,\ \text{no re--binding}\}$, the occupation
1070	$\Lambda_T:=\int_\tau^T\bone\{|R(t)|=1\}\dd t$ of the adjacent set obeys
1071	$\E[\Lambda_T]=O(\sqrt T)$.
1072	\end{lemma}
1073	\begin{proof}
1074	The identities \eqref{eq:symm} follow from $X_i=(S\mp R)/2$ and the invariance of the
1075	law of the process under $R\mapsto-R$. After the split and with no merge, $R$ is a
1076	continuous--time walk on $\Z\setminus\{0\}$ of total rate $\le2(1+q^2)$, symmetric on
1077	$\{|R|\ge2\}$; by Lemma~\ref{lem:free} its time--$t$ marginal is $\le C/\sqrt{1+t}$
1078	uniformly, so the expected occupation of $\{\pm1\}$ up to $T$ is
1079	$\int_0^T C/\sqrt{1+t}\dd t=O(\sqrt T)$.
1080	\end{proof}
1081	
1082	\begin{proposition}[two--phase functional CLT]\label{prop:twophase}
1083	Conditionally on $\tau/T\to u\in[0,1]$ and on $A_T$,
1084	\[
1085	  \frac1{\sqrt{2T}}\big(X_1(T),X_2(T)\big)\To
1086	  \big(\sqrt u\,\xi_0+\sqrt{1-u}\,\xi_1,\ \sqrt u\,\xi_0+\sqrt{1-u}\,\xi_2\big),
1087	\]
1088	with $\xi_0,\xi_1,\xi_2$ i.i.d.\ $N(0,1)$ --- a standard bivariate normal of correlation
1089	$u$. Mixing over $\tau/T\To U=\min(\Exp(4c),1)$ gives the limiting law of
1090	$(X_1,X_2)/\sqrt{2T}$.
1091	\end{proposition}
1092	\begin{proof}
1093	\emph{Pre--split.} On $[0,\tau]$ the common pair position $D$ is a walk of right rate
1094	$1$ and left rate $q^4$, hence variance rate $1+q^4\to2$ and drift $1-q^4=O(c/T)$. By
1095	Donsker's invariance principle with $\tau\approx uT$, $D(\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\To\sqrt u\,\xi_0$
1096	(the drift contributes $(1-q^4)\tau/\sqrt{2T}=O(c\sqrt u/\sqrt T)\to0$). Since
1097	$S(\tau)=2D(\tau)+O(1)$ and $R(\tau)=O(1)$, the split deposits
1098	$S(\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\To2\sqrt u\,\xi_0$ and $R(\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\to0$.
1099	
1100	\emph{Post--split.} Write $\bar S(s)=S(\tau{+}s)-S(\tau)$, $\bar R(s)=R(\tau{+}s)-R(\tau)$;
1101	each is a compensated jump process. Reading the rates of \S\ref{sec:kernel}, the
1102	instantaneous drifts vanish for $R$ on $\{|R|\ge2\}$ and equal $2\eps$ for $S$, while on
1103	$\{|R|=1\}$ they are $O(\eps)$ for $R$ and $\eps$ for $S$ (the deficit $2\eps\to\eps$ is
1104	the excluded merge); hence $\E[\bar R(T{-}\tau)]$ is supported on $\{|R|=1\}$ with
1105	magnitude $\le\eps\,\E[\Lambda_T]=O(c/\sqrt T)$, and
1106	$\E[\bar S(T{-}\tau)]=2\eps(T{-}\tau)-\eps\,\E[\Lambda_T]=O(c)$, both $o(\sqrt T)$. The
1107	predictable quadratic--variation rates are, on $\{|R|\ge2\}$,
1108	\[
1109	  a_S=a_R=2(1+q^2),\qquad a_{SR}=0,
1110	\]
1111	and on $\{|R|=1\}$ the bounded values $a_S=1+q^2$, $a_R=1+5q^2$, $a_{SR}=\eps$ (the swap
1112	$R=\pm1\mapsto\mp1$ contributes $\Delta R=\mp2$). Therefore
1113	\[
1114	  \langle\bar S\rangle=2(1+q^2)(T{-}\tau)-(1+q^2)\Lambda_T,\ \
1115	  \langle\bar R\rangle=2(1+q^2)(T{-}\tau)+(3q^2{-}1)\Lambda_T,\ \
1116	  \langle\bar S,\bar R\rangle=\eps\,\Lambda_T,
1117	\]
1118	and by Lemma~\ref{lem:occ} every $\Lambda_T$--term is $O_\PP(\sqrt T)=o_\PP(T)$. With
1119	$q^2\to1$ and $(T{-}\tau)/T\to1-u$,
1120	\[
1121	  \tfrac1{2T}\langle\bar S\rangle\to2(1-u),\quad
1122	  \tfrac1{2T}\langle\bar R\rangle\to2(1-u),\quad
1123	  \tfrac1{2T}\langle\bar S,\bar R\rangle\to0.
1124	\]
1125	The jumps are bounded by $2$, so the martingale functional CLT
1126	\cite[Thm.~7.1.4]{EK} gives $(\bar S,\bar R)(T{-}\tau)/\sqrt{2T}\To
1127	(\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_S,\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_R)$ with $\eta_S,\eta_R$ i.i.d.\ $N(0,1)$,
1128	independent of $\cF_\tau$ (hence of $\xi_0$) by the strong Markov property at $\tau$.
1129	
1130	\emph{Recombination.} Adding the two phases,
1131	$S(T)/\sqrt{2T}\To2\sqrt u\,\xi_0+\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_S$ and
1132	$R(T)/\sqrt{2T}\To\sqrt{2(1-u)}\,\eta_R$. Setting $\xi_1=(\eta_S-\eta_R)/\sqrt2$,
1133	$\xi_2=(\eta_S+\eta_R)/\sqrt2$ (an orthogonal change of variables, so $\xi_0,\xi_1,\xi_2$
1134	are i.i.d.\ $N(0,1)$) and using $X_i=(S\mp R)/2$ gives the claim. Integrating against
1135	$\tau/T\To U$ of Lemma~\ref{lem:split} yields the $U$--mixture.
1136	\end{proof}
1137	
1138	\begin{theorem}[closed forms for the crossover]\label{thm:closed}
1139	With $U$ as above and $g(u)=\E[Z_1^+Z_2^+]$ the positive--part covariance of a standard
1140	bivariate normal of correlation $u$,
1141	\[
1142	  \Corr(X_1,X_2)\ \longrightarrow\ \frac{1-e^{-4c}}{4c},\qquad
1143	  \Corr(X_1^+,X_2^+)\ \longrightarrow\
1144	  \frac{\pi}{8(\pi-1)c}\big[1-2e^{-4c}+I_0(4c)-L_0(4c)\big],
1145	\]
1146	with $I_0$ the modified Bessel and $L_0$ the modified Struve function. Both tend to $1$
1147	as $c\to0$ and decay as $1/c$ as $c\to\infty$.
1148	\end{theorem}
1149	\begin{proof}
1150	\emph{Full position.} By the exact identity $\Cov(S,R)=0$,
1151	$\Corr(X_1,X_2)=(\Var S-\Var R)/(\Var S+\Var R)$. The per--state increment second
1152	moments of $S,R$ satisfy $a_r+c_r=4(1+q^2)$ for every internal state $r$ (a direct
1153	check of the rates), so $\Var S+\Var R=4(1+q^2)\sum_r\tau_r=4(1+q^2)T$ up to the
1154	drift--compensator variances, which are $O(1)$ (the compensators are
1155	$O(\eps)$--Lipschitz functionals of occupations) and are absorbed in the error terms
1156	below, with $\tau_r$ the occupation of state $r$; and $a_r-c_r$ is supported on $\{0,\pm1\}$ with
1157	$a_0-c_0=4(1+q^4)$, $a_{\pm1}-c_{\pm1}=-4q^2$, so
1158	$\Var S-\Var R=4(1+q^4)\tau_0-4q^2(\tau_{+1}+\tau_{-1})$. In the scaling limit the
1159	bound--state occupation $\tau_0$ is the first--split time (re--binding negligible,
1160	Lemma~\ref{lem:rebind}), $\E[\tau_0]/T\to(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$, and the $\{|r|=1\}$
1161	occupations are $o(T)$; hence $\Corr\to(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$.
1162	
1163	\emph{One--sided observable.} Each marginal $Z_i^u\sim N(0,1)$ in
1164	Proposition~\ref{prop:twophase}, so $\E[Z_i^+]=1/\sqrt{2\pi}$ and
1165	$\Var(Z_i^+)=\tfrac12-\tfrac1{2\pi}$ are $u$--independent, and (by uniform
1166	integrability --- the fourth moments of $X_i/\sqrt{2T}$ are bounded --- together with
1167	$\PP(A_T^c)\to0$ and Cauchy--Schwarz to remove the conditioning,
1168	Proposition~\ref{prop:twophase})
1169	$\Corr(X_1^+,X_2^+)\to(\E[g(U)]-\tfrac1{2\pi})/(\tfrac12-\tfrac1{2\pi})$. By Price's
1170	theorem \cite{Price}, $g'(u)=\partial_u\E[Z_1^+Z_2^+]=\PP(Z_1>0,Z_2>0)$, and Sheppard's
1171	orthant formula \cite{Sheppard} gives $\PP(Z_1>0,Z_2>0)=\tfrac14+\tfrac{\arcsin u}{2\pi}
1172	=\tfrac1{2\pi}(\tfrac\pi2+\arcsin u)$, with $g(0)=\tfrac1{2\pi}$. Writing
1173	$g(U)=g(0)+\int_0^U g'$ and $\PP(U>s)=e^{-4cs}$,
1174	\[
1175	  \E[g(U)]-\tfrac1{2\pi}=\int_0^1 g'(s)e^{-4cs}\dd s
1176	  =\frac1{2\pi}\int_0^1\Big(\frac\pi2+\arcsin s\Big)e^{-4cs}\dd s.
1177	\]
1178	Integrating by parts and using
1179	$\int_0^1 e^{-4cs}(1-s^2)^{-1/2}\dd s=\int_0^{\pi/2}e^{-4c\sin\theta}\dd\theta
1180	=\tfrac\pi2[I_0(4c)-L_0(4c)]$ (DLMF 11.5.2) yields the stated form. As $c\to\infty$,
1181	$I_0(z)-L_0(z)=\tfrac2{\pi z}+O(z^{-3})$ gives the $1/c$ tail; as $c\to0$ both expressions
1182	tend to $1$.
1183	\end{proof}
1184	
1185	\begin{remark}\label{rem:icmeaning}
1186	By Theorem~\ref{thm:ewmain} the limiting fields are decoupled, so the crossover is an
1187	initial--condition effect, not a transport coefficient: from a block of bound pairs
1188	($Y_1(\cdot,0)\equiv Y_2(\cdot,0)$) the two decoupled flows decorrelate, the residual
1189	correlation measured by the $O(c)$ splits the run permits. In this picture $\rho(c)$ is
1190	the fading memory of a common origin --- the two species released by a single split
1191	start out at the same place and are then carried apart by two independent flows, so the
1192	correlation surviving at time $T$ records only how many such shared splits the run
1193	allowed. This is consistent with $C_{12}\equiv0$ and $\sigma_{12}=0$
1194	(Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}).
1195	\end{remark}
1196	
1197	\section{The Tracy--Widom regime}\label{sec:tw}
1198	
1199	Now fix $q\in(0,1)$ and study the integrated currents $N_1(s),N_2(s)$ across the origin
1200	from the step initial condition at a single time $s$, with standardised currents
1201	$\cO^i=(N_i-\E N_i)/\sigma_i$, $\sigma_i\asymp s^{1/3}$. The marginal statements hold
1202	for \emph{every} $n$ by Proposition~\ref{prop:decouplen}, via the time--changed
1203	generator $\Lt^{(n)}=\beta_n^{-1}\cL^{(n)}$, under which the single--species rates
1204	are the $n$--free $q^{\mp1}$. The joint statement (Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}) uses the
1205	duality and is proved at $n=\infty$; it extends verbatim to $n=2,3$, where the
1206	duality is known \cite{REU}, and to every $n$ modulo the duality conjecture of
1207	\cite[Rmk.~4]{REU}.
1208	
1209	\subsection{Marginals}
1210	\begin{theorem}[Tracy--Widom marginals]\label{thm:marg}
1211	For every $n\in\N\cup\{\infty\}$ and each species, $\cO^i_s\To F_2$, the GUE
1212	Tracy--Widom law.
1213	\end{theorem}
1214	\begin{proof}
1215	By Propositions~\ref{prop:decouple}(a) and \ref{prop:decouplen}, each species' current
1216	is an autonomous single--species ASEP --- with rates $r_R=1,r_L=q^2$ at $n=\infty$ and
1217	$q^{\mp1}\beta_n$ at finite $n$, the factor $\beta_n$ a pure time change removed by
1218	the standardisation. The step block (state $3$ on $\{x\le0\}$, empty on $\{x>0\}$)
1219	projects, per species, to the step initial condition, and step--ASEP currents are
1220	Tracy--Widom by \cite[Thm.~1.4]{BCS}.
1221	\end{proof}
1222	
1223	\begin{remark}
1224	Theorem~\ref{thm:marg} proves the Tracy--Widom conjecture of \cite[\S3.1.1]{REU}
1225	(stated there for $n=2,3$; here for every $n$), up to the standard equivalence
1226	between current and tagged--position asymptotics.
1227	\end{remark}
1228	
1229	\subsection{Triangular duality and $q$--Laplace decoupling}
1230	For the cross sector the dual has one walker of each species; let
1231	$\mathfrak r=X_2-X_1$ be the relative coordinate, which is driftless (the two species
1232	share the drift), finite--range, with a bounded perturbation at the origin from the
1233	binding. The triangular duality of Corollary~\ref{cor:tri} pairs finite dual
1234	configurations with the step sector, on which it takes a strikingly simple form.
1235	
1236	\begin{lemma}[step--sector duality identities]\label{lem:tridual}
1237	Let $\eta^0$ be the step (state $3$ on $x\le0$, empty on $x>0$), let $X(\cdot)$ denote
1238	the free asymmetric walk (rates $1$ right, $q^2$ left), and let $(X_1,X_2)$ denote the
1239	two--particle dual --- one particle of each species, each marginally a free walk by
1240	Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}, jointly carrying the binding interaction on the
1241	contact set $\{|X_1-X_2|\le1\}$. Then for all $a,b\in\Z$ and $s\ge0$,
1242	\begin{align}
1243	  \E_{\eta^0}\Big[\eta_{i,a}(s)\,q^{2\left(a+N^+_{a+1}(\eta_i(s))\right)}\Big]
1244	   &=\PP_a\big(X(s)\le0\big),\label{eq:tri1}\\
1245	  \E_{\eta^0}\Big[\eta_{1,a}(s)\,\eta_{2,b}(s)\,
1246	    q^{2\left(a+N^+_{a+1}(\eta_1(s))\right)+2\left(b+N^+_{b+1}(\eta_2(s))\right)}\Big]
1247	   &=\PP_{(a,b)}\big(X_1(s)\le0,\ X_2(s)\le0\big),\label{eq:tri2}
1248	\end{align}
1249	and $\PP_{(a,b)}(X_1(s)\le0)=\PP_a(X(s)\le0)$ exactly.
1250	\end{lemma}
1251	\begin{proof}
1252	Apply Corollary~\ref{cor:tri} with $\xi$ a single species--$i$ dual particle at $a$
1253	(respectively the pair at $(a,b)$). With one particle per species, $N^-\equiv0$; and
1254	on the step, $N^+_{z+1}(\eta^0_i)=-z$ for $z\le0$, so every weight in
1255	$D^{\mathrm{tri}}(\xi_s,\eta^0)$ equals $q^{2(X_i-X_i)}=1$ and
1256	$D^{\mathrm{tri}}(\xi_s,\eta^0)=\bone\{X_i(s)\le0\ \forall i\}$. On a finite lattice
1257	the displays are then exactly the duality relation; the extension to $\Z$ is the
1258	standard finite--propagation--speed approximation (couple the infinite system to its
1259	restriction to $[-K,K]$: for fixed $s$, observables of bounded support and the
1260	finitely many dual particles are affected only with probability $O(e^{-cK})$). We
1261	have additionally verified \eqref{eq:tri1}--\eqref{eq:tri2} exactly, by matrix
1262	exponentiation of the full forward dynamics on $8$ sites against the one-- and
1263	two--particle dual sectors. The marginal consistency is
1264	Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}: the species--$1$ coordinate of the dual pair is an
1265	autonomous free walk.
1266	\end{proof}
1267	
1268	The identities \eqref{eq:tri1}--\eqref{eq:tri2} show precisely what the two--particle
1269	dual computes: the currents enter through the \emph{$q$--deformed} weights
1270	$q^{2N^+}$, not linearly. Summing the telescope
1271	\begin{equation}\label{eq:telescope}
1272	  q^{2N^+_{a+1}(\eta_i)}-q^{2N^+_{a}(\eta_i)}
1273	  =(1-q^2)\,\eta_{i,a}\,q^{2N^+_{a+1}(\eta_i)}
1274	\end{equation}
1275	over half--lines converts them into exact joint $q$--Laplace formulas, and the
1276	decoupling theorem of this regime is the following contact representation.
1277	
1278	\begin{theorem}[$q$--Laplace decoupling: exact contact representation]\label{thm:cov}
1279	At $n=\infty$, from the step initial condition, for all $s\ge0$,
1280	\begin{equation}\label{eq:qmom}
1281	  \E\big[q^{2N_i(s)}\big]=1-(1-q^2)\sum_{a\ge1}q^{-2a}\,\PP_a\big(X(s)\le0\big),
1282	\end{equation}
1283	\begin{equation}\label{eq:qcov}
1284	  \Cov\big(q^{2N_1(s)},\,q^{2N_2(s)}\big)
1285	  =(1-q^2)^2\sum_{a,b\ge1}q^{-2(a+b)}\,C_s(a,b),
1286	\end{equation}
1287	where
1288	$C_s(a,b):=\PP_{(a,b)}\big(X_1(s)\le0,X_2(s)\le0\big)
1289	-\PP_a\big(X(s)\le0\big)\PP_b\big(X(s)\le0\big)$ is the connected pair kernel and all
1290	sums converge absolutely. The kernel is generated entirely by contact:
1291	$|C_s(a,b)|\le\PP_{(a,b)}(\tau_{\mathrm c}\le s)$, with $\tau_{\mathrm c}$ the first
1292	meeting time of the two dual walkers, and $C_s\equiv0$ if the binding interaction is
1293	removed. In particular the two currents decouple in the $q$--Laplace sense:
1294	$\big|\Cov(q^{2N_1},q^{2N_2})(s)\big|\le\E\big[q^{2N_1(s)}\big]\to0$.
1295	\end{theorem}
1296	\begin{proof}
1297	\eqref{eq:telescope} is $N^+_a=N^+_{a+1}+\eta_{i,a}$; summed over $a\ge m$ it
1298	telescopes to $1-q^{2N^+_m(\eta_i)}$ (the configuration is right--finite, so
1299	$N^+_a\to0$), and $N^+_1(\eta_i)=N_i$. Taking expectations at $m=1$ and inserting
1300	\eqref{eq:tri1} weighted by $q^{-2a}$ gives \eqref{eq:qmom}; the double telescope
1301	with \eqref{eq:tri2} gives
1302	\[
1303	  \E\Big[\frac{(1-q^{2N_1})(1-q^{2N_2})}{(1-q^2)^2}(s)\Big]
1304	  =\sum_{a\ge1}\sum_{b\ge1}q^{-2(a+b)}\,\PP_{(a,b)}\big(X_1(s)\le0,\ X_2(s)\le0\big),
1305	\]
1306	and expanding the product and subtracting the marginal identities yields
1307	\eqref{eq:qcov}. Absolute convergence: to reach $\{\le0\}$ from $a$ the walk makes at
1308	least $a$ jumps, so $\PP_a(X(s)\le0)\le\PP(\mathrm{Poi}((1+q^2)s)\ge a)$ decays
1309	super--exponentially in $a$ for fixed $s$, beating $q^{-2a}$; this justifies Fubini
1310	throughout. Contact generation: realise the pair $(X_1,X_2)$ and an independent pair
1311	$(\widetilde X_1,\widetilde X_2)$ on one probability space, with identical
1312	trajectories until the first time $\tau_{\mathrm c}$ at which the walkers come within
1313	distance $1$ --- possible since off the contact set the pair dynamics consists of the
1314	same independent free jumps. Then
1315	$C_s(a,b)=\E\big[\bone\{X_1(s)\le0,X_2(s)\le0\}
1316	-\bone\{\widetilde X_1(s)\le0,\widetilde X_2(s)\le0\}\big]$, which vanishes on
1317	$\{\tau_{\mathrm c}>s\}$; hence $|C_s(a,b)|\le\PP(\tau_{\mathrm c}\le s)$, and
1318	$C_s\equiv0$ for independent walkers. Finally, for $U,V\in[0,1]$ one has
1319	$|\Cov(U,V)|\le\min(\E U,\E V)$, and $\E[q^{2N_1(s)}]\to0$ since $N_1(s)\to\infty$
1320	almost surely (the autonomous ASEP marginal from step has strictly positive limiting
1321	current).
1322	\end{proof}
1323	
1324	\begin{conjecture}[linear covariance]\label{conj:cov}
1325	At every $n$, from the step initial condition,
1326	$\Cov(N_1,N_2)(s)\sim c(q)\sqrt s$ as $s\to\infty$ with $c(q)\in(0,\infty)$;
1327	consequently $\Corr(N_1,N_2)\asymp s^{-1/6}\to0$ and the two Tracy--Widom currents
1328	are asymptotically uncorrelated. At $q=\tfrac12$, Monte Carlo gives
1329	$c=0.099\pm0.003$, with the $\sqrt s$ scaling holding over
1330	$s\in[50,3.3\times10^4]$ and the correlation decaying at the $s^{-1/6}$ rate
1331	(\S\ref{sec:numerics}).
1332	\end{conjecture}
1333	
1334	The linear covariance is not a finite--mass dual observable: by
1335	\eqref{eq:tri1}--\eqref{eq:tri2} the duality reaches the currents only through the
1336	weights $q^{2N^+}$, and extracting $\E[N_1N_2]$ requires the full tower of joint
1337	$q$--moments (same--species dual particles in unbounded number) --- the same
1338	difficulty as the joint law itself, left open in \S\ref{sec:disc}. This, and not a
1339	missing estimate, is why the covariance asymptotics are stated as a conjecture.
1340	
1341	The natural candidate for the conjectured coefficient $c(q)$ is the contact
1342	combination
1343	$(1+q^4)\tau_0-q^2(\tau_{+1}+\tau_{-1})$, $\tau_r=\int_0^s\PP(\mathfrak r(t)=r)\dd t$,
1344	since (exactly as in the proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:closed}) the per--state increment
1345	second moments of $\mathfrak s=X_1+X_2$ and $\mathfrak r$ coincide off contact
1346	($a_r=c_r$ for $|r|\ge2$) while at contact $a_0-c_0=4(1+q^4)$,
1347	$a_{\pm1}-c_{\pm1}=-4q^2$. Two corrections to an earlier version of this draft are
1348	required here, and we record them precisely.
1349	
1350	\begin{proposition}[contact occupations of the relative walk]\label{prop:occ}
1351	The relative walk $\mathfrak r$ is reversible with respect to the measure
1352	$m(0)=q^{-2}$, $m(r)=1$ \textup($r\ne0$\textup): detailed balance across the bond
1353	$\{0,1\}$ reads $m(0)\cdot q^2\eps=m(1)\cdot\eps$ \textup(split out of the bound state
1354	against merge into it\textup), and is immediate at the swap and at all bulk bonds.
1355	Consequently
1356	\[
1357	  \frac{\tau_0(s)}{\tau_{\pm1}(s)}\ \longrightarrow\ q^{-2}\qquad(s\to\infty),
1358	\]
1359	the bound state being overweighted by exactly the stickiness ratio $q^{-2}$, and
1360	\[
1361	  (1+q^4)\,\tau_0-q^2(\tau_{+1}+\tau_{-1})\ \sim\
1362	  \frac{1-q^4}{q^{2}}\,\sqrt{\frac{s}{\pi(1+q^2)}}.
1363	\]
1364	\end{proposition}
1365	\begin{proof}
1366	Reversibility: the bulk rates ($1+q^2$ each way) and the swap ($q^2$ each way between
1367	$\pm1$) are symmetric, so $m$ is constant off the origin; the only nontrivial bond is
1368	$0\leftrightarrow\pm1$, with rate $q^2\eps$ out (split) and $\eps$ in (merge), giving
1369	$m(0)=q^{-2}m(\pm1)$. The walk is recurrent (off a finite set it is the symmetric
1370	nearest--neighbour walk) and satisfies the hypotheses of Lemma~\ref{lem:tau} with
1371	$a=1+q^2$, the swap being part of the finite defect, so
1372	$\tau_r(s)\sim m(r)\sqrt{s/(\pi(1+q^2))}$, and the two displays follow.
1373	Numerically (exact integration of the master equation at $q=\tfrac12$):
1374	$p_t(0,0)/p_t(0,1)=4.002$ at $t=3000$ against $q^{-2}=4$, and the combination divided
1375	by $\sqrt s$ is $1.875$ at $s=3000$ against the predicted limit $1.892$, the deficit
1376	decaying as $s^{-1/2}$.
1377	\end{proof}
1378	
1379	\begin{remark}[the leading constant is open]\label{rem:covconst}
1380	An earlier version of this draft asserted the exact identity
1381	$\Cov(N_1,N_2)=(1+q^4)\tau_0-q^2(\tau_{+1}+\tau_{-1})$ together with the claim that the
1382	three occupations share a common leading coefficient, concluding
1383	$\Cov\sim(1-q^2)^2c'\sqrt s$. Both steps fail. First, the occupations do \emph{not}
1384	share a coefficient: by Proposition~\ref{prop:occ} the combination carries the weight
1385	$q^{-2}(1-q^4)$, not $(1-q^2)^2$ --- the bound state's $q^{-2}$ overweighting is
1386	precisely the residual trace of the binding interaction, and it changes the order of
1387	vanishing as $q\to1$ from quadratic to linear in $1-q^2$. Second, the identity itself
1388	cannot hold with the occupations of a bound--started walk: forward Monte Carlo of the
1389	full lattice dynamics at $q=\tfrac12$ ($4.5\times10^4$ trials, \S\ref{sec:numerics})
1390	gives $\Cov(N_1,N_2)=(0.099\pm0.003)\sqrt s$, whereas
1391	$(1+q^4)\tau_0-q^2(\tau_{+1}+\tau_{-1})\sim1.89\sqrt s$ and the earlier claimed form
1392	evaluates to $0.28\sqrt s$. The structural reason is now transparent from
1393	Lemma~\ref{lem:tridual}: the two--particle dual computes the \emph{$q$--deformed}
1394	currents \eqref{eq:qcov}, not the linear ones, so any occupation formula for
1395	$\Cov(N_1,N_2)$ necessarily carries the nontrivial $q^{2N^+}$ weighting. Identifying
1396	$c(q)$ in Conjecture~\ref{conj:cov} is open; the $\sqrt s$ scaling itself is
1397	confirmed numerically over $s\in[50,3.3\times10^4]$.
1398	\end{remark}
1399	
1400	\begin{remark}[why there is no ballistic term]\label{rem:noballistic}
```
</details>

```
1400	\begin{remark}[why there is no ballistic term]\label{rem:noballistic}
1401	The step block is deterministic and species--$i$ particles enter $\{x>0\}$ only across
1402	the bond $(0,1)$, so $\delta N_i=\delta J_i$ with $J_i$ the single--bond integrated
1403	current; this localization gives the transport reading. Decomposing
1404	$J_i=M_i+A_i$ (martingale plus compensator), the martingale cross--bracket is exactly the
1405	contact carr\'e du champ $\langle M_1,M_2\rangle(s)=\int_0^s V_0(\eta_u)\dd u$ with $V_0$
1406	of \eqref{eq:Vdef} --- only bound--pair hops and swaps move both species across one bond.
1407	The drift cross--terms $\Cov(M_i,A_j),\Cov(A_1,A_2)$ have a leading part equal to the
1408	equilibrium Green--Kubo cross--mobility $\sigma_{12}\cdot s$, which vanishes by
1409	Proposition~\ref{prop:cross}. So $\Cov(N_1,N_2)$ carries no $O(s)$ ballistic part, and
1410	the surviving $\sqrt s$ is the transient contact contribution evaluated above by duality.
1411	The forward decomposition thus explains the absence of an $O(s)$ term but does not
1412	\emph{by itself} yield the constant: $M_i$ and $A_i$ each have $\Theta(s)$ variance and
1413	their cancellation to the $O(\sqrt s)$ remainder is a transport--coefficient near
1414	cancellation, in contrast to the exact, term--by--term off--contact identity
1415	$a_r=c_r$ supplied by the duality.
1416	\end{remark}
1417	
1418	\begin{remark}\label{rem:uncorr}
1419	Theorem~\ref{thm:cov} is the strongest joint statement we prove unconditionally: an
1420	exact identity, valid for all $s$, in which the inter--species coupling enters only
1421	through the contact kernel $C_s$ --- the $q$--Laplace analogue of uncorrelatedness.
1422	For the linear currents, Conjecture~\ref{conj:cov} is supported by the exact
1423	$\sqrt s$ scaling in the simulations and by the occupation analysis of
1424	Proposition~\ref{prop:occ}; a proof would require joint control of the full
1425	$q$--moment tower, and even then says nothing about higher joint cumulants.
1426	\end{remark}
1427	
1428	\section{The asymmetry--exponent phase picture}\label{sec:phase}
1429	
1430	The two regimes are endpoints of a one--parameter family of scalings, and the
1431	following observations --- established at the level of the explicit rate algebra and
1432	extensive simulation, but not with the rigour of \S\S\ref{sec:ew}--\ref{sec:tw} --- place
1433	them in a single picture. Tune
1434	\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha}
1435	  q=1-c\,T^{-\alpha},\qquad \alpha\ge0,\ c>0,
1436	\end{equation}
1437	and observe the integrated currents at time $T$; the splits per particle are
1438	$\sim T(1-q^2)\sim2cT^{1-\alpha}$, governing the limiting cross--correlation.
1439	
1440	\begin{itemize}
1441	\item $\alpha<1$: $\to\infty$ splits per particle, the species mix,
1442	$\Corr(N_1,N_2)\to0$; the marginals are Tracy--Widom (the asymmetry is still
1443	macroscopic), and $\alpha=0$ is the fixed--$q$ regime of \S\ref{sec:tw}.
1444	\item $\alpha=1$ (critical): $O(c)$ splits, $\Corr\to\rho(c)\in(0,1)$, the crossover of
1445	Theorem~\ref{thm:closed}; $\gamma\sim c/T$ vanishes, the KPZ nonlinearity switches off,
1446	and the limit is the Edwards--Wilkinson pair of \S\ref{sec:ew}.
1447	\item $\alpha>1$: $\to0$ splits, bound pairs survive, $\Corr\to1$ continuously --- the
1448	locked limit of Remark~\ref{rem:range}.
1449	\end{itemize}
1450	
1451	\noindent A single axis thus interpolates from decoupled Tracy--Widom ($\alpha=0$)
1452	through the EW crossover ($\alpha=1$) to locking ($\alpha\to\infty$); the hydrodynamics
1453	decouple for every $\alpha,n$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}), only the
1454	fluctuation--level coupling depending on the scaling. The crossover correlation
1455	$\rho(c)$ is not a transport coefficient: $C_{12}\equiv0$ and (numerically)
1456	$\sigma_{12}\approx0$ (measured $-0.024\pm0.022$ at $c=1$, against the front value
1457	$\rho(1)\approx0.27$), so what remains is a transient, shared--source correlation --- the
1458	species released by a common split carrying correlated currents, $\rho(c)$ the decaying
1459	memory of the perfectly correlated block initial condition. To our knowledge this
1460	combination (Edwards--Wilkinson class, diagonal compressibility, vanishing
1461	cross--mobility, nonzero initial--condition--driven cross--correlation with a
1462	$\rho(c)\sim1/c$ crossover) matches no model in the multi--species fluctuating
1463	hydrodynamics or macroscopic fluctuation theory literature.
1464	
1465	We record three further numerical observations, consistent across $n$ (and into the
1466	negative--$n$ window of Remark~\ref{rem:range}):
1467	\begin{itemize}
1468	\item \emph{Crossover time.} At fixed $q$ near $1$ the Tracy--Widom statistics emerge only
1469	past $t_{\mathrm{cross}}\sim(1-q)^{-3/2}$; observed earlier the marginal looks Gaussian
1470	(the $\alpha\ge1$ behaviour at finite time). At $q=\tfrac12$ the law is clean by
1471	$T\sim10^3$ (skewness $\to-0.21$, the $F_2$ value).
1472	\item \emph{Subleading variance.} $\Var(N_i)=A\,s^{2/3}+B\,s^{1/2}+\cdots$, a
1473	relative--mode (Popkov--Sch\"utz--type) correction; the standardised remainder
1474	$\sigma_{\mathrm{extra}}^2\asymp s^{-1/6}$ decays at the same rate as the cross
1475	correlation ($\sigma_{\mathrm{extra}}\approx0.39$ vs $0.36$ at $n=2$ vs $13$,
1476	$T=3.3\times10^4$).
1477	\item \emph{Multipoint uncorrelatedness.} The cross--species height functions are
1478	uncorrelated at all spatial separations ($n=2$, $q=\tfrac12$, $T=3.3\times10^4$), so
1479	the decoupling extends from the integrated current to the spatial process, and it is
1480	$n$--independent at that level.
1481	\end{itemize}
1482	
1483	\section{Numerical evidence}\label{sec:numerics}
1484	
1485	We summarise the Monte Carlo simulations that corroborate the theorems and the
1486	phase picture. Lattice simulations use the exact $n=\infty$ rate table \eqref{eq:rates}
1487	from a block initial condition of bound pairs; dual computations use the two-- and
1488	few--particle generators directly. All runs store only currents and scalars (not lattice
1489	states), with $5\times10^4$ trials unless noted.
1490	
1491	\subsection{The Edwards--Wilkinson regime}
1492	The single--species current standard deviation fits the EW law $\mathrm{std}(N_1)\sim
1493	T^{1/4}$ across $T\in[100,10^4]$ (local slopes $0.22$--$0.28$, fit exponent $0.244$),
1494	excluding the $T^{1/2}$ that a bound--pair third field would produce, consistent with
1495	the autonomous single--species drift of Proposition~\ref{prop:drift}. The initial--condition crossover matches the closed forms of
1496	Theorem~\ref{thm:closed} to sampling error, with the predicted $1/c$ tail
1497	(Figure~\ref{fig:rho}); the simpler full--position observable $(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$ matches
1498	equally well. Direct measurement gives $\Corr(J_1,J_2)=-0.02\pm0.02$ (vanishing
1499	cross--mobility) and $C_{12}=0$ within error, confirming that $\rho(c)$ is neither a
1500	static nor a dynamic transport coefficient.
1501	
1502	\begin{figure}[h]\centering
1503	\includegraphics[width=0.49\textwidth]{corr_Xplus_c.png}\hfill
1504	\includegraphics[width=0.49\textwidth]{rho_c_duality.jpg}
1505	\caption{The initial--condition crossover of Theorem~\ref{thm:closed}. Left: the
1506	one--sided observable $\Corr(X_1^+,X_2^+)$ (Bessel--Struve closed form, curve) against
1507	two--particle Monte Carlo (dots), with the $\tfrac{\pi}{8(\pi-1)}c^{-1}$ tail. Right: the
1508	full--position observable $\Corr(X_1,X_2)\to(1-e^{-4c})/(4c)$ against Monte Carlo. Both
1509	run from perfectly correlated data ($\Corr\to1$ as $c\to0$) to the decoupled $1/c$ tail.}
1510	\label{fig:rho}
1511	\end{figure}
1512	
1513	\subsection{The Tracy--Widom regime}
1514	The covariance scales as $\Cov(N_1,N_2)\sim T^{1/2}$ (Conjecture~\ref{conj:cov}), confirmed
1515	by exact augmented--matrix occupation--time computation ($\tau_0\sim T^{0.505}$,
1516	$\Cov\sim T^{0.504}$ at $q=\tfrac12$) and by forward simulation
1517	(Figure~\ref{fig:cov}, left). A dedicated forward run ($4.5\times10^4$ trials,
1518	$T\le800$, $q=\tfrac12$) pins the prefactor: $\Cov(N_1,N_2)=(0.099\pm0.003)\sqrt T$,
1519	in agreement with the $n=\infty$ data of Figure~\ref{fig:cov} ($\approx0.105\sqrt T$
1520	over $T\in[10^2,10^4]$); the same run reproduces the Borodin--Corwin--Sasamoto
1521	variance $2^{-8/3}(\gamma T)^{2/3}\Var(\chi_2)$, $\gamma=1-q^2$, to within $10\%$, and
1522	exact integration of the relative--walk master equation gives
1523	$\tau_0/\tau_1\to q^{-2}$ as in Proposition~\ref{prop:occ}. Both theoretical
1524	candidate prefactors of Remark~\ref{rem:covconst} are excluded, so the constant
1525	carries a nontrivial front factor. The marginals converge to $F_2$ (Figure~\ref{fig:cov},
1526	middle: CDF/histogram; skewness $\to-0.21$, excess kurtosis $\to0.09$, the GUE
1527	Tracy--Widom values), and the limit is $n$--independent (Figure~\ref{fig:cov}, right:
1528	$n=2$ and $n=13$ collapse onto $F_2$). The standardised correlation accordingly decays,
1529	$\Corr(N_1,N_2)\sim s^{-1/6}\to0$, the asymptotic decoupling of
```
</details>

## 🤖 Assistant

Fresh pass complete — full report, written as if I'd never seen the paper:

## What survives a from-scratch verification (re-derived, not recalled)

- **§2–3 algebra**: detailed balance (all twelve channels including mixed hops, which I checked separately this time — $\nu(1,3)=q^{-2}\nu(3,1)$ ✓), `prop:decouple` case by case, the `prop:decouplen` finite-$n$ cancellations re-derived by hand ($q^{-2}\sigma_n + q^{2n-2}-q^{2n-4}+2q^{-2} = q^{-2n}+q^{2n-2}$ ✓ etc.), $V_x$ as the correct cross carré du champ, and the Kolmogorov cycle condition for `prop:occ`'s reversibility ($\varepsilon\cdot q^2\varepsilon\cdot q^2$ both ways around the $-1\to0\to1\to-1$ cycle ✓).
- **§4**: `lem:free`'s Nash chain checks (including the discrete Nash with constant 4); `lem:Rlclt`'s excursion proof holds at every step — killing domination, exit-intensity, the bootstrap $g\le CK\sqrt t$, and both constant chases close within the window; `lem:Slclt`'s skeleton conditioning is legitimate (rates depend only on $R$, so signs really are conditionally independent — and I re-checked that splits/merges/swaps are unambiguous while $R=0$ pair hops and all outward steps are not); `lem:tau`'s two identities, the first-passage root $\varrho = 1-\sqrt{\lambda/a}+O(\lambda)$, and the Karamata constants ($\Gamma(3/2)$ bookkeeping gives exactly $m(r)\sqrt{s/\pi a}$ ✓).
- **§6–8**: `lem:orth`'s table, `lem:eqvar`, the `prop:twophase` bracket rates (all re-derived: $a_S=1+q^2$, $a_R=1+5q^2$, $a_{SR}=\varepsilon$ on $|R|=1$ ✓), the full Bessel–Struve computation in `thm:closed` (integration by parts, boundary terms, $\pi/(8(\pi-1)c)$ ✓), and the entire $q$-Laplace theorem — telescopes, the coupling construction (valid including the entry step into contact), Fubini, $|\mathrm{Cov}(U,V)|\le\min(\mathbb EU,\mathbb EV)$.

## What the fresh eye caught (all fixed, compiles clean)

1. **One genuine logical gap** — the most important catch, in `prop:conc`: it invoked `lem:orth` (orthogonality to degree-≤1 *polynomials*) to kill the mass-≤1 components of the *REU* expansion — but the REU mass-1 functions are nonlocal, not degree-1 polynomials, so the inference didn't follow. The needed statement is true: I verified all cases by hand (the four support configurations of $V_x$ carry identical bond species-counts, so off-bond counting factors are constants and on-bond ones vanish in the alternating sum) and added the computation to `lem:orth`. The mass-≥3 contributions are now *explicitly* assigned to the deferred finite-volume item rather than silently dropped.
2. **An outright improvement to `prop:drift`**: the correction-term bound needed a uniform-in-time correlation-summability claim that was justified glibly. Cauchy–Schwarz in time reduces it to an equal-time covariance, where the product measure kills everything beyond $|x-y|\le1$ — the proof is now elementary, no duality input at all.
3. **`lem:asep` rewritten**: the Bethe-ansatz "product of factors" reading was the weakest proof in the paper; replaced with the same $R/S$-coordinate argument used everywhere else (Schütz kept as an alternative), and noted honestly that the lemma is included for completeness — the EW analysis only uses the different-species channel.
4. Smaller repairs: `lem:tridual`'s infinite-volume sentence (the observable carries right-tail counts, not bounded support — fixed via the step's superexponential far-particle bound); `thm:cov`'s "a.s." → "in probability" (what's actually proven and all that's needed); the `cor:tri` coefficient extraction now states why sector-gluing is legitimate ($|\xi_i|$ conserved by the dual generator); `prop:twophase` now says why conditioning on $A_T$ is innocuous (total variation); `lem:rebind` points to the excursion bound for re-binding episodes; the §1.4 Organisation paragraph and one abstract phrase were stale relative to the §8 restatement.

Bottom line: no false statements found; one broken inference (repaired with a real proof), one proof upgraded, one proof rewritten, and the labeled open items (`conj:cov`, the finite-volume uniformity, the mass-≥3 bookkeeping) are exactly where the paper says they are. That's as clean a bill as I can give my own work — though for the record, the same disclaimer applies recursively: items 1–3 above are now also proofs I wrote.


## 🧑 User

tell me about this logical gap in #1


## 🤖 Assistant

Here's the anatomy of it.

## What `prop:conc` needs

The cross-noise proposition controls the space-time correlation $\mathbb E_\nu[V_x(\eta_0)V_y(\eta_t)]$ by expanding $V_x$ in the orthogonal family of duality functions and applying Lemma `lem:acr`: the correlation becomes a sum over pairs of dual configurations of (coefficients) × $p_t(\xi,\xi')$. The whole point of the architecture is that the *lowest mass present* dictates the decay: a mass-1 component would propagate with the one-particle kernel ($t^{-1/2}$), only mass-2 gives the two-particle kernel ($t^{-1}$) that makes the time integral behave the way `rem:noH` advertises. So the proof must establish: **$V_x$ has zero coefficient on every dual configuration of mass ≤ 1.**

## What the proof actually invoked

The first line said "by Lemma `lem:orth`, $V_x$ has no order-≤1 component." But `lem:orth` proves $V_x \perp 1$ and $V_x\perp(\eta_{i,y}-\rho_y)$ — orthogonality to **polynomials of degree ≤ 1**.

In the *original* draft those were the same thing: the (incorrect) duality functions were the local products $\prod\kappa_1$, for which dual mass = polynomial degree, so "span of mass-≤1 duals" = "degree-≤1 polynomials" and the inference was valid. When we replaced the duality function with REU's correct one, the mass-1 function at site $w$ became

$$D(\xi_w,\eta) = 1 - \frac{1}{\alpha_i}\,\mathbf 1\{\eta_{i,w}=1\}\;q^{2\left(w+N^+_{w+1}(\eta_i)\right)},$$

which depends on the occupation at $w$ *and the total particle count to its right* — a nonlocal function of unbounded polynomial degree. So now span{mass ≤ 1} ≠ {degree ≤ 1}, and orthogonality to linear functions says nothing a priori about $\langle V_x, D(\xi_w,\cdot)\rangle$. The proof's sentence silently identified two gradings that stopped coinciding when the duality function was corrected — classic refactoring residue, and exactly the kind of thing only a from-scratch read catches, because every individual ingredient is true; it's the bridge between them that had quietly become a non sequitur.

## Why it's true anyway (the fix)

You need $\mathbb E_\nu[V_x\cdot\mathbf 1\{\eta_{i,w}\}q^{2N^+_{w+1}(\eta_i)}]=0$ for every $w$. The factor decomposes over sites: $q^{2N^+_{w+1}} = \prod_{y>w}q^{2\eta_{i,y}}$. Three cases under the product measure:

- $w > x+1$: everything is independent of the bond, and $\mathbb E_\nu[V_x]=0$ finishes it.
- $w < x$: the count reaches across the bond through the factor $q^{2(\eta_{i,x}+\eta_{i,x+1})}$. Here's the structural fact that saves the day: on all four support configurations of $V_x$ — $(3,0), (0,3), (1,2), (2,1)$ — the bond carries **exactly one particle of each species**, so $\eta_{i,x}+\eta_{i,x+1}\equiv1$ on the support and the "nonlocal" factor restricts to the constant $q^2$. Constants pull out; $\mathbb E_\nu[V_x]=0$ again.
- $w\in\{x,x+1\}$: a four-entry check of the alternating sum $f(3,0)+f(0,3)-f(1,2)-f(2,1)$ with $f=\mathbf 1\{\eta_{i,x}\}q^{2\eta_{i,x+1}}$ (values $1,0,1,0$ for species 1 and $1,0,0,1$ for species 2) or $f=\mathbf 1\{\eta_{i,x+1}\}$ — zero every time, the same $1{+}1{-}1{-}1$ cancellation that runs through the whole paper.

The physical reading is nice: $V_x$ is the noise of events that move both species *together*, and such events never change the species count seen from outside the bond — so no density-like observable, local or counting, can overlap with it. That computation is now the final paragraph of `lem:orth`, and `prop:conc`'s opening cites it properly.

## How bad would it have been?

Worth being honest about the blast radius. If a mass-1 component had actually been present, $C_\Theta(s)$ would have lost all its $s$-decay and degraded to $O(N^{-1})$ — which still gives $\mathbb E[\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\rangle^2]\lesssim t^2N^{-1}\to0$. So the *qualitative* conclusion (X), and with it the decoupling theorem, would have survived even in the worst case; what was genuinely at stake was the stated convergence rate and the paper's structural story ("the cross-noise is a two-dual-particle object, whence the integrable $s^{-1/2}$"). A gap in the load-bearing narrative more than in the destination — but a gap all the same, and unlike the others, this one was created *by our own earlier repair*: fixing the duality function upstream invalidated an inference downstream that had been fine when written.

One loose end remains, now stated rather than silent: $V_x$ does have nonzero mass-≥3 coefficients in finite volume (the counting factors prevent the exact vanishing the local basis enjoyed), and bounding their kernel contributions sits in the deferred finite-volume bookkeeping of `rem:orthstatus`, alongside the uniformity of constants.


## 🧑 User

how should we fix the gap?


## 🤖 Assistant

Good question to push on, because when I sat down to design the full repair I hit something that changes the plan. Let me lay out the state of it honestly.

## What's already fixed vs. what remains

The mass-≤1 part is done (the new computation in `lem:orth`). What remains for a complete `prop:conc` is: **(a)** the mass-≥3 contributions to the expansion of $V_x$, and **(b)** the finite-volume/window bookkeeping in which the whole expansion lives. Working through both, here's what I found.

## A new structural lemma that shrinks the problem

The same constancy mechanism that saved mass-≤1 gives more: $\langle V_x, D(\xi,\cdot)\rangle_\nu \ne 0$ forces $\xi$ to have **at least two dual particles on the bond** $\{x,x+1\}$. Reason: any $\xi$-particle off the bond contributes a factor that either doesn't see the bond at all ($w>x+1$) or sees it only through $q^{2(\eta_{i,x}+\eta_{i,x+1})}$, which is the constant $q^2$ on the support of $V_x$ (the bond always carries one particle of each species there); and if exactly *one* $\xi$-particle sits on the bond, its restricted factor has the same vanishing alternating sums as in the mass-1 case — the far particles only multiply it by constants and independent factors. So the expansion of $V_x$ is supported on $\xi$ = (two-to-four particles on the bond) ∪ (anything far), which organizes the mass-≥3 sector nicely: it's the mass-2 bond skeleton dressed by far particles. That lemma is provable today and I'd add it regardless of the rest.

## The hard part, and why it's gated

Estimating the dressed terms requires the coefficients $\langle V_x,D_\xi\rangle/a(\xi)$ — i.e., the **norms** $a(\xi)$ and the centring of the family. And here my own computations keep hitting the same wall: in the plain $L^2(\nu)$ pairing, the mass-1 function has

$$\mathbb E_\nu[D(\xi_w,\cdot)] = 1 - \frac{1}{1+t_L} = \rho_L \ne 0,$$

the density at the right edge of the box — by an exact telescoping ($q^2t_y = t_{y-1}$). So the family is *not* orthogonal to constants in the naive pairing, even inside the fugacity window — which is consistent with my earlier failed numerical orthogonality checks. I don't doubt the REU orthogonality statement; I doubt my reconstruction of its precise *form* — the pairing, possible weights, and the exact window. And there's a second tension that the precise form has to resolve: in the EW scaling the window is comfortable for boxes $L\sim KN$ (since $q^{2KN}\to1$), but a naive finite-speed comparison of the finite and infinite systems needs $L\gg TN^2$ — the two requirements are incompatible, so the volume bookkeeping has to go through the window-compatible box with a diffusive (not ballistic) boundary argument, e.g. proving (X) for the finite-volume field theorem at $L=KN$ and taking $K\to\infty$ at the level of the theorem statement.

## Recommended plan, in order

1. **Step 0 (gating, and it's yours):** pin down the exact orthogonality relation — the inner product, any weights, and the window — from REU §3.1 and the single-species references it reduces to (CFG20/FKZ22). Earlier you told me not to chase this and I deprioritized it, which was right *then*; but for this particular gap it's now load-bearing: every bookkeeping choice downstream depends on the precise form, and my $L^2(\nu)$ reconstruction is demonstrably not it. If you can state it from memory or point me at the right display in CFG20, that one input unblocks the rest.
2. **Step 1 (today, independent of Step 0):** add the support lemma above to §6.
3. **Step 2 (after Step 0):** redo the expansion with the correct norms; for the dressed mass-3/4 terms, two routes — crude kernel bounds plus coefficient smallness if the correct norms make the far-particle dressing summable, or extend the $R/S$ machinery to three and four dual particles (the binding only ever acts on different-species pairs, so the extra particles are spectators up to contact events — plausibly the same excursion analysis).
4. **Step 3:** the diffusive volume argument sketched above for the $K\to\infty$ step.

**Fallback** if Step 0 stalls: a duality-light decomposition — split $\Theta$ into its slow pair-mode component (whose autocorrelation is exactly the two-particle object `thm:kernel` already controls; pleasingly, the $N^{-1}e^{-4cs}$ atom term in the current proof *is* this slow mode) plus an orthogonal rest, which would relax fast given a spectral gap on the pair-orthogonal sector. That trades the orthogonality question for a gap estimate — a different research input, and the gap comparison degenerates with $\varepsilon$, so I'd only go there if Step 0 is truly stuck.

So: the single most useful thing you could do is tell me (or point me at) the exact orthogonality statement. Everything else in the fix is either done, doable today, or mechanical once that's in hand.
