```
    p_i^x(\xi_i,\eta_i)=\alpha_i^{-1}q^{-2\left(N_{x-1}^-(\xi_i)-N_{x+1}^+(\eta_i)\right)+2x-2}
\end{equation}
and
$\displaystyle{N_{x-1}^{-}\left(\xi_{i}\right)=\sum_{1\le y\le x-1} \xi_i^y} $ and $\displaystyle{N_{x+1}^{+}\left(\eta_{i}\right)=\sum_{x+1\le y\le L}\eta_i^y }$ denotes the number of particles in the configuration considered at the left, respectively right, of  site $x$.

$D_{\alpha_i}$ are orthogonal with respect to $\mu_{\alpha_i}$ when $\alpha_i \in(0, q^{-1+(2 L+1) })$  (see Theorem 3.2 in \cite{CFG} or Theorem 3.1 in \cite{FKZ}).



\begin{theorem}
Assume that $\alpha_1,\alpha_2 \in(0, q^{-1+(2 L+1) }).$ The type D ASEP with parameters $(q,2,0)$ or $(q,3,0)$  is self-dual with respect to the orthogonal function

\[D^L_{\alpha_1, \alpha_2}(\eta, \xi) = D^L_{\alpha_1}(\eta_1, \xi_1) \cdot D^L_{\alpha_2}(\eta_2, \xi_2).\]
\end{theorem}
\begin{remark}
    The duality function does not depend on the parameter $n$, it is believed that this Theorem still holds true for general $n$. However, we don't pursue this direction in this paper.
\end{remark}



%satisfying the following orthogonality relation:
%\[
%\langle D_\alpha(\cdot,\eta),D_\alpha(\cdot,\xi)\rangle_{\omega_\alpha^{ASEP(q,\theta)}}=\frac{\delta_{\eta,\xi}}{\omega_\alpha^{ASEP(q,\theta)}}\cdot %g_{\alpha,-1}(\eta),
%\]

%with $\omega_\alpha^{ASEP(q,\theta)}$ and $g(\eta)$ as in \cite{CFG}.





\begin{proof}
We will actually provide two proofs for this theorem, with one being probabilistic and one being algebraic.


The probabilistic proof will be based on induction on the number of sites. For the base case of $L=2$, one simply explicitly computes the multiplication of $16\times 16$ matrices. Details are omitted. 

Note that $$K_{\eta_i^x}\left(q^{-2\xi_i^x}, p_i^x(\xi_i,\eta_i),1,q^2\right)\neq 1 \text{ if and only if  }\xi_i^x=\eta_i^x=1.$$
Rewrite the duality function as 
\begin{equation*}
    D^L_{\alpha_i}(\eta, \xi) = \prod_{x \in C(\eta_i, \xi_i)} \left( 1 - \frac{q^{2(x - N_{x-1}^{-}(\xi_i) + N_{x+1}^{+}(\eta_i)}}{\alpha_i} \right),
```

```
I found the paper you're looking for. The paper is titled "q-Orthogonal dualities for asymmetric particle systems" by authors Gioia Carinci, Chiara Franceschini, and Wolter Groenevelt.

The paper studies a class of interacting particle systems with asymmetric interaction showing a self-duality property. The class includes the ASEP(q,θ), asymmetric exclusion process, with a repulsive interaction, allowing up to θ∈ℕ particles in each site, and the ASIP(q,θ), θ∈ℝ⁺, asymmetric inclusion process, that is its attractive counterpart.

The analysis leads to multivariate q-analogues of Krawtchouk polynomials and Meixner polynomials as orthogonal duality functions for the generalized asymmetric exclusion process and its asymmetric inclusion version, respectively.

The paper's arXiv identifier is **2003.07837**, and it was published in the Electronic Journal of Probability in 2021.
```

```
\section{Construction of the orthogonal dualities} \label{proofofresults}
From the analysis  developed in \cite{CGRS1} and \cite{CGRS}   the processes ASIP($q,\theta$) and ASEP($q,\theta$) are known to be self-dual with respect to self-duality functions that have a nested-product structure and  a {\em triangular} form, with triangular  meaning that they have support contained in the set of couples $(x,n)\in \Omega_L^2$ such that $n_i\le x_i$ for all $i\in \Lambda_L$.
In this section  we start   from these triangular duality-functions to construct new duality functions satisfying  suitable orthogonality relations.

\subsection{Triangular dualities}  \label{ssec:triangular dualities}

The functions
\be
\label{tria1asip}
D_{\lambda}^{\text{tr}}(x, n )= {\prod_{i=1}^L}  \frac{\binom{x_i}{n_i}_q}{\Psi_{q,\sigma}(\theta,n_i)}\,
\cdot \,
q^{x_i\left(2N^-_{i-1}(n) +n_i\right)- 2\sigma\theta  i n_i} \, \lambda^{n_i}
\ee
and
\be
\label{tria2asip}
 \widehat D_{\lambda}^{\text{tr}}( x, n )=
 {\prod_{i=1}^L} \frac{\binom{x_i}{n_i}_q}{\Psi_{q,\sigma}(\theta,n_i)}\,
\cdot \,
q^{-n_i\left(2N^-_{i-1}(x) +x_i\right)- 2\sigma\theta  i n_i} \, \lambda^{n_i}
\ee
with $\Psi$ the $q$-binomial coefficient given in \eqref{Psi}, are self-duality functions for the ASEP($q,\theta$) (for $\sigma=-1$), resp.~for ASIP($q,\theta$) (for $\sigma=+1$).
For the proof of the duality relation we refer to  \cite[Theorem 5.1]{CGRS1} for the case  $\sigma=+1$ and to  \cite[Theorem 3.2]{CGRS} for $\sigma=-1$. We notice moreover that these two functions are the same function modulo a multiplicative quantity that only depends on the total number of particles $N(x)$ and $N(n)$. {More precisely, using \eqref{N1}}, we have that
\beq
\widehat D_{\lambda}^{\text{tr}}( x, n )= q^{-2N(n)N(x)} \cdot  D_{\lambda}^{\text{tr}}( x, n ).
\eeq







\subsection{From triangular to orthogonal dualities} \label{generalresult}
The following theorem, {which is a slight generalization of \cite[Proposition 4.5]{CFGGR},} will be the key ingredient needed to produce biorthogonal duality functions from the triangular ones.

\begin{theorem}[Biorthogonal self-duality functions via scalar product] \label{prop:orthogonality}
Let $X$ be a Markov process on a countable state space $\Omega$, with generator $L$. Let $\mu_1$ and $\mu_2$ be two reversible measures for $X$,
and  $d_1$, $d_2$, $\tilde d_1$ and  $\tilde d_2$ be four self-duality functions for $X$. Suppose that
\begin{equation}\label{d12}
\langle d_1(x,\cdot), {d}_2(\cdot,n) \rangle_{\mu_1}=\dfrac{\delta_{x,n}}{\mu_2(n)} \;\qquad\text{and}\qquad\langle \tilde{d}_2(x,\cdot), \tilde{d}_1(\cdot,n) \rangle_{\mu_2}=\dfrac{\delta_{x,n}}{\mu_1(n)}
\end{equation}
for $x,n \in \Omega$. Here $\langle \, \cdot\, , \, \cdot\, \rangle_{\mu_i}$ denotes the scalar product corresponding to the measure $\mu_i$. Then the functions $D, \widetilde D : \Omega \times \Omega \to \R$ given by
\be \label{ordu}
{ D}(x,n) := \langle \tilde{d}_1(x,\cdot),  d_1(n,\cdot)\rangle_{ \mu_1} \qquad \widetilde{D}(x,n) := \langle \tilde{d}_2(\cdot,x) , d_2(\cdot,n) \rangle_{\mu_1}
\ee
are self-duality functions for $X$. Moreover, they satisfy the biorthogonality relations
\be \label{or}
\langle D(\cdot,m), \widetilde{D} (\cdot,n)  \rangle_{\mu_2} = \frac{ \delta_{m,n}}{\mu_2(n)}, \qquad m,n \in \Omega.
\ee
In particular, if $\widetilde D = c_1(x)c_2(n) D$, where $c_1$ (resp. $c_2$) is a positive function of the total number of particles (resp. dual particles), then
equation \eqref{or} becomes an orthogonality relation for $D$ with respect to the weight $c_1(x)\mu_2(x)$ and with squared norm $ \frac{ 1}{c_2(n) \mu_2(n)}$.

\end{theorem}

\bpr
Since scalar products of self-duality functions are self-duality function by \cite[Proposition 4.1]{CFGGR}, we have that both $D$ and $\widetilde{D}$ are self-duality functions. For the biorthogonality relation, assuming we can interchange the order of summation, we get
\begin{align*}
\langle D(\cdot,m), \widetilde{ D}(\cdot,n)\rangle_{\mu_2} &= \sum_{x} D(x,m) \widetilde{ D}(x,n) \mu_2(x) \\
& = \sum_{x} \left(\sum_y \tilde{d}_1(x,y)d_1(m,y)  \mu_1(y)\right) \left( \sum_z \tilde{d}_2(z,x)  d_2(z,n) \mu_1(z)\right)\mu_2(x)\\
& = \sum_{y,z} { d}_1(m,y) d_2(z,n)  \mu_1(y)\mu_1(z)\sum_x \tilde{d}_2(z,x)  \tilde{d}_1(x,y)\mu_2(x) \\
& = \sum_{y,z}  \mu_1(y)\mu_1(z) { d}_1(m,y) d_2(z,n) \, \frac{ \delta_{y,z}}{\mu_1(y)} \\
& = \sum_y { d}_1(m,y) d_2(y,n) \mu_1(y) = \frac{ \delta_{m,n}}{\mu_2(m)}.
\end{align*}
This proves the result.
\epr

\vskip.5cm
\noindent
In order  to apply this theorem to produce biorthogonal self-duality functions from the triangular ones we need to show that the triangular duality functions \eqref{tria1asip} and \eqref{tria2asip} satisfy the relations \eqref{d12}.  This property is the content of  proposition below.

\vskip.2cm
\noindent
Let $\mu_\alpha$, $\alpha\in\R\setminus\{0\}$ be the family of reversible signed measures defined in \eqref{SM}, then from now onward we will use the notation
 $\langle \, \cdot\, , \, \cdot\, \rangle_\alpha$ for the scalar product with respect to the reversible measure $\mu_\alpha$.

\bp\label{Prop1} Let $D_{\lambda}^{\textup{tr}}$ and $\widehat D_{\lambda}^{\textup{tr}}$ the functions defined in \eqref{tria1asip}-\eqref{tria2asip}, then, for all $\alpha,\beta\in \R\setminus\{0\}$  we have
 \beq
 &&\langle D_{1/{\alpha q}}^{\textup{tr}}(x,\cdot), \widehat D_{-q/\beta}^{\textup{tr}}(\cdot,n)\rangle_{-\alpha}    = \frac{\delta_{x,n}}{\mu_\beta(n)} \;.
 \eeq
\ep
\noindent
We will prove this result  in Section \ref{p5.1} only for ASEP($q,\theta$) as the proof for ASIP($q,\theta$) is similar.


\vskip.4cm
\noindent
Proposition \ref{Prop1} guarantees that the two conditions in \eqref{d12} are satisfied for the self duality functions
\[
d_{1}= D^{\text{tr}}_{1/\alpha q}, \quad \tilde d_{1}= \widehat  D^{\text{tr}}_{q/\alpha}, \quad
\quad d_{2}= \widehat D^{\text{tr}}_{-q/\beta}, \quad \tilde d_{2}= D^{\text{tr}}_{-1/\beta q} \]
by taking the scalar product with respect to the measures
\[
```

```
\label{SM}
\mu_{\alpha,\sigma}(x) = \prod_{i=1}^L\Psi_{\sigma}(\theta,x_i)\cdot  \alpha^{x_i} \, q^{2\sigma\theta  ix_i}, \qquad \text{for} \quad \alpha\in \R\setminus \{0\}
\ee
for $x\in\Omega_L=S_{\sigma,\theta}^L$.
\vskip.2cm
\noindent
  We define a modified version $\omega_{\alpha,\sigma}$ of \eqref{SM} that will appear in the statement of the main results in Section \ref{mainres}.
  This new signed measure differs from \eqref{SM} only through  multiplication  by a function of the total number of particles $N(x)$:
\beq\label{w}
\omega_{\alpha,\sigma}(x)=\frac{\mu_{\alpha,\sigma}(x)}{{\cal Z}_{\alpha,\sigma}}\cdot q^{N(x)(N(x)-1)} \cdot  (-\sigma \alpha q^{1+2N(x) +\sigma\theta(2 L+1)})_\infty
\eeq
where ${\cal Z}_{\alpha,\sigma}$ is a constant.
We remark that, as the processes conserve the total number of particles,   detailed balance condition is preserved under this operation, then  $\omega_{\alpha,\sigma}$ is  again a reversible signed measure for the processes. In order to interpret it as a probability measure we have to restrict to the case $\alpha>0$.  This condition is sufficient for the case $\sigma=+1$, while, for $\sigma=-1$ we have to impose the further condition $\alpha<q^{-1+(2L+1)\theta}$ in order to assure the positivity of the infinite $q-$shifted factorials. Under these conditions and choosing
\be
{\cal Z}_{\alpha,\sigma}:=\sum_{x}{\mu_{\alpha,\sigma}(x)}\cdot q^{N(x)(N(x)-1)} \cdot  (-\sigma \alpha q^{1+2N(x) +\sigma\theta(2 L+1)})_\infty.
\ee
$\omega_{\alpha,\sigma}$ is a reversible probability measure for the corresponding process:
\be\label{W}
\begin{array}{lll}
\omega^{\text{\tiny{ASEP($q,\theta$)}}}:=\omega_{\alpha,-1},& \text{for }  \alpha\in(0,q^{-1+(2L+1)\theta})\\
&&\\
\omega^{\text{\tiny{ASIP($q,\theta$)}}}:= \omega_{\alpha,+1},& \text{for }  \alpha \in (0, q^{-1-\theta}).\\
\end{array}
\ee
Finally we define the function:
\be\label{tw}
g_{\alpha,\sigma}(x):= \frac{q^{2N(x)(N(x)-1)}} {{\cal Z}^2_{\alpha,\sigma}}\cdot  (-\sigma \alpha q^{1+2N(x) +\sigma\theta(2 L+1)})_\infty\cdot(-\sigma\alpha q^{1-2N(x)+\sigma\theta})_\infty 
\ee
that will also appear in the statement of the main results.
%\beq\label{tw}
%\widetilde \omega_{\alpha,\sigma}(x)=\frac{\omega_{\alpha,\sigma}(x)}{g_\alpha(x)} .
%\eeq
%\wolter{For ASIP we also need $\alpha<q^{-1-\theta}$}

%\br
%Notice that, even though the measures \eqref{w}-\eqref{tw} contain infinite $q-$Pochhammer symbols, if one takes the product $\omega_{\alpha,\sigma} \times \widetilde \omega_{\alpha,\sigma}$ many of the terms in the infinite product simplify. This reduces, for the case $\sigma=-1$, the infinite product to a finite product. This property will be crucial later on in the proof of orthogonal relations for the case of ASEP$(q,\theta)$.
%\er

\section{Main Results} \label{mainres}

The main result of this paper is the proof of self-duality properties for the processes
introduced in the previous section via $q-$hypergeometric orthogonal polynomials. For each process we show the existence of a self-duality function, $D$ and another one, $\widetilde D$, that is the same modulo multiplication by a function of the total number of particles and the size of the lattice. Such duality functions can be written in terms of the  $q-$Krawtchouk polynomials (respectively $q-$Meixner polynomials) for the ASEP($q,\theta$) (respectively for the  ASIP($q,\theta$)). $D$ and  $\widetilde D$  satisfy a biorthogonality relation if one considers the scalar product with respect to the (one site) reversible measures. However, the biorthogonal relation can easily be stated as an orthogonal relation by performing the change of measure of equation \eqref{w} and the consequently change of norm in equation  \eqref{w}.
We start by recalling below the definition of duality.
\bd
\label{standard}
Let  $\{X_t\}_{t\ge0}$,  $\{\widehat{X}_t\}_{t\ge0}$ be two  Markov processes with state spaces  $\Omega$ and $\widehat{\Omega}$ and $D: \Omega\times \widehat{\Omega}\to\R$ a measurable function. The processes  $\{X_t\}_{t\ge0}$,  $\{\widehat{X}_t\}_{t\ge0}$ are said to be \textbf{dual} with respect to $D$  if
\be\label{standarddualityrelation1}
\E_x \big[D(X_t, \widehat{x})\big]=\widehat{\mathbb{E}}_{\widehat{x}} \big[D(x, \widehat{X}_t)\big]\;
\ee
for all $x\in\Omega, \  \widehat{x}\in \hat{\Omega}$ and $t>0$. Here $\E_x $ denotes the expectation with respect to the
 law of the process $\{X_t\}_{t\ge0}$  started at $x$, while $\widehat{\mathbb{E}}_{\widehat{x}} $
denotes  expectation with respect to the law of the process $\{\widehat{X}_t\}_{t\ge0}$
initialized at $\widehat{x}$. If $\{\widehat{X}_t\}_{t\ge0}$  is a copy of $\{X_t\}_{t\ge0}$, we say that the process $\{X_t\}_{t\ge0}$ is \textbf{self-dual}.
\ed



\subsection*{Orthogonal polynomial dualities for ASEP($q,\theta$)}
In this section we display the orthogonal duality function for  ASEP($q,\theta$), namely the $q-$Krawtchouk polynomials, for which we will use the following notation
\begin{equation} \label{def:q-Krawtchoukbis}
K_n(q^{-x};p,c;q):=  \rphis{2}{1}{q^{-x},q^{-n}}{q^{-c}}{q,p{q^{n+1}}},
\end{equation}
where $_{2}\phi_{1}$ is the  $q-$hypergeometric function, $c \in \N$ and $n,x \in \lbrace 0,\ldots, c \rbrace$, see Section \ref{Kraw} of the Appendix for the orthogonality relations.
The following theorem states that nested products of $q-$Krawtchouk polynomials form a family of self-duality functions for ASEP($q,\theta$).
\bt \label{teoasep}
The \textup{ASEP}($q,\theta$) on $\Lambda_L$ is  self-dual  with self-duality functions:
\beq\label{Dasep}
 &&D_\alpha^{\textup{\tiny{ASEP($q,\theta$)}}}(x,n) :=  \prod_{i =1}^L  K_{n_i}(q^{-2x_i};p_{i,\alpha}(x,n),\theta ;q^2), \qquad  \alpha\in(0,q^{-1+(2L+1)\theta}),\nn\\
&& p_{i,\alpha}(x,n):=\frac 1 {\alpha}\; q^{-2(N_{i-1}^-(x)-N^+_{i+1}(n))+\theta(2i-1)-1}
\eeq
 satisfying the following orthogonality relation
\be\label{BiOrtasep}
\langle D_\alpha^{\textup{\tiny{ASEP($q,\theta$)}}}(\cdot , x), D_{\alpha}^{\textup{\tiny{ASEP($q,\theta$)}}}(\cdot , n)\rangle_{\omega_\alpha^{\textup{\tiny{ASEP($q,\theta$)}}}}=\dfrac{\delta_{x,n}}{ \omega_\alpha^{\textup{\tiny{ASEP($q,\theta$)}}}(x)}\cdot g_{\alpha,-1}(x)
\ee
with $\omega_\alpha^{\textup{\tiny{ASEP($q,\theta$)}}}$ and $ g_{\alpha,-1}$
 defined  in \eqref{W}-\eqref{tw}.
\et
\begin{remark} \*
For $L=1$ this gives the orthogonality relations for $q-$Krawtchouk polynomials as stated in Section \ref{Kraw}, so we have obtained a family of multivariate orthogonal polynomials generalizing the $q-$Krawtchouk polynomials.
Note that the restriction  $\alpha\in(0,q^{-1+(2L+1)\theta})$ has been imposed in order to have a scalar product  \eqref{BiOrtasep} w.r. to a (positive) reversible measure, that can be eventually turned in a probability measure, after renormalization.
Note also that this is the condition required  in order to have the conditions \eqref{condK} satisfied, indeed, for $\alpha\in(0,q^{-1+(2L+1)\theta})$,
\be
\theta \in \N \qquad  \text{and} \quad q^{2\theta} \cdot p_{i,\alpha}(x,n)>1 \qquad  \text{for all} \quad  x,n\in \Omega_L, \: i \in \Lambda_L \;.
\ee
If we neglect this condition Theorem \ref{teoasep} holds still true  with the only difference that we can not guarantee the positivity of $\omega_\alpha$.
\end{remark}





\subsection*{Orthogonal polynomial dualities for ASIP($q,\theta$)}

In the same spirit of the previous section we now introduce the orthogonal duality relation for ASIP($q,\theta$). In this case we have that the self-duality functions are a nested product of $q-$Meixner polynomials
\beq \label{q-Meixnerbis}
M_n(q^{-x};b,c;q):=  \rphis{2}{1}{q^{-x},q^{-n}}{bq}{q,-\frac{q^{n+1}}{c}}, \qquad \text{for} \quad x,n \in \N,
\eeq
see Section \ref{Meix} in the Appendix for more details and orthogonality relations. The following theorem is the analogue of the previous one; it says that a family of nested $q-$Meixner polynomials are self-duality functions for ASIP($q,\theta$).
\bt \label{teoasip}
The \textup{ASIP}($q,\theta$) on $\Lambda_L$ is  self-dual  with  self-duality functions
\beq\label{D}
&& D_\alpha^{\textup{\tiny{ASIP($q,\theta$)}}}(x,n) :=  \prod_{i =1}^L M_{n_i}(q^{-2x_i};q^{2(\theta -1)}, c_{i,\alpha}(x,n);q^2), \qquad \alpha>0\nn\\
&&
 c_{i,\alpha}(x,n):=\alpha q^{2(N_{i-1}^-(x)-N^+_{i+1}(n))+\theta (2i-1)+1},
\eeq
for all  $\alpha\in (0,q^{-1-\theta})$, satisfying the following orthogonality relations
```
</details>

```
\subsubsection*{The $q-$Pochhammer symbol}
For $a\in \R$ and $m\in \N$ the $q-$Pochhammer symbol, or $q-$shifted factorial, $(a;q)_m$ is defined by
\be\label{Poch}
(a;q)_{m} = (1-a)(1-aq^1)\cdots (1-aq^{m-1})\;, \quad \text{for} \quad m\ge 1 \quad \text{and} \quad (a;q)_0=1 
\ee
and furthermore,
\be\label{Poch1}
(a;q)_\infty:= \prod_{k=0}^{\infty} \left( 1- aq^{k}\right) \;.
\ee
```

## 🤖 Assistant

**Verified to machine precision** — relative off-diagonals at $10^{-17}$ and the diagonal matching $G/\Omega$ to a constant at $10^{-15}$, for the two-species type D function at $n=\infty$, on $L=2$ and $3$, three parameter sets. And the test settles the orientation, which turns out to be the punchline. Here is the exact statement, in our notation:

$$\boxed{\;\sum_{\eta}\,\omega_{\alpha_1}(\eta_1)\,\omega_{\alpha_2}(\eta_2)\;\bar D(\xi,\eta)\,\bar D(\xi',\eta)\;=\;\delta_{\xi,\xi'}\;\prod_{i=1,2}\frac{g_{\alpha_i}(\xi_i)}{\omega_{\alpha_i}(\xi_i)}\;}$$

where (CFG Theorem 3.2 / eqs. (W),(tw) at $\theta=1$, window $\alpha_i\in(0,q^{2L})$):

- $\omega_\alpha(\zeta) \propto \mu_\alpha(\zeta)\cdot q^{N(N-1)}\cdot(\alpha q^{2N-2L};q^2)_\infty$, $N=N(\zeta)$ — the blocking measure **reweighted by a function of the conserved particle number** (hence still reversible);
- $g_\alpha(\zeta) \propto q^{2N(N-1)}(\alpha q^{2N-2L};q^2)_\infty(\alpha q^{-2N};q^2)_\infty$;
- and — the subtlety that defeated every earlier check — $\bar D$ is the REU function read with **the process configuration in the $N^-$ slot and the dual in the $N^+$ slot**: $\bar D(\xi,\eta)=\prod(1-q^{2(x-N^-_{x-1}(\eta_i)+N^+_{x+1}(\xi_i))}/\alpha_i)$. Both readings satisfy the duality (self-duality is transpose-symmetric), but only this orientation is orthogonal when summed over the process variable.

Three consequences, each substantial:

1. **`lem:acr` gets its exact hypothesis**: pairing measure $\omega$ (reversible ✓), norms $a(\xi) = \prod_i g_{\alpha_i}(\xi_i)/\omega_{\alpha_i}(\xi_i)$ — this is literally CFG's two-time correlation theorem, which is our `lem:acr` verbatim.
2. **The infinite-volume degeneration dissolves.** In the correct orientation the process configuration enters through $N^-(\eta_i)$ — particles to the **left** — which is a.s. *finite* under the blocking measure on $\mathbb Z$ (densities vanish leftward). My "the functions degenerate to 1 on $\mathbb Z$" caution applied to the wrong orientation; the transpose family is nondegenerate exactly where regime A lives. (And my earlier "no mirrored family exists" finding was about reflecting the *lattice* — the right move was transposing the *slots*, which is free.)
3. **The window is harmless in the EW scaling**: $\alpha<q^{2L}$ with $q=1-c/N^2$, $L=KN$ gives $\alpha< e^{-2cK/N}\to1$.

So Step 0 of the gap-fix plan is done, with the statement verified rather than transcribed on faith. What remains for `prop:conc` is now fully concrete and mechanical-looking: redo the expansion in $\bar D$ with the $\omega$-pairing (the $N$-sector reweighting commutes with the dynamics, which is what makes it bookkeeping rather than analysis), the support lemma (≥2 dual particles on the bond), and the mass-≥3 estimates with the now-explicit norms. Let me save the verification script and record the statement in the draft's `rem:orthstatus` — then the remaining work has no unknowns left in it, just pages. Want me to push on and write the corrected expansion into §6 next?

**⚙️ Bash**

```json
{
  "command": "python3 - <<'EOF'\nimport numpy as np\nL = 4\ndef run(q, a1, a2):\n    q2 = q*q\n    alphas = (a1, a2)\n    def qpoch(a, K=2000): return np.prod(1 - a * q2**np.arange(K))\n    def site(c, x): return (c >> (2*(x-1))) & 3\n    def occ(c, x, i): return (site(c, x) >> i) & 1\n    def omega_sp(csp, alpha):\n        occs = [(csp >> (x-1)) & 1 for x in range(1, L+1)]\n        N = sum(occs)\n        mu = np.prod([(alpha*q**(-2*x))**occs[x-1] for x in range(1, L+1)])\n        return mu * q**(N*(N-1)) * qpoch(alpha*q**(2*N-2*L))\n    W = np.zeros(4**L)\n    for c in range(4**L):\n        c1 = sum(occ(c,x,0) << (x-1) for x in range(1,L+1))\n        c2 = sum(occ(c,x,1) << (x-1) for x in range(1,L+1))\n        W[c] = omega_sp(c1, a1) * omega_sp(c2, a2)\n    W /= W.sum()\n    xb = 2\n    def V(c):\n        a, b = site(c, xb), site(c, xb+1)\n        return {(3,0):1.0, (0,3):q**4, (1,2):-q2, (2,1):-q2}.get((a,b), 0.0)\n    def Dbar(xi, c):\n        v = 1.0\n        for (w, i) in xi:\n            if occ(c, w, i) == 1:\n                Nm = sum(occ(c, y, i) for y in range(1, w))\n                Np = sum(1 for (w2,i2) in xi if i2 == i and w2 > w)\n                v *= 1 - q**(2*(w - Nm + Np)) / alphas[i]\n        return v\n    def ip(xi): return sum(W[c]*V(c)*Dbar(xi, c) for c in range(4**L) if V(c) != 0.0)\n    def norm2(xi): return sum(W[c]*Dbar(xi, c)**2 for c in range(4**L))\n    # normalized coefficient mass: c_xi^2 * a(xi) = <V,D>^2 / ||D||^2\n    pair = [(2,0),(2,1)]\n    dressed = [[(2,0),(2,1),(1,0)], [(2,0),(2,1),(1,1)], [(2,0),(3,1),(1,0)],\n               [(1,0),(1,1),(2,0),(2,1)]]\n    m_pair = ip(pair)**2 / norm2(pair)\n    m_dr = sum(ip(xi)**2 / norm2(xi) for xi in dressed)\n    Vn2 = sum(W[c]*V(c)**2 for c in range(4**L))\n    return m_pair, m_dr, Vn2\n\nprint(f\"{'q':>6} {'alpha':>12} {'pair mass':>12} {'dressed mass(4 cfgs)':>20} {'ratio dr/pair':>14}\")\nfor (q, a1, a2) in [(0.7, 0.03, 0.02), (0.9, 0.15, 0.1), (0.95, 0.3, 0.2),\n                    (0.99, 0.4, 0.3), (0.999, 0.4, 0.3)]:\n    mp, md, vn = run(q, a1, a2)\n    print(f\"{q:>6} ({a1},{a2})  {mp:12.4e} {md:20.4e} {md/mp:14.4e}\")\nEOF",
  "description": "Check dressed coefficient mass shrinks as q approaches 1",
  "timeout": 300000
}
```

```json
  "old_string": "\\begin{remark}[orthogonality]\\label{rem:orthstatus}\nThe functions \\eqref{eq:Dreu} are orthogonal with respect to the blocking measure in\nthe fugacity window of \\cite[\\S3.1]{REU}, by reduction to the single--species\n$q$--Krawtchouk orthogonality cited there; this supplies the hypothesis of\nLemma~\\ref{lem:acr} for \\eqref{eq:Dreu}, with $a(\\xi)$ the corresponding squared\nnorms. One caution for regime (A): under $\\nu$ on $\\Z$ the counting factor\n$q^{2N^+(\\eta)}$ vanishes almost surely (the blocking densities tend to $1$ on the\nright), so the functions \\eqref{eq:Dreu} degenerate in infinite volume; the expansion\nbehind Proposition~\\ref{prop:conc} is therefore to be read in finite volume $[-L,L]$,\nwith $L\\to\\infty$ taken on the correlation functions themselves (which converge by\nfinite propagation speed), the uniformity of the constants being deferred to the\nfinal version.   "new_string": "\\begin{remark}[the exact orthogonality relation]\\label{rem:orthstatus}\nThe precise orthogonality satisfied by the type D duality functions is the\ntwo--point, two--species specialisation of \\cite[Thm.~3.2]{CFG20}, the\nsingle--species input cited in \\cite[\\S3.1]{REU}. On a finite lattice $\\Lambda$ of\n$|\\Lambda|$ sites define the \\emph{sector--reweighted} blocking measure and norm\nfunctions ($N=N(\\zeta)$ the particle number, all up to normalisation)\n\\begin{equation}\\label{eq:omegadef}\n  \\varpi_\\alpha(\\zeta)\\ \\propto\\ \\mu_\\alpha(\\zeta)\\,q^{N(N-1)}\\,\n  \\big(\\alpha q^{2N-2|\\Lambda|};q^2\\big)_\\infty,\\quad\n  g_\\alpha(\\zeta)\\ \\propto\\ q^{2N(N-1)}\n  \\big(\\alpha q^{2N-2|\\Lambda|};q^2\\big)_\\infty\\big(\\alpha q^{-2N};q^2\\big)_\\infty,\n\\end{equation}\nwith window $\\alpha\\in(0,q^{2|\\Lambda|})$, and let $\\bar D$ denote \\eqref{eq:Dreu}\nread with the \\emph{process} configuration in the $N^-$ slot and the dual in the\n$N^+$ slot,\n\\[\n  \\bar D(\\xi,\\eta)=\\prod_{i=1,2}\\ \\prod_{x:\\,\\xi_{i,x}=\\eta_{i,x}=1}\n  \\Big(1-\\frac{q^{2\\left(x-N^-_{x-1}(\\eta_i)+N^+_{x+1}(\\xi_i)\\right)}}{\\alpha_i}\\Big);\n\\]\ntransposing the interlacing of Theorem~\\ref{thm:dual}(ii), $\\bar D$ is again a\nself--duality function. Then\n\\begin{equation}\\label{eq:orthexact}\n  \\sum_\\eta \\varpi_{\\alpha_1}(\\eta_1)\\,\\varpi_{\\alpha_2}(\\eta_2)\\,\n  \\bar D(\\xi,\\eta)\\,\\bar D(\\xi',\\eta)\\ =\\ \\delta_{\\xi,\\xi'}\\,a(\\xi),\\qquad\n  a(\\xi)=\\prod_{i=1,2}\\frac{g_{\\alpha_i}(\\xi_i)}{\\varpi_{\\alpha_i}(\\xi_i)},\n\\end{equation}\nwhich we have verified to machine precision for the $n=\\infty$ rates on two and\nthree sites (off--diagonals and the norm formula). Three observations. (i) The\nreweighting in \\eqref{eq:omegadef} depends only on the conserved particle numbers,\nso $\\varpi:=\\varpi_{\\alpha_1}\\otimes\\varpi_{\\alpha_2}$ is again reversible, and\nLemma~\\ref{lem:acr} applies with $(\\varpi,\\bar D,a)$. (ii) In the orientation\n$\\bar D$ the process enters through the \\emph{left} counts $N^-(\\eta_i)$, which are\nalmost surely finite under $\\nu$ on $\\Z$: the degeneration that affects\n\\eqref{eq:Dreu} in infinite volume (where $q^{2N^+(\\eta)}=0$ a.s.) does not occur ---\nthe resolution is to transpose the slots, not to reflect the lattice, which is\nimpossible (the reflected generator fails the interlacing, consistently with the\nreflection corresponding to the non--stochastic continuation $n<n_{\\mathrm{crit}}$\nof Remark~\\ref{rem:range}). (iii) In the regime (A) scaling, $q=1-c/N^2$ on\n$|\\Lambda|=O(N)$ sites, the window is asymptotically $\\alpha_i<1$ (densities below\n$\\tfrac12$; the complementary case by particle--hole symmetry) and the reweighting\nis bounded above and below by constants (Lemma~\\ref{lem:sector}). The remaining\ninfinite--volume step --- replacing $[-KN,KN]$ by $\\Z$ in the correlation functions\n--- is deferred to the final version. In regime (B) we use the triangular duality\nof Corollary~\\ref{cor:tri} instead.\n\\end{remark}"
}
```

```json
  "old_string": "\\emph{Orthogonality to the mass-$\\le1$ duality functions.} Since the mass--one\nfunctions \\eqref{eq:Dreu} are nonlocal, the polynomial statement above does not by\nitself give $\\langle V_x,D(\\xi,\\cdot)\\rangle_\\nu=0$ for $|\\xi|\\le1$; we check it\ndirectly (in any finite volume).   "new_string": "\\emph{Orthogonality and support in the exact pairing.} The expansion of $V_x$ used\nbelow is in the family $\\bar D$ with the pairing\n$\\langle\\cdot,\\cdot\\rangle_\\varpi$ of Remark~\\ref{rem:orthstatus}; since the\nmass--one functions $\\bar D$ are nonlocal, the polynomial statement above does not by\nitself locate the expansion, and we check directly. The key structural fact: on the\nfour support configurations of $V_x$ the bond carries exactly one particle of each\nspecies, so the particle numbers $(N_1,N_2)$ --- hence the sector--reweighting\nfactors of \\eqref{eq:omegadef} --- agree on all four, and the master identity\n$\\E_\\varpi[V_xf]=\\sum_r\\widetilde\\varpi(r)\\,\\nu(3,0)\\big[f(3,0)+f(0,3)-f(1,2)-f(2,1)\\big](r)$\npersists, with $\\widetilde\\varpi$ the reweighted measure on the configuration $r$\noff the bond and the bracket evaluated at fixed $r$. The expansion of $V_x$ is therefore supported on\n$\\xi$ consisting of one different--species dual pair on the bond, possibly dressed\nby further particles off the bond; numerically (four sites, machine precision) the\ndressing is moreover one--sided --- every coefficient with a dual particle strictly\nto the \\emph{right} of the bond vanishes, reflecting the nested structure of the\nfamily \\eqref{eq:orthexact}, in which the factor of the rightmost dual particle is\nconditionally centred given the configuration to its left.\n\\end{proof}"
```

```json
{
  "replace_all": false,
  "file_path": "/Users/kuan.44/Documents/June_Edinburgh_Project/typeD_decoupling-draft.tex",
  "old_string": "are bounded, so the double sum is $\\le C\\sum_x\\varphi'(\\tfrac xN)^4\\le CN$ (a Riemann\nsum). The prefactor $N^{-2}$ gives the claim.\n\\end{proof}\n\n\\begin{proposition}[$L^2$ concentration of the cross bracket]\\label{prop:conc}\n$\\E_\\nu[\\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\\rangle(\\varphi,t)^2]\\le\nC(\\varphi)\\,\\big(t^{3/2}N^{-2}+t\\,c^{-1}N^{-1}\\big)\\to0$;\nhence $\\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\\rangle(\\varphi,t)\\to0$ in $L^2$, establishing \\textup{(X)}.\n\\end{proposition}\n\\begin{proof}\nLet $C_\\Theta(s)=\\E_\\nu[\\Theta^N(\\eta_0)\\Theta^N(\\eta_{sN^2})]$. By stationarity,\n\\begin{equation}\\label{eq:concstat}\n  \\E_\\nu\\Big[\\Big(\\int_0^t\\Theta^N\\dd s\\Big)^2\\Big]=2\\int_0^t(t-s)C_\\Theta(s)\\dd s\n  \\le 2t\\int_0^t C_\\Theta(s)\\dd s.\n\\end{equation}\nBy Lemma~\\ref{lem:orth} (final part), $V_x$ is orthogonal to the duality functions of\nmass $\\le1$, so in the finite--volume expansion of Remark~\\ref{rem:orthstatus} its\nspace--time two--point function is carried by duals of mass $\\ge2$; the mass--two\ncontribution is bounded as follows by Lemma~\\ref{lem:acr} and\nTheorem~\\ref{thm:kernel}, while the mass--$\\ge3$ contributions belong to the deferred\nbookkeeping of Remark~\\ref{rem:orthstatus}. For the mass--two part,\n\\begin{equation}\\label{eq:concbd}\n  \\big|\\E_\\nu[V_x(\\eta_0)V_y(\\eta_{sN^2})]\\big|\\le C\\,p_{sN^2}(\\xi_x,\\xi_y),\n\\end{equation}\n$\\xi_z$ the order--two configuration at $z$. Summing over $x$ with $\\sum_x\\varphi'(\\tfrac xN)^4\\le CN$\nand reinstating $N^{-2}$,\n\\begin{equation}\\label{eq:Ctheta}\n  |C_\\Theta(s)|\\le C\\min\\!\\big(N^{-1},\\,N^{-2}s^{-1/2}\\big)\\;+\\;C\\,N^{-1}e^{-4cs}.\n\\end{equation}\nThe second term is the bound--state part of $p_t$, and it is \\emph{larger} than the\ncontinuum term by a factor $N$ (consistently with Remark~\\ref{rem:boundstate}): summing\nthe atom of \\eqref{eq:kernel} over $y$ costs the full $S$--spread,\n$\\sum_y p_{sN^2}(\\xi_x,\\xi_y)\\bone\\{R(\\xi_y)=0\\}=\\PP\\big(R(sN^2)=0\\big)\\le\nC(N\\sqrt s)^{-1}+e^{-\\nu_{\\mathrm{sp}}sN^2}$, and\n$\\nu_{\\mathrm{sp}}sN^2=4cs(1+o(1))$, so at macroscopic times the damping is only\n$e^{-4cs}=\\Theta(1)$; multiplying by $N^{-2}\\sum_x\\varphi'(\\tfrac xN)^4\\le CN^{-1}$\ngives the second term of \\eqref{eq:Ctheta}. Splitting the first term at $s=N^{-2}$ and\nintegrating the second,\n$\\int_0^t C_\\Theta\\le C\\big(N^{-3}+N^{-2}\\sqrt t+(4cN)^{-1}\\big)$; feeding this into\n\\eqref{eq:concstat} gives the claim.\n\\end{proof}",
  "new_string": "are bounded, so the double sum is $\\le C\\sum_x\\varphi'(\\tfrac xN)^4\\le CN$ (a Riemann\nsum). The prefactor $N^{-2}$ gives the claim.\n\\end{proof}\n\nThe expansion of Remark~\\ref{rem:orthstatus} controls correlations under the\nreweighted measure $\\varpi$; the following comparison transfers them to $\\nu$.\n\n\\begin{lemma}[sector comparison]\\label{lem:sector}\nOn $\\Lambda=[-KN,KN]$ with $q=1-c/N^2$ and $\\alpha_1,\\alpha_2$ fixed in $(0,1)$, the\nmeasures $\\nu$ and $\\varpi$ of Remark~\\ref{rem:orthstatus} have the same conditional\nlaws given the conserved pair $(N_1,N_2)$, and their sector weights are comparable:\n$M:=\\sup_{N_1,N_2}\\nu(N_1,N_2)/\\varpi(N_1,N_2)\\le C(c,K,\\alpha)$, uniformly in $N$.\nConsequently, for all $f,h\\in L^2$ and $t\\ge0$,\n\\[\n  \\big|\\E_\\nu[f(\\eta_0)\\,h(\\eta_t)]\\big|\\ \\le\\ M\\,\n  \\E_\\varpi[f(\\eta_0)f(\\eta_t)]^{1/2}\\,\\E_\\varpi[h(\\eta_0)h(\\eta_t)]^{1/2}.\n\\]\n\\end{lemma}\n\\begin{proof}\nThe two measures differ by the factor $h_1(N_1)h_2(N_2)$ of \\eqref{eq:omegadef}\n(times constants), so the conditionals agree, and the ratio of sector weights is\ncontrolled by $h_i$: $q^{N(N-1)}\\ge q^{|\\Lambda|^2}=e^{-4cK^2(1+o(1))}$, and\n$1\\ge(\\alpha q^{2N-2|\\Lambda|};q^2)_\\infty\\ge(\\alpha';q^2)_\\infty>0$ with\n$\\alpha'=\\alpha q^{-2|\\Lambda|}=\\alpha e^{4cK/N(1+o(1))}\\le\\tfrac{1+\\alpha}2<1$ for\n$N$ large; so the reweighting lies in $[C^{-1},1]$ and $M\\le C(c,K,\\alpha)$. For the\ncorrelation bound, condition on the sector: the restricted semigroup is\nself--adjoint and positive with respect to the canonical measure (it is the square\nof the self--adjoint $P_{t/2}$), so\n$|\\langle f,P_th\\rangle_{\\mathrm{can}}|\\le\n\\langle f,P_tf\\rangle_{\\mathrm{can}}^{1/2}\\langle h,P_th\\rangle_{\\mathrm{can}}^{1/2}$.\nSumming over sectors with weights $\\nu(N_1,N_2)$, Cauchy--Schwarz on the sector sum,\nand replacing the $\\nu$--weights by $\\varpi$--weights at the cost of $M$ (the\nsummands $\\langle f,P_tf\\rangle_{\\mathrm{can}}$ being nonnegative) gives the claim.\n\\end{proof}\n\n\\begin{lemma}[the dressed mass is asymptotically negligible]\\label{lem:eps}\nWrite $V_z=V_z^{(2)}+V_z^{(\\mathrm{dr})}$ for the decomposition of $V_z$ in the\nfamily \\eqref{eq:orthexact} into its four different--species bond--pair components\nand the dressed remainder (Lemma~\\ref{lem:orth}). In the regime (A) scaling there is\n$\\eps_N\\to0$ with $\\|V^{(\\mathrm{dr})}_z\\|^2_{L^2(\\varpi)}\\le\\eps_N$, uniformly over\n$z$ in the field window.\n\\end{lemma}\n\\begin{proof}[Proof sketch; details deferred]\nTwo ingredients. (i) The dressing is one--sided (Lemma~\\ref{lem:orth}): only\nparticles strictly to the left of the bond occur. (ii) Over the field window the\ncounting factors of $\\bar D$ satisfy $q^{-2N^-_{w-1}(\\eta_i)}=1+O(N^{-1})$\nuniformly, so the family deviates from its homogeneous local limit --- in which the\ndressed coefficients vanish identically --- perturbatively. Numerically the dressed\nmass decays rapidly as $q\\to1$ at fixed window--scaled fugacities (the ratio of\ndressed to bond--pair mass falls from $7\\cdot10^{-2}$ at $q=0.7$ to $5\\cdot10^{-5}$\nat $q=0.999$ on four sites); we expect $\\eps_N=O(N^{-1})$ or better, and only\n$\\eps_N\\to0$ is used below.\n\\end{proof}\n\n\\begin{proposition}[$L^2$ concentration of the cross bracket]\\label{prop:conc}\n$\\E_\\nu[\\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\\rangle(\\varphi,t)^2]\\le\nC(\\varphi,c)\\,t\\,\\big(N^{-1}+N^{-2}\\log(tN^2)+t\\,\\eps_N\\big)\\to0$, with $\\eps_N$ as\nin Lemma~\\ref{lem:eps}; hence $\\langle M_1^N,M_2^N\\rangle(\\varphi,t)\\to0$ in $L^2$,\nestablishing \\textup{(X)}.\n\\end{proposition}\n\\begin{proof}\nLet $C_\\Theta(s)=\\E_\\nu[\\Theta^N(\\eta_0)\\Theta^N(\\eta_{sN^2})]$. By stationarity,\n\\begin{equation}\\label{eq:concstat}\n  \\E_\\nu\\Big[\\Big(\\int_0^t\\Theta^N\\dd s\\Big)^2\\Big]=2\\int_0^t(t-s)C_\\Theta(s)\\dd s\n  \\le 2t\\int_0^t C_\\Theta(s)\\dd s.\n\\end{equation}\nWork on $\\Lambda=[-KN,KN]$ in the setting of Remark~\\ref{rem:orthstatus}, $K$ fixed\n(the replacement of the infinite system by $\\Lambda$ is the deferred step recorded\nthere). By Lemma~\\ref{lem:sector},\n\\[\n  \\big|\\E_\\nu[V_x(\\eta_0)V_y(\\eta_u)]\\big|\\ \\le\\ M\\,G(x,u)^{1/2}\\,G(y,u)^{1/2},\n  \\qquad G(z,u):=\\E_\\varpi[V_z(\\eta_0)V_z(\\eta_u)]\\ \\ge0 .\n\\]\nSplit $V_z=V^{(2)}_z+V^{(\\mathrm{dr})}_z$ as in Lemma~\\ref{lem:eps}. The dual\ndynamics conserves the particle numbers $(|\\xi_1|,|\\xi_2|)$, so the mass sectors of\nthe expansion are invariant under $P_u$ and the cross terms vanish:\n$G=\\E_\\varpi[V^{(2)}P_uV^{(2)}]+\\E_\\varpi[V^{(\\mathrm{dr})}P_uV^{(\\mathrm{dr})}]$.\nFor the first part, Lemma~\\ref{lem:acr} (with $\\varpi,\\bar D,a$) gives\n$\\E_\\varpi[V^{(2)}_zP_uV^{(2)}_z]=\\sum_{\\xi,\\xi'}c_\\xi c_{\\xi'}\\,p_u(\\xi,\\xi')\\,a(\\xi')$,\na sum over at most sixteen pairs of different--species bond configurations with\ncoefficients and norms bounded in the window, each kernel entry bounded by\nTheorem~\\ref{thm:kernel}; hence\n$\\E_\\varpi[V^{(2)}_zP_uV^{(2)}_z]\\le\nC\\big[(1+u)^{-1}+e^{-\\nu_{\\mathrm{sp}}u}(1+u)^{-1/2}\\big]$. For the dressed part,\n$P_u$ is an $L^2(\\varpi)$ contraction, so\n$\\E_\\varpi[V^{(\\mathrm{dr})}_zP_uV^{(\\mathrm{dr})}_z]\\le\\eps_N$ by\nLemma~\\ref{lem:eps}. With $u=sN^2$, $\\nu_{\\mathrm{sp}}sN^2=4cs(1+o(1))$, and\n$\\sum_x\\varphi'(\\tfrac xN)^2\\le C(\\varphi)N$,\n\\begin{equation}\\label{eq:Ctheta}\n  |C_\\Theta(s)|\\ \\le\\ \\frac MN{}^{\\!2}\\Big(\\sum_x\\varphi'(\\tfrac xN)^2G(x,sN^2)^{1/2}\\Big)^{\\!2}\n  \\ \\le\\ C\\Big[\\frac1{sN^2}+\\frac{e^{-4cs}}{N\\sqrt s}+\\eps_N\\Big]\n\\end{equation}\nfor $s\\ge N^{-2}$, while $|C_\\Theta(s)|\\le CN^{-1}$ always (Lemma~\\ref{lem:eqvar}).\nIntegrating, $\\int_0^tC_\\Theta\\le\nC\\big(N^{-2}(1+\\log(tN^2))+c^{-1/2}N^{-1}+t\\,\\eps_N\\big)$, and \\eqref{eq:concstat}\ngives the claim.\n\\end{proof}"
}
```

## 🤖 Assistant

Done — the gap-fix is executed end to end. What went into the draft:

## The exact relation, found and verified

The orthogonality statement came out of the REU source itself (a commented-out display pointing to CFG arXiv:2003.07837), and its precise form explains every earlier failure: the pairing measure is the **sector-reweighted** blocking measure $\varpi_\alpha \propto \mu_\alpha\, q^{N(N-1)}(\alpha q^{2N-2L};q^2)_\infty$, the norms are $g_\alpha/\varpi_\alpha$, the window is $\alpha<q^{2L}$ — and, decisively, the **orientation**: the relation holds with the process configuration in the $N^-$ slot. I verified it to machine precision for the type D model at $n=\infty$ on 2 and 3 sites (off-diagonals at $10^{-17}$, norms matching to $10^{-15}$). Two structural payoffs came free:

- **The infinite-volume degeneration dissolves**: in the correct orientation the process enters through *left* counts, a.s. finite under $\nu$ on $\mathbb Z$. (The fix was transposing the slots, not reflecting the lattice.)
- **In the EW scaling the reweighting is uniformly harmless**: $q^{N(N-1)} \ge e^{-4cK^2}$ on $|\Lambda| = O(N)$ sites, window asymptotically just $\alpha<1$.

## The rebuilt §6

- `rem:orthstatus` now states the exact relation (`eq:orthexact`) with $\bar D$, $\varpi$, $g$; `lem:acr` is generalized to the $\varpi$-pairing; CFG20 added to the bibliography.
- `lem:orth`'s final part redone in the correct pairing — same alternating-sum mechanism, and it now also proves the **support theorem**: the expansion of $V_x$ consists of different-species bond pairs, dressed only by off-bond particles. Numerics found a bonus: the dressing is strictly **one-sided** (any dual particle right of the bond kills the coefficient — the rightmost factor of the nested family is conditionally centred), recorded with the verification.
- **New `lem:sector`**: $\nu$ and $\varpi$ share conditionals given $(N_1,N_2)$, sector weights comparable uniformly in $N$, whence $|\mathbb E_\nu[fP_th]| \le M\,\mathbb E_\varpi[fP_tf]^{1/2}\mathbb E_\varpi[hP_th]^{1/2}$ via per-sector positivity of $P_t$ — this is the bridge that transfers the duality-controlled $\varpi$-correlations to the $\nu$-stationary process, fully proved.
- **New `lem:eps`**: the dressed mass $\varepsilon_N\to0$ — the *single* remaining deferred estimate, with a two-ingredient sketch and strong numerics (dressed/pair ratio falls from $7{\times}10^{-2}$ at $q=0.7$ to $5{\times}10^{-5}$ at $q=0.999$).
- **`prop:conc` rebuilt** on these: sector comparison → mass-graded expansion (cross terms vanish because the dual conserves particle numbers) → bond-pair part via `thm:kernel`, dressed part via $L^2$-contraction. Final bound $C(\varphi,c)\,t(N^{-1}+N^{-2}\log(tN^2)+t\varepsilon_N)\to0$.

Compiles clean; `rem:noH` and the status paragraph updated to match. The ledger for regime A is now: everything proved except `lem:eps`'s details (a perturbative estimate with numerical support and a clear route) and the $[-KN,KN]\to\mathbb Z$ step — both named, both bounded. That's the gap from your referee question closed as far as it can be without those two write-ups.

Two genuine items surfaced when I asked myself that question seriously — one small correctness gap in something I wrote yesterday, one administrative. Let me fix them, then give you the verdict.

First: in `rem:orthstatus` I claimed densities above $\tfrac12$ are handled "by particle–hole symmetry." Checking it properly just now: the $n=\infty$ table is invariant under particle–hole *composed with lattice reflection* (I verified all twelve channels map correctly), which flips **both** species' densities. So $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$ both below or both above $\tfrac12$ are covered, but the *mixed* case $\rho_1<\tfrac12<\rho_2$ is not reached by the window plus symmetry — that's an honest scope restriction of the finite-volume orthogonality route that the draft should state rather than paper over:

## What I just fixed (last items I could find)

1. The "particle–hole symmetry" claim in `rem:orthstatus` was imprecise and hid a real scope restriction: the symmetry of the rate table is particle–hole *composed with reflection* (I verified all twelve channels), which flips both species at once — so the exact-orthogonality route covers $\rho_1,\rho_2$ both below or both above $\tfrac12$, and the **mixed case is now honestly flagged as deferred** (with the signed-measure remark in CFG as the likely route).
2. Added a sentence to the Status paragraph promising the verification scripts as ancillary files, since six proofs now cite them.

Beyond that, everything I can see left to do is either already a named deferred item in the draft or requires you, not me.

## What reviewers should check hardest (in order)

1. **`thm:dual`(ii) + `cor:tri`** — the $n=\infty$ duality and the sector-gluing coefficient extraction. The base case is computer-verified; a human should sanity-check that REU's induction really only uses the two-site case and the fugacity-shift covariance, as claimed.
2. **`lem:sector`** — new, short, load-bearing for all of regime A.
3. **The `lem:orth` exact-pairing computation and `prop:conc`'s assembly** — newest mathematics in the paper, written this week.
4. **`lem:Rlclt` and `lem:tau`** — rewritten probabilistic arguments; the excursion bookkeeping deserves an independent eye.
5. **`thm:cov`** ($q$-Laplace) — the coupling construction and the Fubini justifications.

## The known-open ledger to hand them up front

`lem:eps` (perturbative dressed-mass estimate — sketch plus strong numerics), the $[-KN,KN]\to\mathbb Z$ step, the mixed-density case, `lem:gauss`'s blocking-vs-Bernoulli comparison ("routine, omitted"), `conj:cov` with its open constant, and finite-$n$ joint statements resting on REU's Remark 4. Every one is flagged in place — a reviewer should find no silent gaps, only labeled ones.

## Only you can do

The author block is still "(working draft — full version)"; the `revision_checks/` scripts need packaging if you want them as actual ancillary files (I'd include the five `check_*.py` plus `typeD_mc.c`; the MC output files and binaries can go); and the framing call on whether `conj:cov` stays a conjecture or you hold the paper while someone attacks the $q$-moment tower.

One process suggestion for the manual review: give your reviewers the *old* draft too (it's in `archive/`). Several results changed statement — `thm:cov` most of all — and a reviewer who diffs the two will check exactly the places where the mathematics moved, which is where errors live.

```
262	
263	\begin{definition}[orthonormal local basis]\label{def:D}
264	For a dual configuration $\xi$ specifying which (site, species) pairs carry a dual
265	particle, set
266	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Dfac}
267	  D^{\mathrm{loc}}(\xi,\eta)=\prod_{(x,i):\,\xi_{i,x}=1}\kappa_1(\eta_{i,x}),
268	\end{equation}
269	a polynomial in $\eta$ of degree $|\xi|$ (the dual mass). By the product structure of
270	$\nu$ and the single--site orthonormality of \eqref{eq:d1}, the family
271	$\{D^{\mathrm{loc}}(\xi,\cdot)\}$ is orthonormal in $L^2(\nu)$. It is the natural
272	basis for the fluctuation fields: mass--one elements are the centred density fields,
273	and the different--species mass--two element at one site is the bound--pair mode.
274	\end{definition}
275	
276	\begin{remark}[$D^{\mathrm{loc}}$ is \emph{not} the duality function]\label{rem:norm}
277	An earlier version of this draft asserted self--duality with respect to
278	\eqref{eq:Dfac}. That is false, for a structural reason: every
279	$\int D^{\mathrm{loc}}(\xi,\cdot)^2\dd\nu=1$, and reversibility makes
280	$\langle P_tD^{\mathrm{loc}}_\xi,D^{\mathrm{loc}}_{\xi'}\rangle_\nu$ a symmetric
281	matrix, so duality with respect to \eqref{eq:Dfac} would force a symmetric dual
282	transition kernel --- impossible for the asymmetric, sticky--origin dual particle
283	dynamics. (We also verified the failure directly: on two and three sites the
284	interlacing $\cL D^{\mathrm{loc}}=D^{\mathrm{loc}}\cL^{\mathsf T}$ fails by $O(1)$
285	margins at generic parameters.) The true duality function of \cite{REU} carries
286	nonlocal counting factors, as follows.
287	\end{remark}
288	
289	\begin{theorem}[orthogonal $q$--Krawtchouk self--duality]\label{thm:dual}
290	For configurations $\eta,\xi$ and $i\in\{1,2\}$ let $N^-_{x-1}(\xi_i)$ be the number
291	of species--$i$ dual particles strictly to the left of $x$ and $N^+_{x+1}(\eta_i)$
```

## 🤖 Assistant

Here it is as it now stands in rev2 — Corollary 2.6 (triangular degeneration), reading the LaTeX back as prose:

---

**Corollary (triangular degeneration).** The type D ASEP is self-dual with respect to the *triangular* function

$$D^{\mathrm{tri}}(\xi,\eta) = \mathbf 1\{\xi\subseteq\eta\}\prod_{i=1,2}\ \prod_{x:\,\xi_{i,x}=1} q^{2\left(x-N^-_{x-1}(\xi_i)+N^+_{x+1}(\eta_i)\right)},$$

the type D analogue of the Schütz and Borodin–Corwin–Sasamoto $q$-exponential dualities [Schutz, BCS]. On configurations $\eta$ with finitely many particles to the right — in particular on the step initial condition and its evolution — the factors of $D^{\mathrm{tri}}$ are uniformly bounded for each fixed dual mass, and $D^{\mathrm{tri}}$ is the form of the duality used in §7.

**Proof.** Self-duality with respect to (2.5) holds identically in $(\alpha_1,\alpha_2)$, hence coefficient-wise in $\alpha_1^{-1},\alpha_2^{-1}$; and since the dual generator preserves the particle numbers $(|\xi_1|,|\xi_2|)$, the coefficients of $\alpha_1^{-|\xi_1|}\alpha_2^{-|\xi_2|}$, glued across the dual sectors, again form a duality matrix. Extracting the leading coefficients as $\alpha_i\to0$ yields self-duality with respect to $D^{\mathrm{tri}}$. ∎

---

(Here (2.5) is `eq:Dreu`, the orthogonal $q$-Krawtchouk duality function from the theorem just above.)

One thing I notice rereading it aloud: the proof establishes the self-duality but says nothing about the boundedness clause in the statement — that property is currently asserted without justification. It's true and easy (on a right-finite $\eta$, $N^+_{x+1}(\eta_i)$ is bounded and the product is over the fixed-size support of $\xi$), but if you want the proof to cover everything the statement claims, I can add a sentence. Want me to?

```
78:The main result concerns Markov duality (see also \cite{Sch97,BS,BS2,BS3,CGRS,CGRS2,KuanJPhysA,KIMRN} for type $D$  AESP with parameter $(q,2,0)$ and $ (q,3,0)$. The previous duality function of \cite{KLLPZ} was a ``triangular'' duality generalizing Schutz's duality function \cite{Sch97}.  In this paper, we produce an ``orthogonal polynomial'' duality function. Recent work on orthogonal polynomial duality functions was done in \cite{Franceschini2018SelfDualityOM, Carinci2019OrthogonalDO, GroneDual, CFG,FKZ}. More specifically, the paper \cite{CFG} proves that the $q$--Krawtchouk polynomials are duality functions for the single--species ASEP. In this paper, we will prove that the type $D$  ASEP with parameters $n=2,3$ and $\delta=0$ are orthogonal with respect to an independent product of $q$--Krawtchouk polynomials. Because these polynomials have an additional parameter $\alpha$ that is dependent on the reversible measures, they are more suitable for asymptotics than the triangular duality functions.
882:\subsection{Constructing a Triangular Duality (Algebra)}
884:From an algebraic perspective, the triangular duality matrix from \cite{KLLPZ} can also be generated, albeit in a larger $36 \times 36$ matrix in which the correct probabilistic triangular duality can be found as a $16 \times 16$ submatrix. This submatrix emerges from removing extraneous rows and columns that emerge from the representations of $\mathcal{U}_q(\mathfrak{so}_6)$ but do not correspond to probabilistic configurations. 
954:The triangular duality matrix mentioned earlier would be:
```

```
\subsection{Constructing a Triangular Duality (Algebra)}

From an algebraic perspective, the triangular duality matrix from \cite{KLLPZ} can also be generated, albeit in a larger $36 \times 36$ matrix in which the correct probabilistic triangular duality can be found as a $16 \times 16$ submatrix. This submatrix emerges from removing extraneous rows and columns that emerge from the representations of $\mathcal{U}_q(\mathfrak{so}_6)$ but do not correspond to probabilistic configurations. 
\medskip 


 Consider the representation $\rho: \mathcal{U}_q(\mathfrak{so}_6) \rightarrow \mathrm{Hom}_{\mathbb{C}}(V,V)$ where $V= \mathbb{C}^6 \otimes \cdots \otimes \mathbb{C}^6$ (tensor product $L$ times), as defined in Section 2.5. So for any $X$, its image $\rho(X)$ is a $6^L\times 6^L$ matrix. Then
\begin{equation}
\begin{split}
\label{testDuality}
\rho(\exp_{q^2}(\Delta^{L-1} F_2) \exp_{q^2}(\Delta^{L-1}F_3))
\end{split}
\end{equation}
corresponds to the symmetry $S$ that is described in Section 6.1. The symmetry will be found as a $4^L \times 4^L$ submatrix of the above matrix representation (\ref{testDuality}).
```

## 🤖 Assistant

You're partly right, and the part where you're not is worth pinning down before we touch it. Here's what I found in the REU source and KLLPZ:

**What's prior work:** The triangular duality is indeed not new — it's the *original* duality of the type D ASEP from KLLPZ, generalizing Schütz [Sch97], and your students' REU paper explicitly reconstructs it (there's a "Constructing a Triangular Duality (Algebra)" section and an explicit 16×16 triangular matrix at $q=\sqrt{2/3}$). So the *function* $D^{\mathrm{tri}}$ and the duality property are absolutely their/KLLPZ's, not ours. The corollary as written gives no credit, which is the real problem with it.

**The one caveat:** all of that is at $n=2,3$ (so$_6$, so$_8$). Our paper uses it at $n=\infty$, and the $n=\infty$ instance isn't literally in KLLPZ or the REU paper — REU only *conjectures* general $n$ (their Remark 4). So we can't purely cite-and-drop without leaving the $n=\infty$ version technically uncited, which is exactly what `thm:cov`/`lem:tridual` rely on.

Good news: I just checked, and the triangular duality holds at $n=\infty$ **directly** — symbolic interlacing $\mathcal L D^{\mathrm{tri}} = D^{\mathrm{tri}}\mathcal L^{\mathsf T}$ is exactly zero, no dependence on the orthogonal duality at all. So the $n=\infty$ case is elementary on its own.

That gives a clean fix that both credits the students and stands on its own — reattribute the corollary roughly as:

> The triangular duality of the type D ASEP [KLLPZ], generalizing Schütz [Sch97] and exhibited for $n=2,3$ there, takes at $n=\infty$ the form $D^{\mathrm{tri}}$ (2.8); the interlacing is a direct check, and it also degenerates from Theorem 2.4(ii) as $\alpha_i\to0$.

— keeping the boundedness clause and the §7 pointer, with the proof either dropped (since it's a direct check / cite) or reduced to one line.

Two things I'd want your call on, since it's your students' work:
1. Should `Sch97` (Schütz) get added to the bibliography? It's cited in this attribution but isn't currently in our reference list.
2. Do you want it demoted from a Corollary to a Remark, given it's now "recording known prior work at $n=\infty$" rather than deriving something? 

Tell me how you want it phrased/credited and I'll put it in rev2.

```
Based on the search results, I found information about Danyil Blyschak and work on type D ASEP:

Type D ASEP is a two-species interacting particle system which generalizes the usual asymmetric simple exclusion process. For specific cases, the type D ASEP is self-dual with respect to an independent product of q-Krawtchouk polynomials.

A duality function from Blyschak, Burke, Kuan, Li, Ustilovsky, and Zhou for the Type D ASEP has been generalized for all n. Additionally, the work has been extended to higher-rank quantum groups: The Type D ASEP construction was extended from cases of Uq(so6) and Uq(so8) to the case of Uq(so10), and a previously known duality function was generalized for all n.

The main paper appears to be the arXiv paper 2209.11114 on "Orthogonal polynomial duality of a two-species asymmetric exclusion process," which addresses the type D ASEP duality structure you're asking about.
```

```
## Regarding Duality for General n
```

```
Based on the search results, I found the paper you're looking for:

The Type D asymmetric simple exclusion process (ASEP) is a particle system involving two classes of particles analyzed from both probabilistic and algebraic perspectives. From a probabilistic perspective, stochastic fusion is performed on the Type D ASEP and analyzed on generator matrices, limits of drift speed, stationary distributions, and Markov self-duality. From an algebraic perspective, a fused Type D ASEP system is constructed from a Casimir element of U_q(so_6), using crystal bases to analyze and manipulate various representations of U_q(so_6).

The study found that both approaches produce different processes and therefore the previous method which analyzed the usual ASEP does not generalize to all finite-dimensional simple Lie algebras.

The paper is: **"Comparative Analyses of the Type D ASEP: Stochastic Fusion and Crystal Bases"** (arXiv:2407.21015, updated February 10, 2025). The search also confirms that Danyil Blyschak is a co-author on related work in this area.


REMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks.
```

```
78:The main result concerns Markov duality (see also \cite{Sch97,BS,BS2,BS3,CGRS,CGRS2,KuanJPhysA,KIMRN} for type $D$  AESP with parameter $(q,2,0)$ and $ (q,3,0)$. The previous duality function of \cite{KLLPZ} was a ``triangular'' duality generalizing Schutz's duality function \cite{Sch97}.  In this paper, we produce an ``orthogonal polynomial'' duality function. Recent work on orthogonal polynomial duality functions was done in \cite{Franceschini2018SelfDualityOM, Carinci2019OrthogonalDO, GroneDual, CFG,FKZ}. More specifically, the paper \cite{CFG} proves that the $q$--Krawtchouk polynomials are duality functions for the single--species ASEP. In this paper, we will prove that the type $D$  ASEP with parameters $n=2,3$ and $\delta=0$ are orthogonal with respect to an independent product of $q$--Krawtchouk polynomials. Because these polynomials have an additional parameter $\alpha$ that is dependent on the reversible measures, they are more suitable for asymptotics than the triangular duality functions.
80:The Markov duality will be proved with two different methods. The first is a direct probabilistic argument, using induction on the number of lattice sites. The second is a more algebraic method, using the $*$--bialgebra structure of $\mathcal{U}_q(\mathfrak{so}_6)$. The connection between $\mathfrak{so}_6$ and type $D$ ASEP was explored in  \cite{KLLPZ}; in fact, $\mathfrak{so}_6$ is the type $D$  Lie algebra, providing the namesake for the type $D$ ASEP. In that construction, two of the six potential particle configurations were ``discarded'' in order to ensure non--negativity of the jump rates. That paper uses a computer--aided construction of a Casimir element. Here, we calculate the ``reversible measures'' that would appear if all six potential particle configurations were used. While these measures have a factorized form, they do not appear to be an independent product for any values of $(n,\delta)$.
```

## 🤖 Assistant

I believe you — but I can't find it, and I don't want to drop in a wrong citation, so let me tell you exactly what I checked and ask you to point me at it.

What I looked at:
- The REU paper (2209.11114, Blyschak–Burke–Kuan–Li–Ustilovsky–Zhou) itself: its main theorem is orthogonal duality at $n=2,3$ only, and its Remark 4 explicitly says general $n$ "is believed to hold... we don't pursue this direction." Its triangular-duality section is the so$_6$ ($n=2$) reconstruction of KLLPZ. So the all-$n$ triangular result isn't *in* that paper.
- The so$_{10}$ paper (2307.15660, Rohr–Sellakumaran Latha–Yin) — a search blurb attributed an "all $n$" duality generalization here, but that's a different author set, and it's the so$_{10}$ extension.
- The 2024 "Stochastic Fusion and Crystal Bases" paper (2407.21015) — different students (Brodsky et al.), and actually a *negative* result about generalizing.
- A direct arXiv author-page lookup for Blyschak 404'd.

So I've got KLLPZ ($n=2,3$, triangular, after Schütz) and the REU orthogonal paper ($n=2,3$), but not a Blyschak "triangular duality for all $n$." Could you give me the arXiv number or title? If it's a thesis or an unposted/recent preprint, just tell me how you want it cited.

Worth saying why I want to nail this down beyond attribution: **it would strengthen the paper.** Right now `thm:cov` (the $q$-Laplace decoupling, regime B) is built entirely on the triangular duality via `cor:tri`/`lem:tridual` — and I currently hedge its $n$-dependence as "holds at $n=\infty$, extends to $n=2,3$ via REU, and to other $n$ modulo the Remark 4 conjecture." But `thm:cov` never actually uses the *orthogonal* duality — only the triangular one. So if Blyschak proved the triangular duality for **all** finite $n$, then `thm:cov` holds for all $n$ **unconditionally**, and that hedge disappears entirely. Same for `lem:tridual`. That's a real upgrade, so I'd like to cite the right paper and then go relax those caveats.

What's the reference?

<details><summary>↳ tool result</summary>

```
97	\subsection{The model}\label{sec:intromodel}
98	Fix $q\in(0,1)$. The \emph{type D ASEP} was introduced by Kuan, Landry, Lin, Park and
99	Zhou \cite{KLLPZ}, who constructed it from the quantum groups $U_q(\so_6)$ and
100	$U_q(\so_8)$ ($n=2,3$ in $\so_{2n+2}$, Cartan type $D$); the construction has been
101	extended to $U_q(\so_{10})$ \cite{RSL}, and the explicit rate matrix (displayed for
102	general $n$ in \cite[\S2.1]{REU}) makes sense for every $n\in\N$. It is a
103	continuous--time Markov process of two conserved species on $\Z$ which, beyond
104	hopping, may bind into a composite \emph{bound pair} and later split. This binding is
105	what makes the model a stringent test of decoupling: the two species are genuinely
106	interacting, not two independent copies sharing the exclusion rule. Blyschak, Burke,
107	Kuan, Li, Ustilovsky and Zhou \cite{REU} established an orthogonal $q$--Krawtchouk
108	self--duality for $n=2,3$ and conjectured it for all $n$; we verify it at the
109	$n=\infty$ degeneration used here (Theorem~\ref{thm:dual}(ii)). The duality is the
110	analytic engine of this paper: it reduces every fluctuation question to a computation
111	with a handful of dual particles.
```
</details>

```
276	\begin{theorem}[orthogonal $q$--Krawtchouk self--duality]\label{thm:dual}
277	For configurations $\eta,\xi$ and $i\in\{1,2\}$ let $N^-_{x-1}(\xi_i)$ be the number
278	of species--$i$ dual particles strictly to the left of $x$ and $N^+_{x+1}(\eta_i)$
279	the number of species--$i$ particles of $\eta$ strictly to the right of $x$, and set
280	\begin{equation}\label{eq:Dreu}
281	  D_{\alpha_1,\alpha_2}(\xi,\eta)\ =\ \prod_{i=1,2}\ \prod_{x:\,\xi_{i,x}=\eta_{i,x}=1}
282	  \Big(1-\frac{q^{2\left(x-N^-_{x-1}(\xi_i)+N^+_{x+1}(\eta_i)\right)}}{\alpha_i}\Big),
283	\end{equation}
284	the two--point specialisation of the $q$--Krawtchouk product of
285	\cite[Thm.~3.1]{REU}.
286	\textup{(i)} \cite[Thm.~3.1]{REU}: for parameters $(q,n,\delta)=(q,2,0)$ and
287	$(q,3,0)$, the type D ASEP is self--dual with respect to \eqref{eq:Dreu}.
288	\textup{(ii)} At $n=\infty$, i.e.\ for the rates \eqref{eq:rates}: the two--site
289	interlacing $\cL D=D\cL^{\mathsf T}$ holds identically in $(q,\alpha_1,\alpha_2)$ ---
290	a finite rational identity, which we have verified by computer algebra --- and the
291	induction in the proof of \cite[Thm.~3.1, eqs.~(16)--(19)]{REU}, which uses only the
292	two--site case and the fugacity--shift covariance of \eqref{eq:Dreu}, extends it to
293	any number of sites. This settles the $n=\infty$ degeneration of the conjecture of
294	\cite[Rmk.~4]{REU} that the duality holds for all $n$. In the lineage of orthogonal
295	stochastic dualities from $U_q$--representations \cite{Groenevelt,CGRS}, this is the
296	type D instance.
297	\end{theorem}
298	
299	\begin{corollary}[triangular degeneration]\label{cor:tri}
```

```
64	In the fixed--$q$ (Kardar--Parisi--Zhang) regime an exact current--decoupling identity,
65	valid at every $n$ (Propositions~\ref{prop:decouple}, \ref{prop:decouplen}), makes each
66	species' current an autonomous single--species ASEP, hence Tracy--Widom for every $n$
67	--- proving a conjecture of \cite{REU}. Here too the species decouple: we prove an
68	exact contact representation for the joint $q$--Laplace observable ---
69	$\Cov(q^{2N_1},q^{2N_2})$ is a weighted sum of connected two--particle dual hitting
70	probabilities, vanishing identically without the binding (Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}) ---
71	while for the linear currents simulations give
72	$\Cov(N_1,N_2)=(0.099\pm0.003)\sqrt s$ at $q=\tfrac12$, so that
73	$\Corr(N_1,N_2)\asymp s^{-1/6}\to0$ (Conjecture~\ref{conj:cov}). The common engine is the $q$--Krawtchouk orthogonal
74	self--duality, together with the fact --- which we make precise --- that the
75	inter--species coupling is invisible to every equilibrium transport coefficient, so
76	that in both regimes what remains of it is a transient, initial--condition--driven
77	correlation rather than a feature of the limiting law.
```

```
148	\subsection{Relation to previous work}\label{sec:introlit}
149	Regime~(A) belongs to the nonlinear fluctuation theory of weakly asymmetric systems and
150	the passage to stochastic Burgers/KPZ, due to Gon\c{c}alves and Jara \cite{GJ}, with
151	uniqueness by Gubinelli and Perkowski and spectral--gap--free refinements by
152	Gon\c{c}alves, Jara and Simon \cite{GJS}. The few--body estimates we need we obtain
153	through the \emph{orthogonal polynomial duality} method of Ayala, Carinci and Redig
154	\cite{ACR,ACR2}, which reduces them to a decay bound on the few--particle dual kernel. In
155	our setting the exact current decoupling (Proposition~\ref{prop:decouple}) makes the
156	drift an autonomous single--species WASEP, so the duality enters only for the
157	inter--species cross--noise, controlled by the type D two--particle kernel bound of
158	\S\ref{sec:kernel}; the would--be slow internal mode of the bound pair never couples to
159	the species current at all (Proposition~\ref{prop:sym}).
160	
161	For regime~(B), the single--species Tracy--Widom asymptotics are
162	Borodin--Corwin--Sasamoto \cite{BCS}; the exact $q$--Laplace decoupling identity
163	(Theorem~\ref{thm:cov}) is to our knowledge new, and the Tracy--Widom marginals at
164	every $n$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:marg}) prove the conjecture of \cite[\S3.1.1]{REU}.
```

## 🤖 Assistant

Good question, and it's the right instinct — citing a result and proving it is redundant unless there's a reason. Here the reason is real but unstated, which is the actual defect: **our Lemma 2.8 isn't quite ACR's Lemma 2.1 — it's a mild generalization.** ACR state the covariance identity for the model's standard reversible measure; we state it for an *arbitrary* orthogonalizing measure $\varpi$, because in §6 we apply it with $\varpi \neq \nu$ (the sector-reweighted measure from the orthogonality remark). The proof is genuinely one line and measure-agnostic — it uses only the duality relation and orthogonality, not reversibility — so it covers our $\varpi$ for free.

So the honest fix is to *say* that, rather than leave a cite-plus-proof that looks redundant. Let me make the framing explicit:


**⚙️ Edit**

```json

Then for all\n$\\xi,\\xi'$ and $t\\ge0$,\n\\[\n  \\int \\E_\\eta[D(\\xi,\\eta_t)]\\,D(\\xi',\\eta)\\dd\\varpi(\\eta)=p_t(\\xi,\\xi')\\,a(\\xi').\n\\]\n\\end{lemma}\n\\begin{proof}\nInsert the duality identity",
  "new_string": "The following is \\cite[Lem.~2.1]{ACR}, which we restate for an \\emph{arbitrary}\nmeasure $\\varpi$ orthogonalising the duality family --- ACR state it for the standard\nreversible measure $\\nu$, whereas in \\S\\ref{sec:ew} we apply it with the\nsector--reweighted $\\varpi\\ne\\nu$ of Remark~\\ref{rem:orthstatus}. The proof, identical\nto theirs and using only orthogonality and the duality relation (not reversibility of\n$\\varpi$), is a single line, included for completeness.\n\n\\begin{lemma}[duality covariance; {after \\cite[Lem.~2.1]{ACR}}]\\label{lem:acr}\nLet $\\{D(\\xi,\\cdot)\\}$ be a family of duality functions for the process which is\northogonal in $L^2(\\varpi)$ for some measure $\\varpi$,\n$\\int D(\\xi,\\eta)D(\\xi',\\eta)\\dd\\varpi=\\delta_{\\xi,\\xi'}a(\\xi)$. ## 🤖 Assistant
```

Both done in rev2, compiles clean. Direct answer to your question first, then a summary of the attribution pass.

**Lemma 2.8 — why it's proved separately.** The honest reason is that it *isn't* verbatim ACR Lemma 2.1: ACR state the covariance identity for the standard reversible measure $\nu$, but we need it for the **sector-reweighted measure $\varpi \neq \nu$** (the one from the orthogonality remark, used in §6 for the cross-noise). The proof happens to use only orthogonality and the duality relation — not reversibility — so it extends to any orthogonalizing $\varpi$ for free, but that's a (trivial) generalization of the cited statement, not the statement itself. The old phrasing hid this, so it read as redundant. I've reframed it: the lemma is now "after [ACR Lem. 2.1]," with a lead sentence saying explicitly that we restate it for arbitrary $\varpi$ because we apply it off $\nu$, and that the one-line proof is included for completeness.

If you'd rather not even have the one-liner, the alternative is to delete the proof and just write "the proof of [ACR Lem. 2.1] applies verbatim to any orthogonalizing $\varpi$." Say the word and I'll switch to that — but I'd lean toward keeping it, since a reader chasing the $\varpi \neq \nu$ point will want to see that reversibility isn't used.

**Attribution pass (your "cite prior work / acknowledge incremental" directive):**
- **§1.1** now states plainly that the model carries *two* self-dualities, **both prior work** — the triangular one of KLLPZ after Schütz, and the orthogonal $q$-Krawtchouk one of Blyschak et al. (REU, $n=2,3$, conjectured all $n$) — and says outright they "are not themselves our contribution: we use them as a tool… the substance of the paper is the fluctuation analysis."
- **`thm:dual`(ii)** softened from "settles the conjecture" to "the $n=\infty$ case… we claim no more than the verification, the method being that of [REU]."
- **`cor:tri`** retitled "triangular form at $n=\infty$," with a lead sentence crediting it as "the original duality of [KLLPZ]"; it now records only the $n=\infty$ form rather than presenting the degeneration as a result of ours.
- **Citation bug fixed:** the triangular/Schütz reference was pointing at `\cite{Schutz}` = Schütz's *master-equation* paper (correct only in Lemma 2.10). The triangular duality is from Schütz's *duality-relations* paper — a different 1997 J. Stat. Phys. article — which I added as a new bib entry `SchutzDual` and pointed the relevant citations to.
- Abstract: the engine is now "the $q$-Krawtchouk orthogonal self-duality **of Blyschak et al.**"

One thing I deliberately did *not* do: cite a Blyschak "all-$n$ triangular" paper, since I couldn't verify it. If you locate it, the payoff I flagged still stands — `thm:cov` would become unconditional in $n$. Ready for the next comment.

```
358	\begin{remark}[the exact orthogonality relation]\label{rem:orthstatus}
359	The precise orthogonality satisfied by the type D duality functions is the
360	two--point, two--species specialisation of \cite[Thm.~3.2]{CFG20}, the
361	single--species input cited in \cite[\S3.1]{REU}. On a finite lattice $\Lambda$ of
362	$|\Lambda|$ sites define the \emph{sector--reweighted} blocking measure and norm
363	functions ($N=N(\zeta)$ the particle number, all up to normalisation)
364	\begin{equation}\label{eq:omegadef}
365	  \varpi_\alpha(\zeta)\ \propto\ \mu_\alpha(\zeta)\,q^{N(N-1)}\,
366	  \big(\alpha q^{2N-2|\Lambda|};q^2\big)_\infty,\quad
367	  g_\alpha(\zeta)\ \propto\ q^{2N(N-1)}
368	  \big(\alpha q^{2N-2|\Lambda|};q^2\big)_\infty\big(\alpha q^{-2N};q^2\big)_\infty,
369	\end{equation}
370	with window $\alpha\in(0,q^{2|\Lambda|})$, and let $\bar D$ denote \eqref{eq:Dreu}
371	read with the \emph{process} configuration in the $N^-$ slot and the dual in the
372	$N^+$ slot,
373	\[
374	  \bar D(\xi,\eta)=\prod_{i=1,2}\ \prod_{x:\,\xi_{i,x}=\eta_{i,x}=1}
375	  \Big(1-\frac{q^{2\left(x-N^-_{x-1}(\eta_i)+N^+_{x+1}(\xi_i)\right)}}{\alpha_i}\Big);
376	\]
377	transposing the interlacing of Theorem~\ref{thm:dual}(ii), $\bar D$ is again a
378	self--duality function. Then
379	\begin{equation}\label{eq:orthexact}
380	  \sum_\eta \varpi_{\alpha_1}(\eta_1)\,\varpi_{\alpha_2}(\eta_2)\,
381	  \bar D(\xi,\eta)\,\bar D(\xi',\eta)\ =\ \delta_{\xi,\xi'}\,a(\xi),\qquad
382	  a(\xi)=\prod_{i=1,2}\frac{g_{\alpha_i}(\xi_i)}{\varpi_{\alpha_i}(\xi_i)},
383	\end{equation}
384	which we have verified to machine precision for the $n=\infty$ rates on two and
385	three sites (off--diagonals and the norm formula). Three observations. (i) The
386	reweighting in \eqref{eq:omegadef} depends only on the conserved particle numbers,
387	so $\varpi:=\varpi_{\alpha_1}\otimes\varpi_{\alpha_2}$ is again reversible, and
388	Lemma~\ref{lem:acr} applies with $(\varpi,\bar D,a)$. (ii) In the orientation
389	$\bar D$ the process enters through the \emph{left} counts $N^-(\eta_i)$, which are
390	almost surely finite under $\nu$ on $\Z$: the degeneration that affects
391	\eqref{eq:Dreu} in infinite volume (where $q^{2N^+(\eta)}=0$ a.s.) does not occur ---
392	the resolution is to transpose the slots, not to reflect the lattice, which is
393	impossible (the reflected generator fails the interlacing, consistently with the
394	reflection corresponding to the non--stochastic continuation $n<n_{\mathrm{crit}}$
395	of Remark~\ref{rem:range}). (iii) In the regime (A) scaling, $q=1-c/N^2$ on
396	$|\Lambda|=O(N)$ sites, the window is asymptotically $\alpha_i<1$, i.e.\ both
397	densities below $\tfrac12$; the case of both densities above $\tfrac12$ follows by
398	the particle--hole--plus--reflection symmetry of \eqref{eq:rates} (which flips both
399	species), while the mixed case $\rho_1<\tfrac12<\rho_2$ is \emph{not} reached by the
400	window and is deferred (e.g.\ via the signed--measure version of the orthogonality
401	noted in \cite[Rmk.\ after Thm.~3.2]{CFG20}). The reweighting
402	is bounded above and below by constants (Lemma~\ref{lem:sector}). The remaining
```

## 🤖 Assistant

That remark is the densest thing in §2, and your reaction is justified — it's confusing because it's doing **four different jobs** under one "Remark" heading, which is why the point doesn't come through. Here's what's actually in it:

1. **The load-bearing part (most of it):** it states the *exact* orthogonality relation `(2.11)` — the specific measure $\varpi$ the duality functions are orthogonal under, their norms $a(\xi)$, the fugacity window, and the precise orientation $\bar D$ (process in the $N^-$ slot). This matters because Lemma 2.8 just above is stated abstractly — "for *some* orthogonalizing measure $\varpi$" — and *this is the only place $\varpi$, $a$, and $\bar D$ are actually pinned down.* Without it, the cross-noise vanishing in §5 (property (X), the crux of the whole EW theorem) has no concrete duality to stand on. So this part is essential — arguably too essential to be buried in a remark.

2. **Observation (i):** a one-line check that $\varpi$ is reversible (the reweighting depends only on conserved particle numbers), so Lemma 2.8 applies. Necessary glue.

3. **Observation (ii):** the orientation subtlety — why we use $\bar D$ (left-counts) and not the "obvious" form, which degenerates to the constant $0$ on $\mathbb Z$. Conceptually important — it's *why the approach works in infinite volume at all* — but the parenthetical about the reflected generator and "non-stochastic continuation" is a defensive aside a reader doesn't need.

4. **Observation (iii):** regime-A bookkeeping — the window becomes $\alpha<1$, particle–hole handles densities above $\tfrac12$, the mixed case is deferred, and the reweighting is bounded. This is pure setup for Lemma `lem:sector`, which lives in §5.

The honest diagnosis: it grew by accretion across my revisions (it started life as a one-line "orthogonality TBD" hedge), and it never got refactored into its constituent purposes. The fix I'd recommend:

- **Promote job 1 to a numbered Proposition** — "exact orthogonality of the type D duality functions," with the machine-verification noted — since Lemma 2.8 and §5 genuinely depend on it. Fold job 2 in as its last line.
- **Keep job 3 as a separate two-sentence remark**, cutting the reflected-generator aside (or dropping it to a footnote).
- **Move job 4 down to sit beside `lem:sector` in §5**, where it's the only place it's used — it's misplaced in §2.

That turns one 40-line catch-all into a clean Proposition + a short remark, each with one clear job, and the §5 material lands where it's needed.

Want me to do that restructuring? It's the kind of change that makes the section read much better, but it touches three locations, so I wanted to lay out the plan before executing rather than just rearranging things under you.

## 🤖 Assistant

Traced it through the file. The short answer: **the entire content of that remark feeds exactly one leg of one theorem** — property (X) of the Edwards–Wilkinson theorem (Theorem 5.1, regime A) — and nothing else in the paper. Here's the dependency chain, top to bottom:

**Remark 2.9** defines three objects — the measure $\varpi$, the norms $a(\xi)$, and the orientation $\bar D$ — and asserts the orthogonality identity `(2.11)`.
- → **Lemma 2.8** (`lem:acr`, duality covariance) is stated abstractly "for some orthogonalizing $\varpi$"; Remark 2.9 is what supplies the concrete $(\varpi, \bar D, a)$ it runs on. *(This is the dependency your last question was circling — 2.8 and 2.9 are a matched pair: 2.8 is the abstract identity, 2.9 is its only instantiation.)*
- → **Lemma 5.x** (`lem:orth`, $V_x \perp$ density fields): its proof does the $1{+}1{-}1{-}1$ cancellation *in the $\varpi$-pairing with $\bar D$*, establishing that the cross-noise $V_x$ expands only on bond-pair duals.
- → **Lemma `lem:sector`** (the $\nu \leftrightarrow \varpi$ comparison): exists purely to transfer correlations from $\varpi$ (where the orthogonality lives) back to $\nu$ (where the process is stationary). Depends on the explicit $\varpi$ of `(2.10)`.
- → **Proposition `prop:conc`** ($L^2$ concentration of the cross bracket): assembles all of the above — `lem:acr` with $(\varpi,\bar D,a)$, the mass decomposition, the kernel bound — to prove $\langle M_1^N, M_2^N\rangle \to 0$.
- → **Theorem 5.1** (`thm:ewmain`): property **(X)**, the vanishing cross-noise.

So the punchline on "what's the point": properties (D) and (N) of the EW theorem are classical single-species facts; **(X) is the only genuinely two-species, model-specific input**, and it is the whole reason the paper can claim the two species decouple *in the noise* and not merely in the drift. That entire calculation is grounded in Remark 2.9. If you deleted the remark, (X) would be floating.

Two things worth knowing for the editorial decision:

1. **It's used only in regime A.** Regime B (Theorem `thm:cov`, the $q$-Laplace decoupling) runs on the *triangular* duality (Cor. 2.6) instead, and never touches $\varpi$ or this orthogonal relation. So Remark 2.9's reach is exactly: §5, property (X).

2. This actually *strengthens* the case for promoting it from a remark to a numbered Proposition: Theorem 5.1 — a main result — transitively depends on it through four intermediate steps, and right now that foundation is labeled "Remark," which is exactly why a reader can't tell what it's for. Things that main theorems depend on shouldn't be remarks.

So my recommendation stands and is now better motivated: pull the identity `(2.11)` out as **Proposition (exact orthogonality)**, since (X) → `prop:conc` → `lem:acr` → it; keep the orientation subtlety as a short remark; move the regime-A window bookkeeping down next to `lem:sector` where (X) actually consumes it. Want me to do that?
