One honest flag while it's in front of us — the **mixed-density case** ($\rho_1 < \tfrac12 < \rho_2$) genuinely isn't covered by this orthogonality route (the window forces both densities to the same side of $\tfrac12$), yet Theorem 5.1 claims arbitrary $(\rho_1,\rho_2)$. That's now stated in Remark 2.9 rather than buried mid-paragraph, but it's a real limitation on the EW theorem's stated generality, not just bookkeeping. You may want to either weaken 5.1's density claim or have someone do the signed-measure case. Flagging so it's a conscious choice. Next comment whenever you're ready.


## 🧑 User

ok now a more serious question. What's the different between this new Proposition 2.8 and previous orthogonality results for type D duality functions?


## 🤖 Assistant

The honest answer is the one that matters most for the paper's integrity, so let me be blunt: **there is essentially no new orthogonality content in Proposition 2.8.** It is prior work, and I want to make sure the paper says so unambiguously. Here's the breakdown.

**What's actually previous work:**
- The single-species $q$-Krawtchouk orthogonality is **CFG, Theorem 3.2** (`[CFG20]`) — that's the whole analytic content, including the norm $g_\alpha$.
- The two-species type D version is **REU's**: they state precisely that "the duality function is an independent product of $D_{\alpha_i}$, [so] it is orthogonal with respect to the reversible measure," i.e. they already invoke exactly the product-of-CFG argument my proof gives.

**Why $n=\infty$ adds nothing.** Orthogonality is a statement about the duality *functions* and the *measure* in $L^2$ — the generator never enters. The duality functions don't depend on the ASEP parameter $n$ (REU's own Remark 4 says so), and neither does the measure. So the $n=\infty$ orthogonality is literally the same $q$-Krawtchouk product as at $n=2,3$; it is not a new case. (Contrast `thm:dual(ii)`, the *duality* at $n=\infty$, which genuinely needed the $n=\infty$ generator and the interlacing check — that one isn't free. Orthogonality is.)

So unlike `thm:dual(ii)`, Proposition 2.8 is not even an incremental extension — it's a restatement.

**What it does pin down that a casual reading of REU leaves loose** — and these are precision points, not theorems:
1. **The measure.** The correct orthogonalizing measure is the *sector-reweighted* $\varpi$ (CFG's $\omega$, with the $q^{N(N-1)}$ and $q$-Pochhammer factors), **not** the plain blocking measure $\nu$. This is not cosmetic: it's exactly what made my own first numerical checks fail when I used $\nu$, and REU's phrasing "orthogonal with respect to $\nu$" is loose on this point. We need the right measure because we use the relation *quantitatively* (in `lem:acr` → `prop:conc`), whereas REU only needed to exhibit it.
2. **The orientation** (process in the $N^-$ slot).
3. **Reversibility of $\varpi$ for all $n$** — trivial, since it's $\nu$ reweighted by a function of the conserved counts.

**My recommendation.** Keep it as a Proposition — you were right that something `prop:conc` depends on shouldn't be skippable — but the framing must make crystal clear it's CFG+REU, not ours. Right now the lead says "We record the orthogonality…" and the proof cites CFG/REU, which is *most* of the way there, but the title "orthogonality of the type D duality functions" sitting over a proof can still read as a claim. I'd sharpen it to something like:

> **Proposition 2.8** (orthogonality; CFG [CFG20], REU [REU]). *The type D duality functions $\bar D$ are orthogonal in $L^2(\varpi)$: …* This is the two-species product of the single-species $q$-Krawtchouk orthogonality [CFG20], as noted in [REU]; we restate it only to fix the measure $\varpi$ and orientation used below, and to record that it is independent of $n$.

That puts the attribution *in the statement*, not just the proof.

I'd also gently note the pattern, since you're auditing exactly these: the entire duality layer of this paper — `thm:dual`, `cor:tri`, `lem:acr`, `prop:orth` — is prior work (KLLPZ / Schütz / REU / CFG / ACR), and the §1.1 edit now says that outright. The paper's actual contribution is downstream of all of it. Keeping these four as cleanly-attributed "recollections" rather than dressed-up propositions is the honest presentation.

Want me to make the attribution edit to Proposition 2.8 along those lines?

## 🧑 User

For the Proposition 3.1, the proof can be considerably simplified by simply observing that when n=\infty, the type D ASEP is just two independent single-species ASEPs


## 🤖 Assistant

This is the one place so far where I want to push back before touching anything, because taken literally it would put a false statement into the proof — and it happens to contradict the paper's own thesis. Let me lay out why, then offer the simplification I think you actually mean.

**The marginals are each an autonomous ASEP; the two processes are not independent.** Those are different statements, and the gap between them is the whole paper.

Concretely, look at the bound-pair hop $(3,0)\to(0,3)$ at rate $1$. In $(\eta_1,\eta_2)$ coordinates that is: a species-1 particle hops $x\to x+1$ **and** a species-2 particle hops $x\to x+1$, in one transition. Same with the swap $(1,2)\to(2,1)$: species 1 hops right and species 2 hops left simultaneously. An independent pair of ASEPs is generated by $\mathcal L_1\otimes I + I\otimes \mathcal L_2$, which can only ever move *one* species in a given transition — it structurally cannot produce these simultaneous two-species jumps. So the type D generator at $n=\infty$ is genuinely *not* the independent-ASEP generator; the two species share noise through the pair hops, swaps, and bind/split events.

That shared noise is exactly what `prop:decouple` part (c) records — "the inter-species coupling is carried entirely by correlated jumps" — and it's what the rest of the paper is about: the cross-bracket $\langle M_1, M_2\rangle$ in §5, the crossover correlation $\rho(c)$ in §6, the contact kernel $C_s$ in `thm:cov`. If the two species were independent, all of those would be identically zero and there'd be nothing to prove. (Sanity check: the block initial condition is $\eta_1 \equiv \eta_2$, perfectly correlated; the crossover section computes the correlation *decaying* from $1$, which independence couldn't produce.)

So what `prop:decouple` actually establishes is the weaker, correct fact: **each species' marginal evolves as an autonomous single-species ASEP** — the species-1 hop rates are $(1,q^2)$ regardless of $\eta_2$ — even though $\eta_1$ and $\eta_2$ are jointly coupled.

**The legitimate simplification, which I suspect is what you mean:** rather than the bond-by-bond current tally currently in the proof, observe directly that the projection $\eta \mapsto \eta_1$ is Markov (lumpable), because no transition rate affecting $\eta_1$ depends on $\eta_2$ — the merge $\varepsilon$ and swap $q^2$ channels supply exactly the same total rate $1$ as a hop onto an empty site — so the lumped chain is the single-species ASEP with rates $(1,q^2)$, and (a)/(b) follow at once. That's a cleaner packaging of (a) and is fair game. But the content "species-2 occupancy doesn't change species-1 rates" still has to be checked — the tally is doing that work — and it gives *marginal autonomy*, not independence.

So: I can rewrite the proof of `prop:decouple` in that lumping/marginal-autonomy style if you'd like it tighter — but I'd keep it as "each marginal is an autonomous ASEP," and I'd keep part (c). I don't want to write "the two species are independent," because it's not true and it would undercut Theorems in §5–§7. 

Want me to do the lumping-style rewrite of the proof (keeping autonomy, not independence)? Or did you have a specific independence argument in mind that I'm not seeing — if so, tell me and I'll check it honestly before doing anything.
